# M10c Phase 9 — Cluster Synthesis — structural input

**Date:** 2026-05-26
**Cluster:** M10c — Defilement and Impurity

---

## §1 — Cluster overview

M10c (Defilement and Impurity) holds 4 inner-being characteristics:

| Char | Short name | One-line definition |
|---:|---|---|
| 1 | Ritual defilement-state | The inner-being condition of ritual uncleanness — the state of being unclean as it bears on sacred participation, communal life, and the conscience. |
| 2 | Moral-inner defilement-state | Defilement as the inner condition of moral corruption — conscience, will, and heart corrupted by desire, habitual sin, and idolatrous attachment. |
| 3 | Corporate/covenantal defilement | Defilement extending from persons or community to land, sanctuary, and the divine name through moral defection. |
| 4 | Defilement by external spiritual agency | The inner-being condition of defilement produced by an unclean spirit inhabiting, controlling, and corrupting a person from without. |

Each characteristic produced 189 findings in its Phase 9 Stage A batch (756 rows total in `cluster_finding`).

---

## §2 — Open cluster observations (raised at Phase 8.7)

These 4 observations were raised at characteristic-mapping time and link to VCG-level polysemy splits / cross-register signals from Phase 7. All remain `status='open'`; the Stage B synthesis should address each (confirm or refine).

### Observation #247 — SPLIT_DESIGN_RATIONALE (linked to Char 53)

**Title:** Ritual-defilement characteristic volume-split per §8.6 (M10c-A vs M10c-B)

**Description:**

> Characteristic 1 (Ritual defilement-state) is carried by two sub-groups — M10c-A (bodily-contact mechanism, 93V) and M10c-B (categorical/classificatory mechanism, 40V) — because the combined ritual register (133V) would breach the §8.6 distribution gate (40% of 263V = 105V cap; 133V = 50.6%). The split-axis is mechanism-vs-verdict, not characteristic-divergence: both sub-groups express the same inner-being condition (the state of ritual uncleanness as it bears on sacred participation and conscience), differing in how the state is acquired. Phase 9 findings on characteristic 1 should treat A and B as complementary registers of one inner-being faculty rather than two separate characteristics; T1.1 'characteristic in its inner-being aspect' answers should integrate both registers; T1.2.1 sub-group structural descriptions distinguish them.

---

### Observation #248 — INTEGRATION_NOTE (linked to Char 56)

**Title:** Unclean-spirit register cross-cluster signal to M27 (cosmic-evil agents)

**Description:**

> M10c-E (Defilement by external spiritual agency, 21V — all akathartos NT) carries an M27 cross-register flag inherited from Phase 3. The unclean spirits are cosmic-evil agents recognised in NT exorcism narratives; they participate analytically in M27 (Evil) as well as M10c (Defilement). Phase 9 T6 (Structural Relationships) findings on characteristic 4 should attend to this register: defilement here is the *result* an external evil agent produces; in M27 the same verses analyse the *agent's* nature. The two analytical lenses are complementary, not duplicative.

---

### Observation #249 — INTEGRATION_NOTE (linked to Char 55)

**Title:** Ezekiel idolatry sub-corpus within M10c-D — cross-cluster signal to M10b

**Description:**

> M10c-D-VCG-03 (16V — Eze 14:11, 20:7/18/30/31/43, 22:3-4, 23:30, 36:18, 37:23, 43:8 etc.) and the broader Ezekiel idolatry-defilement corpus within M10c-D carry an M10b (Wickedness/Evil/Abomination) cross-register flag — these verses analyse the same prophetic events under two complementary characteristics: idolatry as abomination (M10b register) and idolatry as defilement of sanctuary/land/name (M10c register). Phase 9 T6 findings on characteristic 3 should attend to the M10b cross-register relationship; the verses are primary M10c but their full analytical force is multi-cluster.

---

### Observation #250 — INTEGRATION_NOTE (linked to Char 54)

**Title:** Moral-inner register cross-cluster signals (M10, M11, M29, M08, M09)

**Description:**

> M10c-C (Moral-inner defilement-state, 26V) carries the heaviest cluster of cross-register flags inherited from Phase 3 — M10 (sin-act producing defilement-state, e.g. Rom 1:24, Rom 6:19, Gal 5:19), M11 (cleansing/repentance as response, e.g. 2Cor 7:1, 1Th 4:7), M29 (desire as vehicle, miasmos 2Pe 2:10), M08 (pride as companion, miasmos), M09 (consecration as opposite, molunō Rev 14:4). Phase 9 T6 findings on characteristic 2 should map these relational pairs explicitly: defilement-state and the sin-act / cleansing-response / desire-vehicle / consecration-opposite are co-evidenced at the verse level. The characteristic's analytical centre of gravity is the relational network between defilement and these neighbouring inner-being faculties.

---

## §3 — Per-prompt synthesis matrix

For each of the 189 prompts (T0.1.1 … T7.3.4), all 4 characteristics' findings are stacked verbatim below. Read all 4 before authoring the cluster-scope row in your output.

### T0

#### T0.1 — Divine Nature Reflected

##### T0.1.1 — What does the verse evidence reveal about the nature or character of God that this characteristic reflects or images?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The ritual defilement-state reflects, by structural contrast, the holiness and categorical purity of God. The characteristic operates as the condition that is incompatible with the divine presence, and this incompatibility is theologically explicit in the evidence. Lev 15:31 names the stakes directly: the people's uncleanness must be kept separate from them "lest they die in their uncleanness by defiling my tabernacle that is in their midst." The divine dwelling cannot coexist with the defiled state — the defilement-state reflects God's character by being precisely what God is not. Lev 11:44 makes the positive mirroring equally explicit: "I am the Lord your God. Consecrate yourselves therefore, and be holy, for I am holy. You shall not defile yourselves with any swarming thing." Ritual purity is the creaturely image of divine holiness; the defilement-state is its direct contradiction. The characteristic thus reveals that God's nature is one of absolute categorical distinction — holy/unclean are not merely labels but ontological realities before him.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The moral-inner defilement-state reveals God's character primarily by contradiction: the characteristic is what God is not, and its presence in the inner person marks the distance between the creature and the Creator. The most direct evidence is Isa 6:5 (M10c-C-VCG-01): confronted by divine holiness ("my eyes have seen the King, the Lord of hosts"), the prophet's immediate response is the recognition that his lips — his inner-moral organ — are unclean. The holiness of God is the revealing force; the defilement-state is what that holiness exposes. Similarly, 1Th 4:7 (M10c-C-VCG-02): "God has not called us for impurity, but in holiness" — the divine calling is defined as holiness, and the moral-inner defilement-state is named as what the divine calling opposes and moves the person away from. God's character — as holy, as morally pure in all inner motivation — is the standard that makes the moral-inner defilement-state visible as a condition of the inner person.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The corporate/covenantal defilement characteristic reveals God's character primarily through the categories of divine holiness, covenantal faithfulness, and the sanctity of the divine name. The characteristic operates as what violates these divine realities. Num 35:34 (M10c-D-VCG-04): "you shall not defile the land in which you live, in the midst of which I dwell, for I the Lord dwell in the midst of the people of Israel" — God's dwelling presence establishes the boundary that defilement violates; his holiness requires a clean habitation. Eze 43:7 (M10c-D-VCG-03): "the house of Israel shall no more defile my holy name" — the divine name is a reality that can be defiled, revealing that God's name is a sacred relational extension of his person that the covenant people's conduct either honours or degrades. Eze 5:11 (M10c-D-VCG-03): defilement of the sanctuary provokes divine withdrawal — "I will withdraw; my eye will not spare" — revealing that God's covenantal presence is not unconditional and responds to covenantal defilement with withdrawal. The characteristic thus reveals God as one whose holiness, name, and dwelling presence constitute real relational vulnerabilities that the covenant people's corporate conduct directly affects.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Characteristic 4 (Defilement by external spiritual agency) reveals God's character primarily through the dynamics of authority and restoration. The characteristic reveals what God is not (the source of defiling agency) and what God does (exercise sovereign authority over defiling agents and restore the defiled person). Mar 3:11 (M10c-E-VCG-03): unclean spirits "fell down before him and cried out, 'You are the Son of God'" — the spirits' recognition of divine identity reveals God as the one before whom every defiling spiritual force is compelled to bow. Luk 4:36 (VCG-03): "with authority and power he commands the unclean spirits, and they come out!" — God's authority over the defiling agents is sovereign and effective. Luk 6:18 (VCG-02): "those who were troubled with unclean spirits were cured" — restoration of wholeness is the divine act. The characteristic reveals a God whose authority is supreme over all defiling forces and whose disposition toward the defiled person is one of restorative power.

---

##### T0.1.2 — Does Scripture explicitly attribute this characteristic to God — and if so, what does that attribution reveal about its significance in the human person?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

The verse evidence does not attribute the ritual defilement-state to God. The 133 verses show the characteristic operating exclusively in the human person and in objects/spaces in relation to the human person. God does not become ritually unclean; he is the standard against which the clean/unclean distinction is measured (Lev 11:44-45). The significance of this absence: the defilement-state is a specifically creaturely vulnerability — a condition that arises from embodied life in contact with death, discharge, and disease. God, being without body and without limitation by death, cannot bear this condition. The absence thus locates the defilement-state within the creaturely domain of finitude and mortality, and signals that the human person's susceptibility to it is part of their created embodied constitution, not a moral failure of the image per se.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (S)

The 26-verse corpus does not attribute the moral-inner defilement-state to God. No verse in §3 portrays God as possessing impurity, defiled conscience, corrupted will, or heart allegiance disorder. The characteristic is exclusively a condition of the human (and, in the Revelation apocalyptic register, of spiritually corrupted beings — Rev 16:13, 17:4, 18:2, VCG-04). The absolute absence of divine attribution confirms the significance: the moral-inner defilement-state is a departure from divine character, not an expression of it. Its significance for the human person is that it marks the inner person's failure to image God — the condition where the interior life has moved from conformity to divine holiness toward conformity to corrupted desire.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes, uniquely at Eze 20:26 (M10c-D-VCG-02): "I defiled them through their very gifts in their offering up all their firstborn, that I might devastate them. I did it that they might know that I am the Lord." God defiles Israel through their own defiant gifts as a judicial act — using the instrument of their own self-defilement against them as a form of punitive desolation. The attribution is judicial and singular: God does not normally possess or generate defilement, but he can deploy it as an instrument of wrath when the people's defiant self-defilement reaches the point of idolatrous child sacrifice. This attribution reveals the characteristic's most extreme form — when the community's defilement is used by God himself as the mechanism of its own devastation.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The 21-verse corpus does not attribute the defilement-by-external-spiritual-agency condition to God. God is not a subject of this characteristic; he is its sovereign counterforce — the one whose authority commands the unclean spirits and whose power restores the defiled person. The absence of divine attribution confirms the characteristic as a condition that God opposes and reverses, not one he possesses or generates.

---

##### T0.1.3 — Where Scripture is silent about God's possession of this characteristic, what does that silence suggest about the characteristic's place in the divine image?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The silence confirms that the ritual defilement-state is not an image-bearer expression in the sense of resembling God, but rather it functions within the image-bearing vocation by defining the boundary of access to divine presence. Lev 10:10 frames the priestly vocation: "to distinguish between the holy and the common, and between the unclean and the clean." The priest's calling is to hold the distinction God himself embodies. The defilement-state, by being what God is not, creates the space in which the image-bearing vocation is exercised: the human person is called to manage the clean/unclean boundary in imitation of divine holiness. The silence about God's possession of defilement means the human engagement with this characteristic is participation in a structure God establishes and maintains, not a reflection of a divine property.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The silence confirms that the moral-inner defilement-state is the condition of the image-bearer when the image is disrupted or distorted. It is not a divine property the person is created to reflect; it is the condition that emerges when the person ceases to image God's holiness. Isa 64:6 (M10c-C-VCG-01) makes this most stark: "we have all become like one who is unclean, and all our righteous deeds are like a polluted garment" — the corporate confession of a community whose interior life no longer reflects divine moral purity. The silence about God's possession of this state positions the characteristic as the marker of image-disruption: the divine image in the person is in proportion to the absence of moral-inner defilement, and in inverse proportion to its presence.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The near-total silence about God's possession of this characteristic (the Eze 20:26 exception being judicial and unique) confirms that the corporate/covenantal defilement-state is a specifically creaturely-covenantal condition. God's silence as a bearer of this characteristic reveals its essential nature: it is the condition that arises when creaturely covenantal persons — whose inner will, shared life, and sacred stewardship are oriented toward God — turn away from him in unfaithfulness. The characteristic requires a covenantal community in relation with a holy God; it cannot exist in God himself, but it exists in the gap between what the covenantal community is called to be and what they have become through corporate moral defection.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The silence confirms that defilement by external spiritual agency is categorically alien to the divine nature. God is holy; the unclean spirits recognise this by their response to Jesus (Mar 3:11 — falling before him, confessing "Son of God"). The silence suggests the characteristic belongs entirely to the adversarial-creaturely domain: it arises from the action of spiritual beings in opposition to God's holiness, affecting human persons who are vulnerable to this external force. The characteristic's place in the divine image is entirely negative: it is the disruption of the image-bearer's proper constitution by an alien spiritual power.

---

#### T0.2 — Created Purpose

##### T0.2.1 — What does the verse evidence suggest about the purpose this characteristic serves in the human person as created — what does it equip the person to be, do, or become?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The ritual defilement-state in the created order equips the person to navigate the boundary between the sacred and the common, between death and life, with appropriate attention and discipline. Its purpose is formative: the discipline of managing the defilement-state — washing, waiting, presenting oneself for examination, maintaining the clean/unclean distinction (Lev 11:47, 10:10) — trains the inner person in watchful restraint, conscience-responsiveness, and sacral orientation. Lev 11:44 frames the purpose explicitly: the call not to defile oneself is the means by which the person participates in imitating divine holiness. The defilement-state, by being something that must be actively managed and resolved, equips the human person to be a creature whose bodily life is morally and sacrally ordered — not a merely biological entity but one whose bodily actions have inner and relational consequence.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (S)

The 26-verse corpus does not evidence a creational purpose for the moral-inner defilement-state. Unlike Characteristic 1 (Ritual defilement-state), which has structural provisions built into the created order (bodily management, cleansing remedies), Characteristic 2 is consistently framed in the evidence as a departure from the divine calling rather than as a creaturely feature designed for formation. The evidence is entirely about the condition's negative impact and the call to leave it (Rom 6:19, 1Th 4:7, 2Cor 7:1). No verse in the 26-verse corpus frames the moral-inner defilement-state as something God created for human flourishing or formation. Its purpose, if it has one, is revealed only indirectly through contrast: what the person is called away from clarifies what they are called toward.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (S)

The 83-verse corpus does not evidence a creational purpose for the corporate/covenantal defilement-state. Like Characteristic 2 (Moral-inner defilement-state), this characteristic is consistently framed in the evidence as a departure from the covenantal calling rather than as a created faculty serving human flourishing. The evidence is entirely about the condition arising through moral defection (VCG-01, -02, -03, -04) and being reversed through divine cleansing (VCG-05). No verse frames corporate/covenantal defilement as something designed for the community's formation or benefit. Its analytical significance is entirely through contrast with what the community is called to be.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The 21-verse corpus does not evidence a creational purpose for defilement by external spiritual agency. The characteristic is presented throughout as an affliction. Those troubled by unclean spirits are "cured" (Luk 6:18, VCG-02) — the language of cure presupposes a prior state of wholeness from which the condition is a departure. Mat 10:1 (VCG-03) frames the characteristic as something requiring "authority... to cast them out" — an opposition to be overcome. No creational purpose for the characteristic is evidenced.

---

##### T0.2.2 — Does the evidence indicate whether this characteristic is part of the original created design, a response to the fallen condition, or both?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The evidence does not resolve this directly, but signals point to the defilement-state as a structural feature of embodied creaturely existence rather than exclusively a consequence of the fall. The physiological defilement register (M10c-A-VCG-05: Lev 12 childbirth, Lev 15 menstruation) attaches defilement to natural bodily processes — reproduction, discharge — not to sin. Similarly, contact with death (M10c-A-VCG-07) is the most severe defilement category; death is a consequence of the fall, but the defilement arising from death-contact is treated as a structural given requiring management, not as moral failure. The Num 9:7 men grieve that their corpse-contact impurity was involuntary — "we are unclean through touching a dead body" — showing no moral fault but a bodily condition. This suggests the defilement-state as a category inhabits both: some sub-registers (bodily discharge, menstruation) may reflect the created order of embodied creaturely vulnerability; others (death-defilement) intersect with the fallen condition. The evidence does not permit a single clean answer here.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The evidence strongly indicates the moral-inner defilement-state is a consequence of the fallen condition, not part of the original created design. Job 14:4 (M10c-C-VCG-01) — "who can bring a clean thing out of an unclean? There is not one" — frames the condition as the constitutional reality of the human being as Job knows it: no clean thing emerges from this unclean origin. This is not a description of original design but of inherited human condition under sin. Rom 6:19 (M10c-C-VCG-02) describes the prior condition as "slaves to impurity and to lawlessness" — a slavery into which people fell, not a state they were created for. Rom 1:24 (M10c-C-VCG-02) frames the condition as God's judicial response to human rejection of him: "God gave them up in the lusts of their hearts to impurity" — the defilement deepens as a consequence of moral defection. Taken together, the evidence locates the characteristic as a condition of the fallen human being, not the originally created one.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The evidence strongly indicates this characteristic is a response to the fallen condition operating in a covenantal context. The corporate register is the site of the characteristic's primary evidence: Psa 106:39 (M10c-D-VCG-02) — "thus they became unclean by their acts, and played the whore in their deeds" — describes the defilement as arising from specific acts of apostasy within a people who were already in covenant with God. 2Ch 36:14 (M10c-D-VCG-03) — "they were exceedingly unfaithful, following all the abominations of the nations. And they polluted the house of the Lord" — frames the defilement as the corporate fruit of habitual defection from an existing covenant. The characteristic presupposes the covenantal relationship as prior; the defilement is what happens when that relationship is betrayed.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The evidence strongly indicates this characteristic is a response to the fallen condition, not part of the original created design. The unclean spirits are "hostile, morally corrupting powers" (Mat 10:1 VCG-03) operating in opposition to divine order. Luk 8:29 (VCG-01): the spirit "had repeatedly seized the man, overpowering all human restraint" — the domination is experienced as an intrusion on the person's proper self-possession. The entire framework of the 21-verse corpus assumes that the defiled state is an aberration requiring correction. The characteristic belongs to the domain of adversarial spiritual opposition that operates in a fallen world.

---

##### T0.2.3 — Is there evidence that this characteristic is oriented toward a future fullness — something the person is moving toward, not only what they currently are?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The evidence within Characteristic 1's 133 verses points forward primarily through the elaborate cleansing provisions that accompany every defilement state: washing, waiting, priestly examination and clearance (M10c-B-VCG-02), the water of impurity (M10c-A-VCG-07). These prescribed remedies signal that the defilement-state is not permanent — it has a designed resolution. The fullness orientation is most explicit in Num 19:9 (VCG-07), where the red-heifer ashes are a "standing remedy" designated for the congregation as a "sin offering" — indicating that defilement management is not merely ritual maintenance but participates in a larger sacrificial-atoning economy pointing toward ultimate purity. The NT akathartos verses in M10c-B-VCG-05 (Act 10:14/28) show the defilement category itself being revised by divine revelation, signalling eschatological movement: the categories formed in the ritual order are not the final word. The future fullness is the state of unrestricted access to divine presence, of which the prescribed cleansing is a present anticipation.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes, through the positive-inverse register (M10c-C-VCG-05) and the call-to-cleansing register (M10c-C-VCG-03). Rev 3:4 (VCG-05): "people who have not soiled their garments... will walk with me in white, for they are worthy" — the future fullness is walking with Christ in white, which is the eschatological resolution of the moral-inner defilement's present struggle. Rev 14:4 (VCG-05): those who have not defiled themselves "follow the Lamb wherever he goes... redeemed from mankind as firstfruits for God and the Lamb" — the orientation is toward eschatological consummation with the Lamb. The call at 2Cor 7:1 (VCG-03): "bringing holiness to completion in the fear of God" — the directional goal is the completion of holiness, a future fullness that the active cleansing from defilement serves. 1Th 4:7 (VCG-02): the divine call is "in holiness" — the fullness is holiness; the defilement-state is what stands between the person and that fullness.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes, substantially. The VCG-05 corpus carries three eschatological-restorative texts. Eze 37:23 (VCG-05): "they shall not defile themselves anymore with their idols... but I will save them from all the backslidings in which they have sinned, and will cleanse them; and they shall be my people, and I will be their God" — a promise of permanent non-defilement as the mark of the restored covenant community. Isa 52:1 (VCG-05): "there shall no more come into you the uncircumcised and the unclean" — the eschatological holy city excludes the defiling condition permanently. Zec 13:1 (VCG-05): "on that day there shall be a fountain opened... to cleanse them from sin and uncleanness" — the divinely provided fountain of cleansing addresses the corporate/covenantal defilement at a future eschatological moment. The characteristic is oriented toward a fullness in which the covenant community is permanently purified and the defilement-state is definitively ended.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes. The expulsion-and-restoration register (VCG-02) consistently points toward the restored state as the positive fullness. Luk 6:18 (VCG-02): "those who were troubled with unclean spirits were cured" — the healing points toward the wholeness that is the characteristic's structural opposite (M12). Luk 9:42 (VCG-01): "healed the boy, and gave him back to his father" — the restoration of the person to the family relationship pictures the positive fullness. Mat 12:43/Luk 11:24 (VCG-02): the spirit's post-expulsion restlessness implicitly points to a future state where such spirits find no access to any person — the eschatological fullness is a community in which the characteristic has no domain.

---

#### T0.3 — Image-Bearer Expression

##### T0.3.1 — In what way does this characteristic express the divine image in the human person — what aspect of being made in God's likeness does it instantiate?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The ritual defilement-state expresses the divine image obliquely and structurally: by being the condition that opposes holiness, it defines the space in which the image-bearing vocation of maintaining sacral distinctions is exercised. The evidence shows this most clearly in M10c-B-VCG-01 (Lev 10:10, 11:47, 20:25): priests and all Israel are called to cultivate active inner discernment — "to distinguish between the holy and the common, and between the unclean and the clean" — which is a creaturely participation in the divine capacity to hold absolute distinctions. The image is expressed not through possessing the defilement-state but through the vocation of managing the clean/unclean boundary in light of divine holiness. The person who actively guards against defilement, who watches over bodily actions, who presents for examination, who manages the niddah cycle, is exercising a sacral stewardship that reflects the divine character.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The moral-inner defilement-state does not positively express the divine image but reveals it negatively: its presence marks a specific dimension of the image's disruption. The most revealing evidence is Isa 6:5 (VCG-01): the prophet's recognition of his unclean lips at the sight of divine holiness shows that the faculty capable of recognising the defilement — the conscience — is itself a feature of the image-bearing capacity. The person who can name their moral-inner defilement is exercising an image-bearing capacity (moral self-awareness before God) that the defilement condition itself cannot eliminate. The evidence thus shows the divine image expressed negatively through this characteristic: the ability to recognise the condition (Isa 6:5), to feel its incompatibility with divine holiness (1Th 4:7: "God has not called us for impurity, but in holiness"), and to be called to cleansing (2Cor 7:1) presupposes the image-bearing capacity for holiness.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The corporate/covenantal defilement-state expresses the divine image negatively — through its disruption. The image-bearing capacity that the characteristic reveals (by its absence) is the community's stewardship of sacred space, covenant relationship, and the divine name. These are image-bearing responsibilities: the covenant community is entrusted with land (Num 35:34 — God dwells in it), sanctuary (Eze 5:11 — God's holy place), and divine name (Eze 43:7 — the name that the community either honours or defiles). The corporate defilement-state reveals that the image-bearing community has failed its stewardship: it has defiled what God entrusted to it. Positively, the evidence shows that the proper exercise of the image-bearing capacity is the maintenance of covenantal fidelity, sexual integrity (VCG-01), and sacral stewardship — all of which the defilement-state violates.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The characteristic expresses the divine image negatively — through its disruption. The image-bearing capacities violated are: will (Luk 8:29 — "repeatedly seized him, overpowering all human restraint"), speech and hearing (Mar 9:25 — "mute and deaf spirit"), and communal belonging (Mar 5:2 — "utterly cut off from clean, communal life"). These are precisely the faculties through which image-bearing operates. The characteristic reveals the divine image negatively by showing what is lost when an external spiritual force dominates the person.

---

##### T0.3.2 — Does the evidence suggest that this characteristic is shared between God and the human person, or is it exclusively a creaturely analogue to something in God?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

The evidence confirms this characteristic is exclusively a creaturely condition, with no divine counterpart. As noted at T0.1.2, God is not a subject of this characteristic in the 133-verse corpus. The characteristic has a structural analogue in God: God's holiness is the positive reality against which the defilement-state is measured. But the defilement-state itself — as condition, as vulnerability, as something acquired and managed — belongs to the creaturely domain alone. It is not a shared property between Creator and creature.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (S)

Exclusively a creaturely condition, as evidenced by the silence at T0.1.2. The moral-inner defilement-state is not shared with God. There is no divine analogue to the corrupted conscience (1Cor 8:7), the enslaved will (Rom 6:19), or the heart allegiance disorder equated with idolatry (Eph 5:5). The evidence uniformly frames the condition as what God is not and as what the divine call moves the person away from (1Th 4:7). The characteristic is exclusively creaturely — specifically, it is the condition of the fallen creature whose inner person has come under the dominion of desire, sin, and corrupted allegiance.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Exclusively a creaturely-covenantal condition, with the single judicial exception noted at T0.1.2. The corporate/covenantal defilement-state requires a community embedded in covenantal relationship with God — it is the condition of that community when it betrays the covenant. God as the covenant-giver and the holy One dwelling in the land does not share this condition; he is what the condition violates. Eze 5:11 makes this explicit: the people's defilement of the sanctuary provokes God's withdrawal — showing that God and the defilement-state are mutually exclusive realities.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

Exclusively a creaturely condition. God is not inhabited, controlled, or defiled by unclean spirits; he is their sovereign authority before whom they bow (Mar 3:11, VCG-03). The characteristic presupposes a vulnerable creaturely person who can be invaded and dominated by an external spiritual force — a vulnerability that does not apply to God.

---

##### T0.3.3 — What does the presence or absence of this characteristic in a person reveal about the condition of the divine image in that person?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The presence of the defilement-state does not, by itself, indicate damage to the divine image — because within Characteristic 1's register, defilement can be involuntary (Lev 5:2-3 VCG-01: hidden violation; Num 9:7 VCG-07: involuntary corpse-contact). The men at Num 9:7 who grieve their exclusion from Passover are fully image-bearing persons whose defilement was not moral fault. The image-condition is revealed more by the person's response to the defiled state: does conscience awaken (Lev 5:2-3), does the person seek cleansing (Num 19:19), does the will refuse to remain in the defilement (Num 19:20 — willful non-cleansing is the decisive moral fault)? The absence of the defilement-state — maintained purity — reveals a person actively ordered toward sacred access, exercising the sacral stewardship that the image-bearing vocation requires. The presence of defilement reveals vulnerability and finitude; the response to it reveals the condition of the image.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The presence of moral-inner defilement reveals disruption of the divine image at the most interior level — the conscience, will, and heart are not oriented toward God but toward corrupted desire and allegiance. The clearest evidence: Mat 23:27 (VCG-04) — "within are full of dead people's bones and all uncleanness" — the inner life that should reflect divine purity is instead marked by death and corruption. Eph 5:5 (VCG-04): the impure person is equated with an idolater — their interior has displaced God with corrupt desire, revealing the image's most fundamental disruption (misplaced allegiance). The absence of the characteristic — the positive-inverse state — reveals the image functioning toward its intended fullness: Rev 14:4 (VCG-05), those not defiled follow the Lamb, are called firstfruits for God — the image is expressed in the orientation of the whole inner person toward God.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The presence of the corporate/covenantal defilement-state reveals a specific failure of the image-bearing vocation: the community created to reflect divine holiness in the land, to maintain covenant fidelity, and to guard the divine name has instead become the source of the land's pollution, the sanctuary's desecration, and the name's defilement. Eze 36:17 (VCG-04): "their ways before me were like the uncleanness of a woman in her menstrual impurity" — the corporate conduct has become repugnant to divine holiness. The absence of the characteristic — the condition of the community before the defection begins, or after restoration — reveals the image functioning: land kept holy (Num 35:34), sanctuary guarded (Eze 44:23/25), covenant fidelity maintained. Eze 20:43 (VCG-02) reveals a distinctive image-bearing moment: the future community will remember its defilement and "loathe yourselves for all the evils that you have committed" — even the memory of the defilement serves the image-bearing vocation of repentance.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The presence of defilement by external spiritual agency reveals the divine image as disrupted and occupied by an alien power: will overridden (Luk 8:29), communicative faculties suppressed (Mar 9:25), person's proper selfhood dominated by the spirit's agenda. The image-bearing functions (willing, communicating, relating) are not destroyed but overridden. The absence of the characteristic — or its reversal through expulsion — reveals the image functioning: the person restored to their own will, faculties returned, and communal access restored (Luk 9:42 — "gave him back to his father").

---

#### T0.4 — Typological Significance

##### T0.4.1 — Does Scripture use this characteristic typologically — deploying it to point toward or participate in a reality beyond the immediate (covenantal, eschatological, christological)?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes, at two points in the characteristic's 133-verse corpus. First, Num 19 (M10c-A-VCG-07): the red-heifer purification rite — the most elaborate response to the most severe defilement (corpse-contact) — is treated in the NT as a type of the blood of Christ (cited in Heb 9:13-14, though that verse is not in the M10c corpus). Within the corpus itself, the rite's structure — a sin offering preserved as a standing remedy for the entire congregation, administered through water — anticipates a purification economy beyond its own scope (Num 19:9: "it is a sin offering"). Second, the NT akathartos categorical revision (M10c-B-VCG-05: Act 10:14/28): the defilement category that shaped Peter's conscience is used by the divine vision to signal the covenantal transition — "what God has made clean, do not call unclean" (Act 10:28). The ritual-defilement-state category is deployed typologically as the boundary whose revision marks the new-covenant's extension to the nations.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes, in two moves evidenced in the corpus. First, the Hebrew prophetic register provides typological scaffolding for the NT moral-inner register: Job 14:4 (VCG-01), Isa 6:5 (VCG-01), and Isa 64:6 (VCG-01) all express the constitutional moral-inner defilement of the human before God, which the NT then addresses directly in terms of the gospel and sanctification. The Hebrew voices point forward to a problem the NT claims is addressed in Christ. Second, the positive-inverse in Rev 14:4 (VCG-05) — "these have not defiled themselves... they follow the Lamb... redeemed from mankind as firstfruits" — is explicitly christological-eschatological: the undefiled inner condition is defined in relation to the Lamb, constituting a typological participation in the Lamb's purity. The few in Rev 3:4 (VCG-05) who have "not soiled their garments" will "walk with me in white" — the white garments are eschatological, pointing toward divine fullness.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes, in two directions. First, the land-defilement register (VCG-04) and sanctuary-defilement register (VCG-03) function typologically in the prophetic corpus: the desecration of the physical land and temple in the pre-exilic prophets points forward to the eschatological restoration (Eze 37:23, Isa 52:1, Zec 13:1, VCG-05) in which both are permanently cleansed. The physical defilement and restoration is the type; the eschatological fullness is the antitype. Second, the cleansing fountain of Zec 13:1 (VCG-05) — "a fountain opened... to cleanse them from sin and uncleanness" — has a christological-typological dimension: the fountain that will address the corporate/covenantal defilement at a future eschatological moment is widely understood in the tradition as pointing toward the atonement. Within §3 alone, Zec 13:1 carries its own eschatological-promissory typological weight without requiring external cross-reference.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes. The pattern of unclean spirit possession, divine authority expelling the spirit, and the person restored — this narrative arc functions typologically for the NT's presentation of the kingdom of God. Mat 10:1 (VCG-03): authority over unclean spirits is paired with healing, framing it as a sign of the kingdom's arrival. Mar 3:11 (VCG-03) — the spirits' confession "You are the Son of God" — functions typologically as the cosmic acknowledgment of Christ's identity. The expulsion narratives function as enacted parables of the kingdom's defeat of the adversarial powers that hold humanity captive.

---

##### T0.4.2 — If typological use is present, what is the direction of the typology — does the human instance point toward the divine, or does the divine instance establish the pattern for the human?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The direction is bidirectional within the two typological instances identified at T0.4.1. In the Num 19 red-heifer rite, the human ritual instance (the most severe defilement state and its prescribed remedy) points forward and upward toward its divine antitype — the rite is the shadow; the cleansing power of Christ's sacrifice is the substance. In the Act 10 categorical revision, the divine initiative (God's voice declaring what is clean) establishes the pattern: the old human category (unclean persons/nations) is dissolved by divine speech, showing the divine instance as authoritative over the ritual category. In both cases, the ritual-defilement-state is the human creaturely structure that the divine economy uses as its scaffolding.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The direction is from the human negative instance toward the divine-eschatological positive. The Hebrew moral-inner defilement descriptions (Job 14:4, Isa 6:5, Isa 64:6, VCG-01) name a human problem in need of divine resolution — they point forward to the NT announcement that the problem is addressed. The call at 1Th 4:7 (VCG-02) — "God has not called us for impurity, but in holiness" — frames the divine calling as the telos that the person is moving toward. The typological direction is: human defilement (present) → divine call to holiness (active) → eschatological fullness of holiness (Rev 14:4) — human-to-eschatological. The divine does not establish defilement as a pattern for the human; the divine call to holiness establishes the goal the human defilement-state must be left behind.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The direction runs from the historical-covenantal instance toward the eschatological-divine antitype. The defilement of land, sanctuary, and name through Israel's corporate moral defection (the present historical instance evidenced in the pre-exilic corpus) points forward to a future divine act of comprehensive cleansing that exceeds the ritual and political restorations of the OT period. Eze 37:23 (VCG-05): "I will save... and will cleanse them" — the divine subject of the future cleansing is God himself; the human corporate defilement (the type) requires divine action (the antitype). The typological direction is thus upward and forward: from creaturely corporate failure toward divine eschatological redemption.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The direction is from the present historical instance toward the eschatological-divine antitype. The individual possession-and-expulsion events in the gospel narratives (Mar 1:23-27, Mar 5:2-13, Luk 8:29, Luk 9:42, VCG-01 and -02) are particular instances pointing forward to the comprehensive eschatological defeat of all adversarial spiritual powers. The divine instance — Christ's authority over unclean spirits — establishes the pattern: divine authority is supreme, and their defeat in individual cases anticipates their ultimate defeat at the consummation.

---

##### T0.4.3 — If no typological use is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Typological use is evidenced (see T0.4.1 and T0.4.2). No note required.

## T1 — Inner Being Faculty in Operation (24 prompts)

---

### T1

#### T1.1 — Name and Naming

##### T1.1.1 — What is this characteristic called in the programme — and what does the name itself signal about its essential nature?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic is named "Ritual defilement-state." The name signals three things. First, *ritual*: this is the register governed by cultic law and sacral practice, distinguishing this characteristic from the moral-inner defilement register (Characteristic 2) and the corporate-covenantal register (Characteristic 3). Second, *defilement*: the term names an active contamination — something has been transmitted, incurred, or declared; the person has not merely failed but has acquired a condition. Third, *state*: this is a condition of the person, not an act — the characteristic names what the person is in (a status), not what they do. The name therefore signals: a legally and ritually defined condition of contamination that attaches to the inner-being person through bodily mechanism or authoritative verdict.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic is named "Moral-inner defilement-state." Three elements of the name are analytically significant. *Moral*: the defilement is located in the moral domain — it concerns the inner person's orientation toward good, evil, right, and wrong, not merely a ritual or bodily condition. *Inner*: the locus is the interior of the person — conscience, will, heart — not external contact or authoritative verdict (that is Characteristic 1). *Defilement-state*: it is a condition, not an act — the person is in a state of corruption, not merely performing corrupt acts. The name signals that this characteristic is the inner-being condition of a morally compromised interior, which the evidence confirms: Mat 23:27 (VCG-04) — "within are full of dead people's bones and all uncleanness"; Eph 4:19 (VCG-02) — "greedy to practice every kind of impurity" arising from a silenced conscience.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The characteristic is named "Corporate/covenantal defilement." Three elements of the name are analytically significant. *Corporate*: the defilement extends beyond the individual to the community as a body — shared land, shared sanctuary, shared name, shared moral failure. *Covenantal*: the defilement operates within and against the covenantal relationship; it is betrayal of a specific relational bond between God and his people, not merely moral failure in general. *Defilement*: the state of contamination that results from the betrayal, spreading to the physical and sacral environment the community inhabits. The name thus signals: a condition of contamination that arises from corporate covenantal unfaithfulness and extends from the inner will of the community outward to land, sanctuary, and divine name.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The characteristic is named "Defilement by external spiritual agency." Four elements are analytically significant. *Defilement*: the characteristic produces the same inner-being condition as Characteristics 1-3 — the person is in a defiled state. *External*: the source of the defilement is outside the person, not from bodily contact (Characteristic 1), moral self-corruption (Characteristic 2), or corporate moral defection (Characteristic 3). *Spiritual*: the defiling agent is a spiritual being. *Agency*: the defiling force is an agent — purposeful, self-aware, volitional. The name signals: a condition of defilement imposed by a purposeful, external spiritual agent onto the inner and bodily life of the human person.

---

##### T1.1.2 — What do the primary Hebrew and Greek terms reveal at the definitional level — before deeper lexical analysis begins?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Three terms carry this characteristic. H2930A (ta.me, verb): "to be/become unclean" — the dynamic acquisition of the defilement-state; the action of contracting or entering it. H2931 (ta.me, adjective): "unclean" — the condition itself, the static description of one who has the state. H5079 (nid.dah): "menstrual impurity / impurity of separation" — the paradigm case of a time-bound, physiologically-sourced defilement state that governs not only menstruation (Lev 15:19-33, M10c-A-VCG-05) but bodily discharge impurity more broadly, and becomes the term for the water of impurity used in corpse-defilement cleansing (Num 19:9, M10c-A-VCG-07). G0169 (akathartos): "unclean" — the NT categorical term, carrying the same clean/unclean distinction into conscience-level conviction (Act 10:14, M10c-B-VCG-05) and covenantal-status application (1Cor 7:14). At the definitional level, the Hebrew verb/adjective pair shows defilement as both a dynamic event (acquiring the state) and a static condition (being in it); nid.dah shows it as a paradigm case governing a whole category; akathartos shows the categorical conviction operative in the inner conscience.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Five terms carry this characteristic. H2931 (ta.me adj): "unclean" — appearing in its Hebrew metaphorical-inner register here (Job 14:4, Isa 6:5, Isa 35:8, Isa 52:11, Isa 64:6, Hag 2:14, VCG-01 and -03/05), pointing to the inner condition of moral uncleanness before God. G0167 (akatharsia): "impurity" — the primary NT noun, appearing 10 times (VCG-02 and -04), consistently naming the inner condition of moral corruption in the flesh-desire register. G3435 (molunō): "to defile, soil" — a verb for the act of defiling the inner person (1Cor 8:7, Rev 3:4, Rev 14:4, VCG-03 and -05). G3436 (molusmos): "defilement" — the noun from the molunō root (2Cor 7:1, VCG-03). G3394 (miasmos): "defilement" — from miainō, to stain or pollute (2Pe 2:10, VCG-03). Definitionally, these terms together reveal the characteristic as: an inner condition of contamination (akatharsia, molusmos, miasmos — state nouns), producible through actions of the will (molunō — verb), and affecting the whole constitution of the person.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Three terms carry this characteristic, all Hebrew (the characteristic has no NT Greek evidence in its corpus): H2930A (ta.me verb, 63V): "to be/become unclean, to defile" — the dominant term, capturing both the act of defiling and the resulting condition. Its verb form is critical for Characteristic 3: the characteristic is frequently expressed as an active defiling of the land (Eze 36:17/18, VCG-04), sanctuary (Eze 5:11, VCG-03), and name (Eze 43:7/8, VCG-03) by the community's acts — the verb captures the dynamic of defilement as an act with consequences for sacred objects and spaces. H2931 (ta.me adj, 11V): "unclean" — the stative form naming the condition of persons, spaces, or objects once defiled (Eze 22:5 — "your name is defiled"; Lam 4:15 — "Unclean!"; Jos 22:19). H5079 (nid.dah, 9V): "impurity, menstrual impurity" — in the corporate-prophetic register, nid.dah is used metaphorically for moral uncleanness: Eze 36:17 ("their ways before me were like the uncleanness of a woman in her menstrual impurity"), Lam 1:17 ("Jerusalem has become a filthy thing among them").

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

One Greek term carries this characteristic exclusively: G0169 akathartos (alpha-privative + katharos — "not clean/pure"), always appearing as the modifier of pneuma ("unclean spirit" — pneuma akatharton). At the definitional level the term names the spirit's character — it is the un-clean spiritual force whose nature is the absence of holiness and the presence of defilement. Unique to Characteristic 4: the term names the character of the agent producing the condition, not the condition of the person. In Characteristics 1-3, the ta.me/akatharsia vocabulary names the condition of the person; here akathartos names the character of the agent.

---

##### T1.1.3 — Does the name carry directional, relational, or constitutional implications that orient the enquiry from the outset?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes, all three. Directional: the defilement-state is always moving toward something — toward restriction (from sacred participation), toward remedy (washing, waiting, examination), or toward communal re-entry. The corpus is structured around this directionality. Relational: the characteristic is inherently relational — it affects one's standing before God (access to the tabernacle, Lev 15:31 VCG-08), within community (social exclusion, Lev 13:46 VCG-03), and toward others (the duty not to transmit, Lev 15:11 VCG-06). Constitutional: the name "state" signals a condition of the whole person — not a faculty, not an act, but a status that bears on the person's constitutional integrity as a participant in the sacral community.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes, all three. Directional: "moral-inner" immediately orients the enquiry toward the interior of the person — the question is not what the person has touched or done outwardly but what has happened to the interior. The direction is inward, from the surface to the core. Relational: the defilement-state positions the person in a specific relational posture — away from divine holiness (1Th 4:7 — what God has not called the person for), away from Christ (Rev 3:4 — those not defiled walk with him), and in a corrupted relational posture toward God (Eph 5:5 — the impure person as idolater displacing God with corrupt desire). Constitutional: "state" signals that the enquiry is into the person's condition, not merely their behaviour — the characteristic is something the person is in, which has implications for the whole person's constitution (2Cor 7:1: "defilement of body and spirit").

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

All three. Directional: the defilement moves outward from the inner will of the community to the land, sanctuary, and divine name — a centrifugal movement from the community's inner disposition outward to the sacred environment it inhabits. Relational: the characteristic is constitutively relational — it requires the prior covenantal relationship (God-Israel) as the context within which the defilement of name, sanctuary, and land makes sense; outside that relationship there would be no "name" to defile, no "holy place" to desecrate. Constitutional: the characteristic spans individual and community — VCG-01 shows individual acts (adultery, Nazirite defilement) that have corporate consequences; VCG-02 and VCG-03 show the community as a whole (the city, the land, the house of Israel) as the subject of defilement.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

All three. Directional: *external* signals an inward invasion — the defilement moves from outside the person into the person's inner being, the opposite of Characteristic 2 (originating within the person's own desires). Constitutional: the defilement penetrates the whole person — will (Luk 8:29 — overriding all restraint), faculties (Mar 9:25 — speech and hearing suppressed), and bodily agency (Luk 8:29 — driven into the desert). Relational: the characteristic positions the person dominated by the unclean spirit, severed from communal life (Mar 5:2), accessible to divine authority (Mar 3:11), and in need of external intervention (Mat 10:1).

---

#### T1.2 — Kind

##### T1.2.1 — What kind of inner-being phenomenon does this characteristic appear to be — an act, a disposition, a condition, a quality, or something else?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic is a condition — a state the person is in, not an act they perform or a disposition they hold. The verse evidence consistently uses stative language: "he shall be unclean," "she is unclean," "his uncleanness is still on him" (Num 19:13, M10c-A-VCG-07). The condition has two acquisition mechanisms, both carrying their own structure: (1) the bodily-contact mechanism (M10c-A): the condition is incurred through specific physical interactions with defiling agents — touch, carry, proximity, ingestion; (2) the verdict mechanism (M10c-B): the condition is established through authoritative pronouncement — "the priest shall pronounce him unclean" (Lev 13:3 et al.). In both cases, the person is in the defilement-state; they did not choose it as a disposition and they do not enact it as an act — they are subject to it. However, within the condition, the will is engaged: one may seek remedy or refuse it (Num 19:20, M10c-A-VCG-07); one may volitionally avoid what causes it (Lev 11:43-44, M10c-A-VCG-04) or be warned to guard against it. The characteristic is a condition with strong volitional engagement at its perimeter.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Primarily a condition, but with a strong dispositional dimension. The noun forms (G0167 akatharsia, G3436 molusmos, G3394 miasmos) all name states the person is in. Rom 6:19 (VCG-02) — "slaves to impurity" — frames it as a condition of slavery: the will is not free but bound. Eph 4:19 (VCG-02) — "given themselves up to sensuality, greedy to practice every kind of impurity" — shows a dispositional dimension: the person has developed a habitual appetite for impurity once conscience has been silenced. 2Cor 12:21 (VCG-02) — "impurity... that they have practiced" — shows the condition as persistently practiced, revealing a dispositional pattern. The characteristic is thus a condition (present state of the inner person) with an entrenched dispositional character (habitual orientation of will and desire toward corruption) — not a single act, but a sustained state generated by repeated acts of will.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The characteristic is a condition with a strong dispositional-volitional generating force. As a condition: the land, sanctuary, and divine name are named as "defiled" — a stative condition of contamination that has been produced by the community's acts (H2931 ta.me adj — Eze 22:5: "your name is defiled"). As a dispositional-volitional generator: the evidence shows the acts of defiling arising from sustained corporate inner dispositions — habitual unfaithfulness (2Ch 36:14 VCG-03: "exceedingly unfaithful, following all the abominations of the nations"); persistent idolatrous lust (Eze 23:7 VCG-02: "she defiled herself with all the idols of everyone after whom she lusted"); deliberate will-acts (Jer 7:30 VCG-03: the sons of Judah "set their detestable things in the house that is called by my name, to defile it"). The characteristic is thus a condition (of land, sanctuary, name) produced by a dispositional-volitional inner reality (habitual unfaithfulness, desire-driven idolatry, deliberate desecration).

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The characteristic is a condition — a state of being invaded and dominated by an external spiritual agent, not an act the person performs or a disposition they hold. Mar 1:23 (VCG-01): "a man with an unclean spirit" — the having is a condition. Luk 8:29 (VCG-01): the spirit "had repeatedly seized him" — the seizure is an event producing a persisting condition of domination. The condition arises through spiritual invasion that bypasses the person's will entirely — distinct from all three other M10c characteristics in this regard.

---

##### T1.2.2 — Is this characteristic simple in structure or does it appear to have constituent elements at first encounter?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic has constituent elements even within its ritual register. The SPLIT_DESIGN_RATIONALE (carry-forward observation) identifies two mechanisms — bodily-contact (M10c-A) and verdict/categorical (M10c-B) — as complementary registers of one inner state. Within M10c-A alone, the constituent sub-registers are: carcass-contact (VCG-02), object-contamination (VCG-03), volitional self-defilement (VCG-04), menstrual/physiological (VCG-05), discharge-contact (VCG-06), corpse-contact (VCG-07), and sacred-boundary framing (VCG-08). Within M10c-B: discernment discipline (VCG-01), priestly verdict (VCG-02), public declaration/stigma (VCG-03), disease in objects/structures (VCG-04), and NT categorical conscience (VCG-05). The characteristic is not simple — it is a unified condition with differentiated sub-registers that share the core inner-being reality (the state of ritual uncleanness bearing on sacred access and conscience) but differ in mechanism, severity, duration, and resolution.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Composite in structure. The 26-verse corpus distributes across five VCGs, each identifying a distinct inner-being facet: VCG-01 (constitutional-existential uncleanness before God — Job 14:4, Isa 6:5, Isa 64:6, Hag 2:14), VCG-02 (impurity as flesh-dominion and habitual corruption — Rom 1:24, 6:19, 2Cor 12:21, Gal 5:19, Eph 4:19, Col 3:5, 1Th 2:3/4:7), VCG-03 (conscience and will as locus of defilement / deliberate self-purification — 1Cor 8:7, 2Cor 6:17, 2Cor 7:1, 2Pe 2:10, Isa 52:11), VCG-04 (heart allegiance disorder and idolatrous impurity — Mat 23:27, Eph 5:3/5:5, Rev 16:13/17:4/18:2), VCG-05 (maintained moral purity and consecrated non-defilement — Isa 35:8, Rev 3:4, Rev 14:4). These five facets are constituent elements of one condition: the inner person's moral corruption, experienced from the existential (VCG-01), dispositional-habitual (VCG-02), conscience-will (VCG-03), heart-allegiance (VCG-04), and positive-inverse (VCG-05) dimensions.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Composite. The 83-verse corpus distributes across five VCGs that identify distinct inner-being registers: VCG-01 (23V — sexual/covenantal-relational defilement: Gen 34, Num 5 ordeal, Lev 18 sexual prohibitions, Eze 18/22/33 sexual catalogues), VCG-02 (24V — idolatrous self-defilement: 2Ki 23 reforming king, Psa 106:39, Eze 20/22/23 idolatry corpus, Hos/Jer whoredom), VCG-03 (10V — sanctuary/sacred-space defilement: 2Ch 36:14, Psa 79:1, Jer 7:30/32:34, Eze 5:11/9:7/23:38/43:7/8/44:25), VCG-04 (9V — land defilement: Num 35:34, Deu 21:23, Jos 22:19, Jer 2:7, Eze 36:17/18, Hos 9:4, Mic 2:10), VCG-05 (17V — exile consequences and cleansing promise: Num 5:3/6:7/9/12, Isa 52:1, Jer 19:13, Lam 1:17/4:15, Eze 4:13/14/22:5/22:26/37:23/44:23, Hos 9:3, Amo 7:17, Zec 13:1). These five facets together constitute the corporate/covenantal defilement characteristic, held together by the shared structural feature: defilement of a sacred relational order.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Composite. Three VCGs identify distinct registers: VCG-01 (8V — the inhabited person's defilement-state: Mar 1:23, Mar 5:2/8, Mar 7:25, Mar 9:25, Luk 4:33, Luk 8:29, Luk 9:42), VCG-02 (8V — expulsion dynamics and restoration: Mat 12:43, Mar 1:26, Mar 3:30, Mar 5:13, Luk 6:18, Luk 11:24, Act 5:16, Act 8:7), VCG-03 (5V — authority over unclean spirits: Mat 10:1, Mar 1:27, Mar 3:11, Mar 6:7, Luk 4:36). Simple in that all 21 verses concern the same agent-type and person-type; composite in the different inner-being perspectives each VCG illuminates.

---

##### T1.2.3 — What is the current best working description of this characteristic — encapsulating its constitutional location, the faculties it primarily engages, and its impact on the person?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Ritual defilement-state: a legally and sacrally defined condition of the whole person — acquired through bodily contact with a defiling agent (corpse, discharge, carcass, fluid) or established through authoritative priestly examination and verdict — that restricts the person's access to sacred participation and communal life for a defined duration. Constitutionally, the condition bears on the person as embodied being in sacral community: the body is the locus of acquisition; the conscience, will, and social-relational capacity are primarily engaged in its management and resolution. Immediate impact: exclusion from worship and communal participation; duty of self-declaration; social distancing. The primary faculties engaged are: conscience (awakening to contamination incurred — Lev 5:2-3 VCG-01; grief at exclusion — Num 9:7 VCG-07), will (active watchfulness over bodily actions; pursuit or refusal of cleansing — Num 19:20 VCG-07), discernment (the faculty required for clean/unclean distinction — Lev 10:10 VCG-01 M10c-B), and social conscience (the duty not to transmit one's state — Lev 15:11 VCG-06). Structural opposite: M12 (purity/holiness).

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Moral-inner defilement-state: the condition of the inner person — conscience, will, and heart — in a state of corruption arising from desire, habitual sin, and allegiance disorder. The defilement is located within the person (not through external contact), penetrates the full inner-outer constitution (2Cor 7:1: "defilement of body and spirit"), and functions as a prior master that directs the will and bodily members toward escalating moral disorder (Rom 6:19, VCG-02). It encompasses the constitutional human vulnerability to moral uncleanness (Job 14:4, VCG-01), the habitual flesh-impulse register (Gal 5:19, VCG-02), the conscience as locus of defilement (1Cor 8:7, VCG-03), and the heart's displacement of God with corrupt desire (Eph 5:5, VCG-04). Its structural opposite is M12 (purity/holiness of the inner person). Its primary cross-register relationships are M10 (sin-act producing the state), M11 (cleansing as the active response), M29 (desire as vehicle), M08 (pride as companion), M09 (consecration as positive orientation).

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Corporate/covenantal defilement: the condition of contamination that extends from the community's inner volitional disposition (unfaithfulness, idolatrous desire, deliberate desecration) outward to the sacred relational order it inhabits — land defiled (Num 35:34, Jer 2:7, Eze 36:17/18, VCG-04), sanctuary desecrated (Eze 5:11, 2Ch 36:14, VCG-03), and divine name degraded (Eze 43:7/8, VCG-03). It includes both covenantal-relational defilement (sexual betrayal of covenant bonds — VCG-01, ordeal law, Nazirite defilement) and the corporate prophetic register (idolatry defiling sacred spaces — VCG-02, VCG-03). Its unique inner-being contribution is Eze 20:43 (VCG-02): memory of defilement functioning as the inner mechanism of corporate repentance. Structural opposite: M12 (purity/holiness of sacred space, divine name, covenant relationship).

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Defilement by external spiritual agency: the inner-being condition of a person whose will, faculties, and bodily agency are invaded and dominated by an unclean spirit — an external adversarial force that enters the person, overrides their self-possession (Luk 8:29 — "driven by the demon"), suppresses their communicative faculties (Mar 9:25 — "mute and deaf spirit"), severs their communal access (Mar 5:2), and subjects their bodily agency to the spirit's purposes. The spirits recognise and submit to superior divine authority (Mar 3:11, Luk 4:36, VCG-03) and resist expulsion (Act 8:7). Restoration reverses the condition, returning the person to wholeness (Luk 6:18 — "were cured") and communal belonging (Luk 9:42 — "gave him back to his father"). Structural opposite: M12 (purity/wholeness).

---

#### T1.3 — Boundary

##### T1.3.1 — What is the structural opposite of this characteristic — the inner-being reality that stands against or excludes it?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The structural opposite is M12 (Purity). Every sub-group and VCG in the characteristic's 133-verse corpus names purity as the positive state that defilement opposes. The vocabulary of clean/unclean (tahor/tame) is a binary pair: to be clean is to be eligible for sacred access; to be unclean is to be excluded from it. Lev 10:10 (M10c-B-VCG-01) frames the opposition as the core priestly vocation: "to distinguish between the holy and the common, and between the unclean and the clean." Lev 15:31 (M10c-A-VCG-08) frames the stakes: defilement must be separated from the people "lest they die" by contaminating the divine dwelling. The Deu 12:15/22/15:22 (M10c-A-VCG-08) verses show the clean as the norm: those without defilement eat sacred food while the unclean are restricted to common eating. M12 (purity) is not simply the absence of defilement but an actively maintained positive condition of readiness for divine access.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

M12 (Purity/holiness of the inner person) is the structural opposite, confirmed throughout the corpus. The binary is explicit at 1Th 4:7 (VCG-02): "God has not called us for impurity, but in holiness" — holiness (M12) and impurity (Characteristic 2) are named as antitheses within a single divine calling. 2Cor 7:1 (VCG-03): "cleanse ourselves from every defilement of body and spirit, bringing holiness to completion" — the goal of cleansing from defilement is the positive completion of holiness. Isa 35:8 (VCG-05): "the unclean shall not pass over" the Way of Holiness — the holy Way excludes the morally unclean. Rev 3:4 (VCG-05): those who have "not soiled their garments" walk with Christ "in white" — moral purity is the positive state. The structural opposite M12 is present implicitly in every verse and explicitly in several.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

M12 (Purity/holiness of sacred space, divine name, and covenant relationship) is the structural opposite, confirmed throughout the corpus. The binary is explicit at Eze 44:23 (VCG-05): "they shall teach my people the difference between the holy and the common, and show them how to distinguish between the unclean and the clean" — the clean/unclean and holy/common binaries are paired as the governing distinctions. Eze 37:23 (VCG-05): "they shall not defile themselves anymore... and they shall be my people, and I will be their God" — the positive covenant formula ("my people / my God") is the structural opposite of the defilement-state; restored relationship is the positive. Isa 52:1 (VCG-05): "put on your beautiful garments, O Jerusalem, the holy city; for there shall no more come into you the uncircumcised and the unclean" — holiness of the city (M12) is the eschatological positive that the defilement opposes.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

M12 (Purity/wholeness) is the structural opposite, confirmed by the restoration language throughout VCG-02. Luk 6:18 (VCG-02): "were cured" — wholeness is the positive M12 state restored. Luk 9:42 (VCG-01): "Jesus rebuked the unclean spirit and healed the boy" — healing is the positive state the spirit's presence had suspended. The structural opposite is not merely the absence of the spirit but the positive condition of wholeness — freedom from invasion, full possession of one's own faculties and bodily agency, restored communal access.

---

##### T1.3.2 — What does this characteristic explicitly exclude or resist?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The ritual defilement-state explicitly excludes the person from: (1) sacred eating — flesh touching an unclean thing is burned and may not be eaten (Lev 7:19 M10c-A-VCG-08); eating holy things while unclean is the grounds for being "cut off" (Lev 7:21 M10c-A-VCG-08; Lev 22:4 M10c-B-VCG-03); (2) communal worship participation — the Passover (Num 9:6-7 M10c-A-VCG-07); the Lord's offering; (3) residence within the community — those with discharge or skin disease are sent out of the camp (Num 5:2 M10c-A-VCG-07; Lev 13:46 M10c-B-VCG-03: "he shall live alone; his dwelling shall be outside the camp"); (4) sacred tithe-giving — Deu 26:14 (M10c-B-VCG-01) the worshiper must declare freedom from unclean state at tithe time; (5) proximity to the divine tabernacle — unchecked defilement risks defiling the tabernacle (Lev 15:31; Num 19:13 M10c-A-VCG-07/08).

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The moral-inner defilement-state explicitly excludes: (1) divine inheritance and kingdom membership — Eph 5:5 (VCG-04): "everyone who is... impure... has no inheritance in the kingdom of Christ and God"; (2) divine welcome — 2Cor 6:17 (VCG-03): "touch no unclean thing; then I will welcome you" — touching what is unclean is the barrier to divine welcome; (3) access to the eschatological Way of Holiness — Isa 35:8 (VCG-05): "the unclean shall not pass over it"; (4) the naming and communal identity of saints — Eph 5:3 (VCG-04): impurity "must not even be named among you, as is proper among saints"; (5) right motivation before God — 1Th 2:3 (VCG-02): the apostolic appeal does not spring "from impurity"; (6) worthiness for eschatological fellowship with Christ — Rev 3:4 (VCG-05): those not soiled are "worthy" to walk with Christ.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The corporate/covenantal defilement-state explicitly excludes: (1) divine presence in the defiled space — Num 35:34 (VCG-04): "you shall not defile the land in which you live, in the midst of which I dwell" — defilement and divine habitation are incompatible; (2) divine inquiry and engagement — Eze 20:31 (VCG-02): "shall I be inquired of by you, O house of Israel? As I live, declares the Lord God, I will not be inquired of by you" — persistent idolatrous self-defilement closes divine accessibility; (3) land possession and rest — Mic 2:10 (VCG-04): "this is no place to rest, because of uncleanness that destroys with a grievous destruction" — defilement disqualifies the land for habitation; (4) covenantal integrity and blessing — Num 5:27/28 (VCG-01): the defiled woman receives the curse; the undefiled receives blessing and children.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The characteristic explicitly suppresses: (1) speech and hearing — Mar 9:25 (VCG-01): Jesus addresses the spirit as "mute and deaf" — both faculties suppressed; (2) communal access — Mar 5:2 (VCG-01): "utterly cut off from clean, communal life"; (3) self-directed bodily agency — Luk 8:29 (VCG-01): "driven by the demon into the desert"; (4) the presence and authority of divine power — the spirits resist expulsion (Act 8:7 — crying out; Mar 5:8 — command must be issued); (5) restoration to familial/social belonging — Luk 9:42 — "gave him back to his father" implies the spirit had severed the familial bond.

---

##### T1.3.3 — What is this characteristic not — where does it end and something else begin?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Characteristic 1 (Ritual defilement-state) is not: (1) moral guilt arising from sin-acts (that is M10 territory — the cross-register flags on H2930A point to M10 where the sin-act producing defilement is the focus); (2) moral-inner defilement of the conscience, will, and heart by desire or habitual corruption (that is Characteristic 2, M10c-C sub-group); (3) corporate-covenantal defilement of land, sanctuary, and divine name through apostasy (that is Characteristic 3, M10c-D sub-group); (4) defilement by external spiritual agency (Characteristic 4, M10c-E sub-group). Within Characteristic 1's domain, the defilement-state is not identical to shame (M07 cross-register): the men at Num 9:7 grieve but are not shamed — their state is involuntary and accommodated. The defilement-state ends where the verdict of clearance is pronounced (Lev 13 — priestly re-examination clears the disease), where the waiting period expires and washing completes (Lev 11:24: "shall be unclean until the evening"), or where the water of impurity is applied (Num 19:19-20).

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Characteristic 2 (Moral-inner defilement-state) is not: (1) Characteristic 1 (Ritual defilement-state) — the moral-inner register operates through the inner person's own volitional and dispositional corruption, not through bodily contact with defiling agents or authoritative verdict; (2) the sin-act itself (M10) — the moral-inner defilement-state is the condition produced by or accompanying the sin-act, not the act itself; at Rom 1:24 (VCG-02), God's giving over to impurity follows the sin-act of rejecting God (Rom 1:21-23), not simultaneous with it; (3) shame (M07) — the defilement-state is an interior moral condition, not the social-relational experience of disgrace; (4) Characteristic 3 (Corporate-covenantal defilement) — Characteristic 2 operates in the individual inner person's conscience, will, and heart, not in the corporate-sacral space; (5) Characteristic 4 (External spiritual agency defilement) — Characteristic 2 originates from within the person's own desires and choices, not from an inhabiting spiritual force. The boundary with Characteristic 1 is the most important: same vocabulary (ta.me, akathartos) but different locus (inner-volitional vs bodily-mechanical).

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Characteristic 3 (Corporate/covenantal defilement) is not: (1) Characteristic 1 (Ritual defilement-state) — Characteristic 3 operates through moral defection and covenantal betrayal, not through bodily contact with defiling agents; Eze 44:25 (VCG-03) — priestly corpse-contact defilement — sits at the boundary; it is in Characteristic 3's corpus because of its priestly-vocational context (guarding the sanctuary), not because it is a ritual contact defilement; (2) Characteristic 2 (Moral-inner defilement-state) — Characteristic 3 extends to land, sanctuary, and name; Characteristic 2 remains within the individual inner person; the prophetic Ezekiel material in Characteristic 3 shows the community's inner disposition producing contamination of the external sacred environment, which is the distinctive Characteristic 3 feature; (3) M10 (Sin-act) — the sin-acts that produce Characteristic 3 belong to M10; Characteristic 3 is the defilement-state that results from those acts, not the acts themselves; (4) M10b (Wickedness/abomination) — the Ezekiel idolatry corpus carries both M10b and M10c flags; Characteristic 3 owns the defilement-state produced by the idolatrous acts; M10b owns the abomination character of those same acts.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Characteristic 4 is not: (1) Characteristic 1 (Ritual defilement-state) — Characteristic 4's defilement is produced by a spiritual agent, not bodily contact with a material defiling object; (2) Characteristic 2 (Moral-inner defilement-state) — Characteristic 4's condition arrives from outside the person without volitional cooperation; the person is not morally guilty for the condition; (3) Characteristic 3 (Corporate/covenantal defilement) — Characteristic 4 operates at the individual level through direct spiritual invasion; (4) M27 (Cosmic-evil agents) — Characteristic 4 is the defilement-state produced in the human person; M27 analyses the character and nature of the unclean spirits themselves. The two are complementary analytical lenses, not the same characteristic.

---
