#### T1.4 — Modes of Operation

##### T1.4.1 — In what distinct ways does this characteristic operate within the inner person?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The ritual defilement-state operates in the inner person in at least four distinct ways evidenced across the 133 verses. (1) As a conscience-awakening signal: Lev 5:2-3 (M10c-A-VCG-01) — defilement may be incurred unknowingly, but when the person "comes to know it and realises his guilt," the conscience surfaces the condition. The defilement arrives before the inner recognition; recognition is its own distinct event. (2) As a duty-forming constraint on the will: the person in the defilement-state must not transmit it (Lev 15:11, M10c-A-VCG-06), must wash and wait, must present for examination, must not enter the tabernacle. The will operates under a structured set of obligations arising from the state. (3) As a grief-producing exclusion: Num 9:7 (M10c-A-VCG-07) — "why are we kept from bringing the Lord's offering?" The men's grief shows the defilement-state operating in the affective dimension — the desire for worship blocked by the condition they are in. (4) As a discernment-forming discipline: M10c-B-VCG-01 — the cultivation of the clean/unclean distinction is a perceptual and volitional discipline formed through sustained engagement with the characteristic's categorical structure.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The moral-inner defilement-state operates in at least four distinct ways within the inner person. (1) As constitutional ontological condition: Job 14:4 (VCG-01) — the impossibility of a clean thing from an unclean origin; the defilement is the person's constituted inner state before action. (2) As habitual flesh-dominion: Rom 6:19 (VCG-02) — "slaves to impurity" — the will's freedom is constrained by the defilement as a prior master; the person is not free but bound toward escalating moral disorder. (3) As silenced conscience leading to active greed: Eph 4:19 (VCG-02) — "become callous and have given themselves up to sensuality, greedy to practice every kind of impurity" — the conscience's silencing enables an active, appetitive pursuit of defilement. (4) As defiled conscience that makes the person's inner moral assessment unreliable: 1Cor 8:7 (VCG-03) — the weak person's conscience is defiled by eating food associated with idols; the defiled conscience cannot form correct moral assessment because the standard itself has been compromised.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The corporate/covenantal defilement-state operates in the inner person in four distinct ways. (1) As a condition of the corporate will in sustained defection: Eze 14:11 (VCG-02) — "that the house of Israel may no more go astray from me, nor defile themselves anymore with all their transgressions" — the defilement-state is the inner expression of a repeatedly straying will. (2) As self-deception regarding one's own condition: Jer 2:23 (VCG-02) — "how can you say, 'I am not unclean, I have not gone after the Baals'?" — the defiled inner condition is denied by the will that is in it; the characteristic includes self-deceived non-recognition of the defilement. (3) As memory functioning as repentance mechanism: Eze 20:43 (VCG-02) — "there you shall remember your ways and all your deeds with which you have defiled yourselves, and you shall loathe yourselves for all the evils that you have committed" — the memory of the defilement-state in exile becomes the inner generative mechanism of self-loathing and repentance. (4) As a condition observed and held by God: Eze 23:13 (VCG-02) — "I saw that she was defiled" — God's divine perception holds the defilement as an objective spiritual reality.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Four distinct ways. (1) Will-domination: Luk 8:29 (VCG-01) — "repeatedly seized him, overpowering all human restraint" and "driven by the demon" — the spirit overrides the person's own volitional direction. (2) Faculty-suppression: Mar 9:25 (VCG-01) — "mute and deaf spirit" — speech and hearing are suppressed, cutting off communicative capacity. (3) Communal-severance: Mar 5:2 (VCG-01) — the man among the tombs utterly cut off; Mar 7:25 — the child's affliction drives the mother to seek external help. (4) Violent bodily affliction: Mar 1:26 (VCG-02): "convulsing him and crying out"; Luk 9:42 (VCG-01): "the demon threw him to the ground and convulsed him."

---

##### T1.4.2 — Does this characteristic operate differently depending on context, direction, or constitutional level?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes, the characteristic operates with different severity, duration, and moral weight depending on the defiling agent and mechanism. In the bodily-contact register (M10c-A): carcass-contact and discharge-contact are typically one-day (until-evening) defilements; corpse-contact is seven-day with the prescribed remedy of water of impurity (Num 19:11, M10c-A-VCG-07) — the most severe and elaborate. Object contamination (M10c-A-VCG-03) is irreversible for earthenware (Lev 11:33 — must be broken). In the verdict/categorical register (M10c-B): disease in persons may be permanent for the duration (Lev 13:46 — "as long as he has the disease"); disease in objects and structures may culminate in demolition (Lev 14:44-45). At the constitutional level, the characteristic operates across the body (as the locus of acquisition), the conscience (as the site of awakening and guilt), and the will (as the site of volitional response). The NT register (M10c-B-VCG-05) shows the characteristic operating at the conscience-level conviction formed by the categorical system — Peter's resistance (Act 10:14) is a deeply formed inner conviction, not mere ritual compliance.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes, across three evident distinctions. By depth: the constitutional-existential register (VCG-01 — Job 14:4, Isa 64:6) describes the condition at the deepest constitutional level — the human person as inherently morally compromised before God; this is prior to specific acts. The habitual-dispositional register (VCG-02 — Rom 6:19, Eph 4:19, Col 3:5) describes the condition as it operates through sustained patterns of will and desire. The conscience-faculty register (VCG-03 — 1Cor 8:7) describes it operating in a specific faculty (conscience) through a specific act (eating food against conviction). By direction: the passive direction — defilement as a state the person is already in (Rom 6:19: "once presented as slaves"); and the active direction — the greedy pursuit of more defilement once the constraint of conscience is removed (Eph 4:19). By scope: individual conscience (1Cor 8:7) vs corporate moral state (Isa 64:6: "we have all become...") — the condition operates at both individual and corporate dimensions.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes, across three axes. By object of defilement: the characteristic operates differently when it defiles a person (sexual betrayal — VCG-01), a place (land — VCG-04, sanctuary — VCG-03), or a name (divine name — Eze 43:7/8, VCG-03). The inner-being content shifts: personal defilement engages the will's volitional choice (Lev 18:20: "make yourself unclean"); sanctuary defilement engages the corporate leadership's habitual defection (2Ch 36:14: "exceedingly unfaithful"); land defilement engages the community's moral conduct over time (Eze 36:17: "habitual conduct defiled the land"). By direction: active self-defilement (Eze 22:3 — "a city that makes idols to defile herself") vs passive-receptive defilement (Eze 23:17 — "the Babylonians... defiled her with their whoring lust" — external agents defiling through corrupting relations). By outcome: some defiling acts produce judicial consequences in the body (Num 5:27 — ordeal-water producing physical judgment); others produce social expulsion (Lam 4:15 — "Unclean! Away!"); others produce divine withdrawal (Eze 5:11).

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes. By severity: Mar 5:2/8 (VCG-01) — the Gerasene demoniac is the most severe case; Luk 8:29 — "repeatedly seized him, overpowering all human restraint." Mar 7:25 (VCG-01) — a child with an unclean spirit is a less severe case. By faculty affected: Mar 9:25 — specifically mute and deaf; Luk 8:29 — bodily agency overridden; Mar 1:26 — convulsing. By social setting: Mar 1:23 (VCG-01) — the synagogue; Mar 5:2 — social exclusion among tombs. Expulsion dynamics also vary: some depart with loud cries (Mar 1:26, Act 8:7); Mat 12:43/Luk 11:24 show the spirit's post-expulsion restlessness.

---

##### T1.4.3 — Does this characteristic have a communicative or speech-based mode of operation — and if so, how does it function?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes, at two points. First, the public self-declaration of the unclean state: Lev 13:45 (M10c-B-VCG-03) — the person bearing skin disease "shall cry out 'Unclean, unclean.'" The inner reality of contamination is verbalized outward through ritual cry. The speech act is not merely announcement; it is the socially constitutive declaration that activates the community's protective response (maintaining distance). Second, the priestly pronouncement of the verdict: throughout M10c-B-VCG-02, "the priest shall pronounce him unclean" (Lev 13:3, 13:8, 13:11, 13:14, 13:15, 13:20, 13:22, 13:25, 13:27, 13:30, 13:44). The priestly speech act establishes the condition officially — it is not merely descriptive but performative. The condition exists objectively but is socially activated by the authoritative pronouncement.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes, at two evidenced points. First, Isa 6:5 (VCG-01): the prophet names his own defilement in speech — "I am a man of unclean lips" — the conscience's recognition of the moral-inner defilement-state is expressed in first-person verbal declaration. The speech is the moment the inner condition is named and acknowledged before God. Second, Mat 23:27 (VCG-04): the Woe pronouncement is the authoritative naming of the defilement that is hidden within — Jesus's speech act makes the inner defilement visible and declares its incompatibility with the name "holy." The communicative mode here is prophetic/judicial: the external word exposes what the inner condition has concealed. Third, by negative implication: Eph 5:3 (VCG-04) — impurity "must not even be named among you" — naming the condition within the community of saints is itself a violation; the word-act of naming defilement where it should not be named is forbidden.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes, at three evidenced points. (1) Public declaration of the corporate defiled condition: Lam 4:15 (VCG-05) — "Unclean! Away!" directed at the exiles — the community's defilement is proclaimed publicly by those who encounter them; the speech act activates social expulsion. (2) Divine naming of the defiled condition: Eze 22:5 (VCG-05) — "your name is defiled" — God's speech act declares the corporate defilement as a public moral identity. (3) The ordeal law's verbal self-declaration: Num 5:13-29 (VCG-01) — the woman is brought before God; the word of the ordeal names the defilement as either present or absent; the divine verdict through the ordeal water either confirms or denies the defilement. (4) The prophetic challenge: Jer 2:23 (VCG-02) — "how can you say, 'I am not unclean'?" — prophetic speech confronts the community's self-deceptive denial of their defilement-state.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes, prominently — the speech operates through the inhabited person, not as the person's own speech. Mar 1:23 (VCG-01): "he cried out" — the man cries out through the spirit's prompting. Mar 3:11 (VCG-03): "they fell down before him and cried out, 'You are the Son of God'" — the spirits use the person's voice to confess divine identity. Mar 1:26 (VCG-02): "crying out with a loud voice" at departure. Act 8:7 (VCG-02): "crying out with a loud voice, came out of many." The spirit appropriates the person's voice as its own instrument of declaration, resistance, and departure — the human voice becomes the medium of adversarial spiritual speech.

---

#### T1.5 — Immediate Response

##### T1.5.1 — What is the first or most immediate inner-being response to receiving or encountering this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The most immediate response evidenced in the corpus is conscience awakening — the moment of recognition that the condition has been incurred. Lev 5:2-3 (M10c-A-VCG-01) describes this precisely: "it is hidden from him and he has become unclean, and he realises his guilt." The defilement precedes awareness; the awakening of guilt is the immediate inner response when the person "comes to know it." A second immediate response is grief at the prospect of exclusion: Num 9:7 (M10c-A-VCG-07) — the men approach Moses immediately upon recognising their condition and express the grief of being "kept from bringing the Lord's offering." The immediacy is notable — they do not wait; the exclusion motivates immediate approach to leadership. These two immediate responses — conscience awakening and grief-driven seeking — characterise the well-formed inner response to the defilement-state in the evidence.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The most immediate inner response evidenced is the recognition of moral collapse in the presence of divine holiness. Isa 6:5 (VCG-01): upon seeing divine holiness the prophet's immediate response is "woe is me! For I am lost; for I am a man of unclean lips" — the encounter with holiness triggers immediate conscience-activated self-recognition of the defilement-state. The response is a cry of distress and lostness. A second immediate response is shown at 2Cor 7:1 (VCG-03): "let us cleanse ourselves from every defilement of body and spirit" — the recognition of defilement in the context of divine promises triggers an active first-response of self-purification. These two immediate responses (self-recognition in distress and active cleansing) represent the two poles of the characteristic's immediate register.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Three immediate inner responses are evidenced, varying by register. (1) Restrained grief and simmering awareness (VCG-01 — Gen 34:5): Jacob's immediate response to the violation of Dinah is restrained, simmering awareness — "Jacob held his peace until they came"; the inner impact is named as felt violation. (2) Jealousy as immediate affective response (VCG-01 — Num 5:14): the spirit of jealousy comes over the husband when he suspects his wife has defiled herself — jealousy is the immediate inner response to suspected covenantal betrayal. (3) Self-loathing as future eschatological response (VCG-02 — Eze 20:43): in the restoration, the community will remember its defilements and loathe itself — this is a prospective immediate response named as the desired future inner state when the community finally perceives what it has done.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Two immediate response patterns are evidenced — in observers and in proxies, not in the affected person. For observers: Mar 1:27 (VCG-03) — amazement ("they were all amazed... 'What is this?'"); Luk 4:36 (VCG-03) — "they were all amazed" at Jesus's authority. For proxies seeking help: Mar 7:25 (VCG-01) — "immediately a woman... came and fell down at his feet" — urgent supplication. For the divine response: Mar 5:8 (VCG-01) — "Come out of the man, you unclean spirit!" is the immediate divine response to encountering the condition.

---

##### T1.5.2 — Is the immediate response consistent across the verse evidence, or does it vary?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The immediate response varies, and the variation itself is significant. The well-formed response is conscience awakening, grief at exclusion, and active pursuit of remedy — as at Lev 5:2-3 and Num 9:7. But Num 19:20 (M10c-A-VCG-07) shows the deviant response: "if the man who is unclean does not cleanse himself, that person shall be cut off from the midst of the assembly." The will can refuse remedy rather than pursue it. The willful non-cleansing is treated as the decisive moral fault — not the defilement itself but the failure to respond to it through the appointed remedy. This contrast between the grief-driven seeking of Num 9:7 and the willful refusal of Num 19:20 shows the characteristic as a diagnostic of the inner person: the same condition produces either conscience-awakened pursuit or will-hardened resistance, revealing the inner orientation of the person.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The immediate response varies significantly across the 26-verse corpus. Three distinct immediate response patterns are evidenced. (1) Conscience-activated distress and recognition (Isa 6:5, VCG-01 — "woe is me"); (2) Active self-purification (2Cor 7:1, VCG-03 — "let us cleanse ourselves"); (3) Hardened non-response — the opposite of recognition — in the cases where the defilement has advanced far enough that the conscience is silenced: Eph 4:19 (VCG-02) — "become callous," giving themselves up to impurity; 2Cor 12:21 (VCG-02) — those who "have not repented." The variation reveals that the characteristic does not produce a uniform response — it produces recognition and distress in those whose conscience remains active, and entrenched non-response in those whose conscience has been suppressed.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The immediate response varies significantly. The corporate idolatry register (VCG-02) shows self-deception as the dominant immediate inner response: Jer 2:23 — "how can you say, 'I am not unclean'?" — the community's immediate inner response is denial and self-justification rather than recognition. The exile register (VCG-05) shows shame and expulsion as the immediate social response: Lam 1:17 — Jerusalem becomes "a filthy thing among them"; Lam 4:15 — "Unclean! Away!" The ordeal register (VCG-01) shows the social mechanism of judgment as the immediate outcome. The variation shows that immediate response depends on who is perceiving the defilement: the community in the defilement-state denies it; God perceives it clearly (Eze 23:13); the surrounding nations expel the defiled community; prophetic speech confronts the self-deception.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The immediate response varies by actor. (1) Divine response: consistently authoritative command — Mar 5:8, Mar 9:25, Luk 9:42. (2) Observer response: consistently amazement at the authority (Mar 1:27, Luk 4:36). (3) Spirit response: consistently submission despite resistance (Mar 1:26 — departing; Act 8:7 — crying out but departing). (4) Family/proxy response: immediate seeking of help (Mar 7:25 — the mother; Luk 9:42 — father receiving son back). (5) The affected person's own immediate response: not narrated — the condition suppresses the person's capacity for self-expression.

---

##### T1.5.3 — Where the verse evidence is silent on immediate response, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The evidence is not silent. Both varieties of immediate response (conscience-awakening/grief-seeking and willful non-response) are directly evidenced. However, the large majority of the 133 verses describe the condition and its prescribed remedy without narrating the person's inner response — they are normative/legal rather than narrative. Immediate response is directly evidenced at Lev 5:2-3, Num 9:6-7, Num 19:20, and Lev 13:45 (the self-declaration cry). The remaining verses provide structural information about the condition but leave the inner response implicit.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The evidence is not uniformly silent — three patterns of immediate response are evidenced (T1.5.2 above). However, the majority of the 26 verses (particularly the legal-didactic VCG-02 corpus: Gal 5:19, Col 3:5, 1Th 2:3/4:7) describe the condition without narrating the person's immediate inner response to recognising it. In these cases the verse evidence is silent on the immediate response and focuses instead on the condition's nature and the calling away from it.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The evidence is not uniformly silent — immediate responses are evidenced across VCGs (Gen 34:5, Num 5:14, Jer 2:23, Lam 4:15, Eze 23:13, Eze 20:43). However, the large majority of the prophetic-legal corpus (Lev 18, Num 35, Deu 21/24, Eze 5/7/9/22/36/43, Hos, Mic) describes the condition and its consequences without narrating a specific immediate inner response. The evidence base is substantially normative/prophetic rather than narrative.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The evidence is silent on the immediate inner-being response of the affected person from within the condition. In all 21 verses, the person in the defilement-state does not narrate or express their own immediate inner response — they are under the spirit's domination. This silence is analytically significant: Characteristic 4 is the only M10c characteristic where the affected person's own inner response to being in the condition is structurally inaccessible — the domination that constitutes the characteristic is what prevents the person from narrating their response to it.

---

#### T1.6 — Sustained Effect

##### T1.6.1 — What does this characteristic produce in the inner being over time?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Sustained engagement with the ritual defilement-state and its management produces two documented inner-being effects over time. First, a formed conscience shaped by the clean/unclean categorical system. M10c-B-VCG-01 (Lev 10:10, 11:47, 14:57, 20:25, Deu 26:14) shows this most clearly: the purity laws exist to cultivate "active moral discernment" — distinguishing clean from unclean becomes "a perceptual and volitional discipline central to covenant life" (Lev 11:47). Peter's conviction at Act 10:14 (M10c-B-VCG-05) — "I have never eaten anything that is common or unclean" — shows the accumulated effect of a lifetime of categorical formation: the conviction is so deeply embedded it resists even divine instruction at first. Second, a vigilant bodily discipline — the duty of watchfulness over bodily actions near defiling agents (Lev 11:24-40, M10c-A-VCG-02; Lev 15:11, M10c-A-VCG-06) becomes an ongoing orientation of the person toward their bodily life and its sacral consequence.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The verse evidence documents a specific trajectory of inner-being deterioration from sustained moral-inner defilement. Rom 1:24 (VCG-02): God "gave them up in the lusts of their hearts to impurity, to the dishonoring of their bodies" — the impurity deepens and expands outward to bodily dishonour when unchecked. Rom 6:19 (VCG-02): "lawlessness leading to more lawlessness" — the defilement-state produces escalating moral disorder over time; the trajectory is intensification. Eph 4:19 (VCG-02): "become callous... greedy to practice every kind of impurity" — the sustained state produces a progressive hardening of the conscience (callousness) and an active appetite for more defilement (greed). The sequence evidenced by these three verses together: initial defilement → unchecked desire → God's judicial abandonment → bodily dishonour → moral escalation → conscience hardened → active seeking of defilement. The characteristic produces, over time, a person whose inner life is progressively oriented away from God and toward deepening corruption.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Sustained corporate/covenantal defilement produces several documented inner-being consequences over time. Eze 20:26/31 (VCG-02): God allows the defilement to deepen through judicial release ("I defiled them through their very gifts") and persistent self-defilement results in God refusing to be inquired of — over time the defilement closes relational access with God. Eze 22:3-4 (VCG-02): the city "makes idols to defile herself" — the defilement becomes self-directed and deliberate over time, evolving from an incidental consequence to an intentional act. Jer 2:23 (VCG-02): sustained self-deception about one's own defilement develops — the community can no longer perceive its own condition. Lam 1:17/4:15 (VCG-05): the sustained defilement produces the outcome of being named "a filthy thing among the nations" and expelled — corporate moral identity becomes publicly defiled over time.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Two forms of sustained effect. (1) Progressive entrenchment of domination: Luk 8:29 (VCG-01) — "for many a time it had seized him" — sustained operation is a repeated pattern of seizure; all human attempts at restraint fail. The domination extends to all external remedies ("bound with chains and shackles, but he would break the bonds"). (2) Social and relational deterioration: Mar 5:2 (VCG-01) — the man among the tombs thoroughly isolated from communal life; sustained possession has reduced him to dwelling in a place of death. The sustained effect of the characteristic is total: will, faculties, communal belonging, and bodily agency all subsumed under the spirit's domination.

---

##### T1.6.2 — What states, qualities, capacities, or orientations does sustained exposure to or possession of this characteristic establish?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Sustained engagement with the ritual defilement-state establishes: (1) the orientation of sacral vigilance — the person habituated to the clean/unclean boundary becomes watchful over bodily actions, over what they touch, eat, and carry; (2) the capacity for discernment — the clean/unclean distinction is the base capacity on which more complex moral-spiritual perception builds (Lev 10:10, M10c-B-VCG-01); (3) the orientation of communal responsibility — the duty not to transmit one's state (Lev 15:11 M10c-A-VCG-06; the Lev 13:45 self-declaration requirement) forms the person in awareness of their relational impact; (4) humility before the body's creaturely vulnerability — the physiological defilement register (M10c-A-VCG-05: Lev 12 and Lev 15 menstrual) attaches defilement to natural processes, forming the person in acceptance of embodied limitation without moral shame; (5) dependence on prescribed remedy — the standing availability of cleansing (water of impurity, Num 19:9) forms the person in an orientation of ongoing reliance on divinely provided resolution.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Sustained moral-inner defilement establishes: (1) callousness — the progressive suppression of conscience (Eph 4:19, VCG-02: "become callous"); (2) lawlessness as an inner orientation — the will directed toward "lawlessness leading to more lawlessness" (Rom 6:19, VCG-02); (3) active moral appetite — "greedy to practice every kind of impurity" (Eph 4:19, VCG-02); (4) hardened will resistant to repentance — 2Cor 12:21 (VCG-02): those who "have not repented of the impurity... that they have practiced"; (5) a defiled cognitive-moral faculty — Tit 1:15 is cross-referenced at VCG-03: "to the defiled and unbelieving, nothing is pure; both their minds and their consciences are defiled." Over time the characteristic establishes an inner person in whom the faculties meant to orient the person toward God (conscience, mind, moral evaluation) are all compromised.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Sustained corporate/covenantal defilement establishes: (1) inability to approach God — Eze 20:31 (VCG-02): persistent self-defilement closes divine accessibility; (2) corporate moral blindness to the condition — Jer 2:23 (VCG-02): "I am not unclean" — the self-deceptive claim; (3) land rendered inhabitable — Mic 2:10 (VCG-04): "no place to rest, because of uncleanness"; (4) sacred space desecrated and eventually destroyed — Psa 79:1 (VCG-03): temple defiled and Jerusalem ruined; (5) the corporate name becoming a byword of defilement — Eze 22:5 (VCG-05): "your name is defiled"; (6) social expulsion from the covenant community and from the land (Lam 4:15, VCG-05; Hos 9:3, VCG-05: "they shall eat unclean food in Assyria").

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Sustained possession establishes: (1) Total will-bondage without moral guilt — the person cannot break free (Luk 8:29 — breaking bonds yet "driven by the demon"); the will is externally overridden, not internally corrupted. (2) Communicative isolation — Mar 9:25 (VCG-01): "mute and deaf spirit" — sustained suppression of the communicative faculties enabling relationship with God and others. (3) Social-communal severance — Mar 5:2 (VCG-01): dwelling "among the tombs" in radical exclusion. (4) Bodily subjugation — the body becomes the instrument of the spirit's violent self-expression (convulsions — Luk 9:42; breaking chains — Luk 8:29; driven into the desert — Luk 8:29).

---

##### T1.6.3 — Does the sustained effect differ from the immediate response — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes. The immediate response is episodic — conscience awakening at a specific incurred defilement (Lev 5:2-3), grief at a specific exclusion (Num 9:7). The sustained effect is formational — the categorical system, repeated across a lifetime of observance, shapes the inner person into a person with a particular kind of conscience: one that is alive to the sacred/common boundary, watchful over bodily life, and oriented toward remedy. The difference is between the moment of defilement-recognition (immediate) and the character formed by years of managing the clean/unclean system (sustained). The sustained formation is what Lev 11:47 names explicitly: the purpose of all purity laws is "to make a distinction between the unclean and the clean" — a cultivated capacity, not a one-time response.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes, significantly. The immediate response (at the point of recognition — Isa 6:5: "woe is me!") is distress and awareness. The sustained effect (Rom 1:24 → Eph 4:19 trajectory) is the progressive elimination of that capacity for distress through the silencing of conscience. The immediate response requires a conscience that can still register the condition; the sustained effect produces a conscience that can no longer register it (callousness). This reveals a critical feature of the characteristic: the longer the condition persists without resolution, the more its own persistence suppresses the capacity for the immediate response that could initiate resolution. The sustained effect is thus increasingly self-reinforcing: moral-inner defilement suppresses the faculty (conscience) whose activation would begin the exit from defilement.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes. The immediate response varies from denial (Jer 2:23) to simmering grief (Gen 34:5) to jealousy (Num 5:14). The sustained effect is a comprehensive corporate deterioration: self-deception solidifying, divine access closing, land rendered uninhabitable, sanctuary destroyed, name defiled, community expelled. The sustained effect is thus more comprehensive and structurally damaging than any immediate response — it shows the characteristic as accumulating over time across all the relational and spatial domains the community inhabits, culminating in the exile and divine abandonment evidenced in the VCG-05 corpus.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes. The immediate event is the seizure — sudden and violent (Luk 9:42: "the demon threw him to the ground and convulsed him"). The sustained effect is domination that becomes a settled condition: Luk 8:29 — "many a time it had seized him" and he was kept in chains; Mar 5:2 — dwelling among the tombs. The immediate is episodic; the sustained is existential. The immediate response (observers' amazement, divine command) addresses the acute manifestation; the sustained condition requires the comprehensive restoration named at Luk 6:18 (cured) and Luk 9:42 (healed and returned to father).

---

#### T1.7 — Conditions of Reception

##### T1.7.1 — What inner conditions or orientations enable genuine reception of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

"Reception" is an unusual frame for a defilement-state; the characteristic is typically incurred rather than received. But if the question is read as: what inner conditions enable the person to recognise, respond to, and resolve the defilement appropriately — the evidence is clear. Three inner conditions enable the full reception of the characteristic's normative function: (1) conscience-alertness: the capacity to recognise when guilt surfaces (Lev 5:2-3, M10c-A-VCG-01 — the person who "comes to know it" and responds); (2) will-alignment with the sacral order: willingness to pursue remedy through appointed means (washing, waiting, examination, water of impurity); and (3) formed discernment: the cultivated ability to distinguish clean from unclean (Lev 10:10, 11:47, M10c-B-VCG-01), which enables one to recognise the defilement-state correctly when it is incurred.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Three enabling inner conditions are evidenced. (1) Unchecked desire: Rom 1:24 (VCG-02) — impurity arises from "lusts of their hearts" that have been given rein through the prior rejection of God. The enabling condition is desire without governance. (2) Silenced or weak conscience: Eph 4:19 (VCG-02) — callousness precedes the giving over to impurity; 1Cor 8:7 (VCG-03) — the conscience is weak and can be defiled when the person acts against it without genuine conviction. The enabling condition is a conscience that cannot hold the person to moral standards. (3) Former association with idols or morally corrupted environments: 1Cor 8:7 (VCG-03) — "through former association with idols, eat food as really offered to an idol" — the context of formation shapes susceptibility to defilement of conscience. Association with what defiles enables defilement.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Three enabling inner conditions are evidenced. (1) Sustained unfaithfulness of the corporate will: 2Ch 36:14 (VCG-03) — "exceedingly unfaithful, following all the abominations of the nations" — habitual corporate unfaithfulness is the primary enabling condition. (2) Desire-driven idolatrous lust: Eze 23:7 (VCG-02) — "she defiled herself with all the idols of everyone after whom she lusted" — unchecked corporate desire for what lies outside the covenant is the engine. (3) Deliberate will-act of desecration: Jer 7:30 (VCG-03) — the sons of Judah "set their detestable things in the house that is called by my name, to defile it" — the will's deliberate choice to install what defiles in the sacred space. The enabling condition is thus the corporate will turned away from God and toward idolatrous attachment, desire, and deliberate desecration.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The 21-verse corpus does not evidence specific inner conditions in the affected person that enable reception. The characteristic is imposed externally by the spirit's own agency without requiring a cooperating inner condition. Possessed persons include a child (Mar 7:25, Luk 9:42), an unnamed man in a synagogue (Mar 1:23), and a man among tombs (Mar 5:2) — no common inner enabling conditions are identified. This is analytically significant: the absence of inner-enabling conditions distinguishes Characteristic 4 structurally from Characteristics 2 and 3.

---

##### T1.7.2 — What inner conditions block, distort, or prevent reception?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Two blocking conditions are directly evidenced. First, ignorance: Lev 5:2-3 (M10c-A-VCG-01) shows defilement preceding awareness — the person is defiled before they know it. Ignorance does not prevent the condition but prevents the appropriate response. Second, willful refusal: Num 19:20 (M10c-A-VCG-07) — the man who is unclean and "does not cleanse himself" is cut off. The will's deliberate choice not to engage the appointed remedy is the primary blocking condition named in the evidence. A third distortion is evidenced in the NT: Peter's categorical conviction (M10c-B-VCG-05, Act 10:14) initially blocks the divine revision of the clean/unclean category — a formed conscience can become an inner resistance to new divine speech.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Two blocking conditions are directly evidenced. (1) A strong/formed conscience: 1Cor 8:7 (VCG-03) — those with "knowledge" (genuine moral conviction) eat without defiling their conscience, because the conviction is genuine and the conscience is not overridden. (2) Active consecration and separation: 2Cor 6:17 (VCG-03) — "go out from their midst, and be separate from them... touch no unclean thing; then I will welcome you" — active separation from defiling environments and influences is the primary blocking condition; the external act of separation protects the inner person from the condition's reception. Isa 52:11 (VCG-03): "purify yourselves, you who bear the vessels of the Lord" — active self-purification is a blocking condition against the characteristic's return.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Three blocking conditions are evidenced. (1) Consecrated separation — the Nazirite's commitment (Num 6:7, VCG-05): "not even for his father or for his mother... shall he make himself unclean, because his separation to God is on his head" — the inner dedication to God overrides even natural relational impulse, preventing the defilement. (2) Active covenantal fidelity: Eze 18:6 (VCG-01): "does not defile his neighbor's wife" — the righteous man's will consistently refusing sexual defilement across generations (18:6, 18:15) is the blocking orientation. (3) Priestly discernment and institutional guardianship: 2Ch 23:19 (the Characteristic 1 register but governing the same principle) and Eze 44:23 (VCG-05): "they shall teach my people the difference between the holy and the common, and show them how to distinguish between the unclean and the clean" — instruction in the clean/unclean distinction is a blocking condition at the institutional level.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The 21-verse corpus does not evidence specific inner conditions in the potential recipient that block the characteristic. The evidence focuses on the authoritative power that removes it (divine command — Mar 5:8, Mar 9:25) rather than on inner conditions that prevent its arrival. The VCG-03 authority-commissioning register names granted authority as the means of opposition (Mat 10:1, Mar 6:7), but this is external authoritative power against the agent, not inner enabling in the potential recipient.

---

##### T1.7.3 — What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic but does not receive it?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The person who is in the defilement-state but does not respond appropriately is characterised by two inner conditions. If the failure is ignorance, the person remains in an unresolved defilement — the guilt is real but inactive; the state persists (Num 19:13 — "his uncleanness is still on him"). If the failure is willful non-cleansing, the person is in a condition of deliberate sacral defection: Num 19:20 names this as "defiling the sanctuary of the Lord" — the will's refusal of remedy becomes an act of corporate sacral harm. The inner state of the willful refuser is one of hardened will operating against the sacral order, which the evidence treats as the most serious form of the characteristic's failure mode.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The person who does not receive the moral-inner defilement-state is characterised in VCG-05 (Rev 3:4, Rev 14:4, Isa 35:8). Rev 3:4 (VCG-05): "people who have not soiled their garments... they are worthy" — their inner state is one of maintained integrity; the moral condition is uncompromised. Rev 14:4 (VCG-05): "they have not defiled themselves... they follow the Lamb wherever he goes" — their inner state is one of total consecration to Christ, actively oriented toward the Lamb rather than toward corrupted desire. The non-reception state is not passive neutrality but an active positive orientation: consecrated following, maintained integrity, worthiness for divine fellowship.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The person who does not receive the corporate/covenantal defilement-state is characterised in the positive-inverse at multiple points. Eze 4:14 (VCG-05): the prophet's declaration — "I have never defiled myself. From my youth up till now I have never eaten what died of itself" — shows the inner state as lifelong personal maintenance of covenantal integrity; the conscience actively defending the inner person's maintained purity. Eze 18:6/15 (VCG-01): the righteous man "does not defile his neighbor's wife" across generations — the inner state is will's consistent covenantal fidelity. The positive-inverse state is thus: a will committed to covenantal faithfulness, a conscience that actively defends maintained purity, and an institutional vocation of teaching the clean/unclean distinction.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The 21-verse corpus does not describe a person whom the spirits attempt to possess but fail to. The structural resistance is authoritative divine power (VCG-03), not inner-being conditioning in the potential recipient. The evidence suggests that the characteristic's reception is entirely determined by the spirit's agency rather than by the recipient's inner resistance.

---

#### T1.8 — Dimension Classification

##### T1.8.1 — What is the primary inner-being dimension of this characteristic from the programme's dimension vocabulary?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The primary dimension of Characteristic 1 (Ritual defilement-state) is the **condition** dimension — specifically, a sacrally and legally defined condition of the person. The characteristic is a state, not an act or disposition. Its primary vocabulary (H2931 ta.me adjective: "unclean" as a descriptor of the person's condition; Lev 13:46: "he is unclean") is stative. The condition is the inner-being reality that the entire characteristic's system of acquisition, management, and resolution is ordered around.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The primary dimension is condition — a morally corrupted state of the whole inner person. Like Characteristic 1, the vocabulary is predominantly stative: akatharsia (impurity — noun/state), molusmos (defilement — noun/state), H2931 ta.me adj (unclean — adjective/state). The condition pervades the inner person: it is not an act performed but a state that the person is in, which then generates acts (Gal 5:19 — "works of the flesh"; 2Cor 12:21 — impurity "practiced").

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The primary dimension is condition — a state of corporate contamination of the sacred relational order that the community inhabits. The vocabulary is predominantly stative and result-focused: the land is "defiled" (Jer 2:7, Eze 36:17/18), the sanctuary is "defiled" (Eze 5:11), the name is "defiled" (Eze 43:7/8), the community is "defiled" (Hos 5:3: "Israel is defiled"; Hos 6:10: "Israel is defiled"). The condition is the endpoint of acts of unfaithfulness; the characteristic names the resulting state rather than the generating acts.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The primary dimension is condition — a state of spiritual domination and defilement imposed on the person from without. The language throughout VCG-01 is stative: "a man with an unclean spirit" (Mar 1:23 — present condition); "a man who had an unclean spirit" (Mar 5:2 — echōn — having, as a present condition); "those afflicted with unclean spirits" (Act 5:16 — ochloumenoi — being afflicted, present participle of sustained condition). The condition is what the person is in; it was not produced by their action and is not a faculty they exercise.

---

##### T1.8.2 — What evidence from the verse evidence supports this classification?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The stative character is pervasive across all 133 verses. The most direct evidence: Num 19:13 (M10c-A-VCG-07) — "his uncleanness is still on him" — names the condition as a persisting, clinging state. Lev 13:46 (M10c-B-VCG-03) — "he shall remain unclean as long as he has the disease" — frames uncleanness as a duration-defined condition. Lev 5:2-3 (M10c-A-VCG-01) — "he has become unclean" — marks the transition into the condition. The resolution formulas ("shall be unclean until the evening / then it shall be clean") confirm the condition as bounded in time. The priestly verdict system (M10c-B-VCG-02) confirms the condition as established by authoritative declaration. Across all sub-registers, the characteristic is consistently a condition the person is in.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Supporting evidence for the condition classification: Rom 6:19 (VCG-02) — "you once presented your members as slaves to impurity" — the slavery metaphor names the condition as a state the person was in, not an act they performed; Eph 4:19 (VCG-02) — "given themselves up to... every kind of impurity" — the giving-over is the event; the impurity is the condition entered; Job 14:4 (VCG-01) — "who can bring a clean thing out of an unclean?" — the unclean is a state of being, not an activity; 2Cor 7:1 (VCG-03) — "defilement of body and spirit" — the defilement is described as inhabiting the body and spirit, confirming stative nature.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The stative character is confirmed by the consistent use of H2930A and H2931 as result-descriptors rather than process-descriptors. Psa 106:39 (VCG-02): "thus they became unclean by their acts" — the becoming-unclean is the result-state produced by prior acts. Eze 22:4 (VCG-02): "you have become guilty... and defiled by the idols that you have made" — defilement is the arrived-at condition following the acts. Hos 5:3 (VCG-02): "Israel is defiled" — the present stative condition is the summary statement. Lam 1:17 (VCG-05): "Jerusalem has become a filthy thing among them" — the city's current condition is the result of the corporate defilement process.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Stative character is consistently evidenced: Mar 1:23 — "a man with an unclean spirit"; Mar 5:2 — "a man with an unclean spirit"; Mar 5:8 — the command "come out of the man" presupposes the spirit is currently within (stative presence); Luk 8:29 — "many a time it had seized him" — the seizures produce a persisting condition of domination. Act 5:16 — "those afflicted with unclean spirits" — the affliction is an ongoing state. The characteristic's resolution requires authoritative external intervention (divine command), not the person's own volitional response — confirming the condition classification.

---

##### T1.8.3 — Does this characteristic carry secondary dimensions — and if so, what are they, and do they compete with the primary classification?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes, two secondary dimensions are evidenced. First, a **volitional** secondary dimension: within the condition, the will is engaged at the perimeter — one may deliberately avoid defiling contact (Lev 11:43-44, M10c-A-VCG-04), seek remedy or refuse it (Num 19:20), guard the clean/unclean boundary through active discernment (Lev 10:10, 20:25, M10c-B-VCG-01). The will does not constitute the condition but actively shapes the person's relationship to it. Second, a **social-relational** secondary dimension: the characteristic is inherently communal — exclusion from camp and worship (Num 5:2, Lev 13:46), public self-declaration (Lev 13:45), the duty not to transmit (Lev 15:11), institutional gatekeeping (2Ch 23:19, M10c-B-VCG-03) all show the characteristic as a condition with built-in social structure. Neither secondary dimension competes with the primary condition classification — they describe what the condition activates, not what the condition is.

---

## T2 — Constitutional Location (31 prompts)

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes, three secondary dimensions. (1) Dispositional: Eph 4:19 (VCG-02) — "greedy to practice every kind of impurity" — the characteristic includes a habitual appetite, a disposition of the will oriented toward corruption. (2) Volitional: the molunō verb (1Cor 8:7, VCG-03 — "conscience is defiled"; Rev 3:4, VCG-05 — "not soiled their garments") names the act by which the condition is incurred or avoided — there is a volitional event at the characteristic's acquisition. (3) Constitutional: Job 14:4 (VCG-01) — the unclean as the constitutional origin point — this is not a condition entered through specific choices but an inherited constitutional reality. None of these secondary dimensions competes with the primary condition classification — they describe how the condition is acquired (volitional), how it operates once entrenched (dispositional), and how deep it runs (constitutional).

## T2 — Constitutional Location (31 prompts)

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes, two secondary dimensions. (1) Volitional: the defilement-state is generated by volitional acts — Eze 20:7 (VCG-02): "do not defile yourselves with the idols of Egypt" — the imperative presupposes a volitional capacity to choose or refuse; Eze 23:7 (VCG-02): "she defiled herself with all the idols of everyone after whom she lusted" — the act of defiling is volitional self-direction. (2) Social-covenantal: the defilement-state inherently affects and involves the covenant community and its relational environment — the land, sanctuary, name, and God himself are all implicated in the characteristic's operation. Neither secondary dimension competes with the primary condition classification; they describe how the condition is generated (volitional) and in what relational domain it operates (social-covenantal).

## T2 — Constitutional Location (31 prompts)

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes, two secondary dimensions. (1) Affliction/suffering: Act 5:16 names those with unclean spirits alongside the "sick"; Luk 6:18 — "cured" — the healing terminology frames the condition as an affliction to be addressed. (2) Adversarial spiritual engagement: the spirits resist expulsion (Act 8:7 — crying out; Mat 12:43 — seeking re-entry), and authority is required to overcome them (Mat 10:1). The adversarial dimension is secondary to the condition dimension but essential for understanding how the condition is both produced and resolved.
