## T2 — Constitutional Location (31 prompts)

---

### T2

#### T2.1 — Spirit-Level Location

##### T2.1.1 — Is this characteristic explicitly located at the spirit level in the verse evidence?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

The 133-verse corpus does not explicitly locate the ritual defilement-state at the spirit level. No verse in M10c-A or M10c-B directly names the spirit (ruach) as the site of ritual defilement. The characteristic is primarily a condition of the person as embodied, sacral participant, not one that is explicitly named as a spirit-level phenomenon in the ritual register.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes. 2Cor 7:1 (M10c-C-VCG-03) is the most explicit: "let us cleanse ourselves from every defilement of body and spirit" — the defilement is explicitly located in both body and spirit (pneuma). The spirit-level location is named directly. This is the locus classicus of Characteristic 2's spirit-level reach.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (S)

The 83-verse corpus does not explicitly name the spirit (ruach) as the locus of corporate/covenantal defilement. The characteristic is located at the level of the corporate will, the community's covenantal conduct, and the sacred physical environment (land, sanctuary, name). No verse in §3 names defilement "of the spirit" in the Characteristic 3 register.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes. The characteristic is constituted by the interaction between an external pneuma and the human person. Luk 4:33 (VCG-01): "the spirit of an unclean demon" — the entity is a spirit; its presence in the person constitutes the defilement-state. Mar 9:25 (VCG-01): "you mute and deaf spirit, I command you, come out of him" — the command is addressed to the spirit as the entity inhabiting the person; the spirit's presence and expulsion define the condition. The external spirit inhabits and dominates the person at their deepest constitutional level.

---

##### T2.1.2 — Does the evidence indicate that this characteristic originates in or is primarily a spirit-level phenomenon?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

No. The origin of the ritual defilement-state is consistently bodily — through physical contact (M10c-A), through bodily condition assessed by examination (M10c-B). The spirit-level register appears in Characteristic 2 (moral-inner defilement: 2Cor 7:1 names "defilement of body and spirit") but that verse is in M10c-C, outside Characteristic 1's corpus. Within the 133 verses, the characteristic is primarily a bodily-mechanism or verdict-mechanism condition, not a spirit-origin phenomenon.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The evidence shows the characteristic inhabiting the spirit level but not originating there. The origin evidence (T2.9 below) points to desire and habitual sin as the generative forces (Rom 1:24, Eph 4:19, VCG-02), which operate at the soul level of will and desire. The characteristic penetrates to the spirit level (2Cor 7:1) — it is the condition that has seeped down from the soul's volitional and desiderative functions into the deepest constitutional level. Origin is at the soul-desire/will level; penetration reaches to the spirit level.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (S)

Not evidenced at the spirit level. The origin evidence (T2.9 below) points to the community's volitional and covenantal defection as the generating force — this is a soul-level (will, desire, heart allegiance) phenomenon that produces consequences at the level of sacred spaces and relationships. The spirit-level penetration evidenced in Characteristic 2 (2Cor 7:1 — "defilement of body and spirit") is not paralleled in Characteristic 3's Hebrew corpus.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes, uniquely within the M10c cluster. The characteristic originates from an external spirit and its primary site of operation is the person's spirit-level constitution. The unclean spirit enters and operates at the spirit level, which is why the domination is total: Luk 8:29 (VCG-01) — the spirit's control overrides all bodily resistance (breaking chains), not because it acts at the bodily level first but because it controls the person at the deepest constitutional level. This distinguishes Characteristic 4 from Characteristic 2, where the defilement penetrates to the spirit level from the soul's desire-level inward; Characteristic 4 arrives at the spirit level directly from an external spiritual agent.

---

##### T2.1.3 — What does spirit-level location reveal about the nature and depth of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

Because spirit-level location is not evidenced in Characteristic 1's 133 verses, this question cannot be answered from the evidence. The absence is informative: the ritual defilement-state operates at the level of the embodied person in sacral community, not at the deepest constitutional level of spirit-to-spirit engagement with God. This distinguishes it from the moral-inner defilement register, which does penetrate to the spirit level (Characteristic 2).

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The spirit-level location at 2Cor 7:1 (VCG-03) reveals the characteristic as reaching the deepest constitutional level of the human person — defilement is not merely a surface moral condition or a habituation of the will, but a condition that has penetrated into the spirit itself, the deepest point of creaturely existence before God. This distinguishes Characteristic 2 fundamentally from Characteristic 1 (Ritual defilement-state), which operates at the bodily-mechanism and social-sacral level but is not explicitly located in the spirit. The spirit-level location of Characteristic 2 reveals it as the most constitutionally deep form of defilement in the M10c cluster: it reaches where no bodily washing can resolve it, requiring a different kind of cleansing.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (S)

The silence on spirit-level location reveals a distinctive feature of Characteristic 3 compared to Characteristic 2: Characteristic 3 is the defilement-state as it operates in the covenantal-communal domain (land, sanctuary, name, covenant relationship) rather than in the deepest personal constitutional domain. It is a condition of the community's shared moral-covenantal existence rather than a condition penetrating to the deepest individual constitutional level.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The spirit-level operation reveals Characteristic 4 as the deepest form of defilement in the M10c cluster — deeper even than Characteristic 2 (which reaches the spirit level but originates at the soul level). Characteristic 4 arrives at the spirit level directly, bypassing the soul's volitional engagement entirely. This explains why the characteristic produces the most comprehensive domination (Luk 8:29 — chains fail) and why divine authority alone (not human will, not human restraint) is the effective remedy — only a power superior to the spirit can address the condition at the constitutional level where the spirit operates.

---

##### T2.1.4 — If the evidence is silent on spirit-level location, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

The evidence is silent on spirit-level location. No verse in the 133-verse corpus explicitly places the ritual defilement-state at the spirit level.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The evidence is not silent. 2Cor 7:1 explicitly locates defilement at the spirit level. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (S)

The evidence is silent on spirit-level location within the 83-verse corpus. No verse in §3 locates the corporate/covenantal defilement-state at the spirit level.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The evidence is not silent. The characteristic is constituted by the operation of an external pneuma at the person's spirit level. Not applicable.

---

#### T2.2 — Soul-Level Location

##### T2.2.1 — Is this characteristic identified in the verse evidence as a soul-level phenomenon?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The 133-verse corpus does not use "soul" (nephesh) language directly, but the condition bears on what the programme would locate as soul-level realities: conscience, will, affect, and relational capacity. Num 9:7 (M10c-A-VCG-07) — the men's grief at exclusion ("why are we kept from bringing the Lord's offering?") — shows a soul-level affective and volitional response to the condition. Lev 5:2-3 (M10c-A-VCG-01) — "he realises his guilt" — shows conscience (a soul-level faculty) activated by the condition. The condition itself is carried by the embodied person but its impact registers in the soul-level faculties. Direct nephesh language is not found in the 133-verse corpus for this characteristic in this register.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes. The soul-level faculties are the primary terrain of Characteristic 2. The evidence engages: will (Rom 6:19 — "slaves to impurity" — the will bound; Eph 4:19 — will surrendering to sensuality), desire (Rom 1:24 — "lusts of their hearts"), conscience (1Cor 8:7 — "conscience is defiled"), and heart (Rom 1:24 — "hearts"; Eph 5:5 — heart allegiance disorder as idolatry). The soul-level is the primary operational domain of the characteristic, engaging all its major sub-faculties.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes, at the level of the corporate will and heart. Eze 20:43 (VCG-02): "there you shall remember your ways and all your deeds with which you have defiled yourselves, and you shall loathe yourselves for all the evils that you have committed" — the loathing and remembering are soul-level responses to recognising the defilement. Eze 14:11 (VCG-02): "the house of Israel may no more go astray from me, nor defile themselves anymore with all their transgressions" — the corporate straying is a soul-level act of will (going astray from God). The will, desire, and corporate heart are the primary soul-level faculties through which the characteristic operates.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes, through soul-level faculty suppression. Mar 9:25 (VCG-01): the spirit is "mute and deaf" — it suppresses speech and hearing, which are soul-level communicative capacities. The will is overridden (Luk 8:29 — "driven by the demon") — the will is a primary soul-level faculty. The characteristic thus operates at the soul level by suppressing the soul's faculties through the external spirit's spirit-level domination.

---

##### T2.2.2 — What does soul-level location reveal about this characteristic's place in the innermost personal experience?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The evidence suggests the ritual defilement-state is not primarily a soul-origin phenomenon but it impinges on soul-level experience through its consequences — exclusion, guilt-awakening, grief. The soul-level impact is secondary to the body-mechanism of acquisition: the condition arrives through the body and is felt by the soul. This reveals the characteristic's place as a bridge condition — it is constitutionally bodily in origin but cannot remain only bodily; it activates conscience, will, and affect, drawing the whole inner person into its management and resolution.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Soul-level location reveals the characteristic as operating in the domain of the person's most active inner life — their willing, desiring, evaluating, and feeling. The soul is where the person engages with their world and with God; the presence of the defilement-state at the soul level means that the primary instruments of engagement (will, desire, conscience, heart) are compromised. This makes the characteristic a condition that distorts the inner-person's most active and engaged dimensions — not a passive background condition but one that actively misdirects the person's inner dynamics.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The soul-level location reveals the characteristic as rooted in the community's deepest volitional and desiderative life — the corporate "heart" that has turned away from God (Eze 23:7 — "all the idols of everyone after whom she lusted"; Eze 20:31 — "you defile yourselves with all your idols to this day") generates the contamination that extends to the sacred environment. The soul-level generating force is communal — not only individual will but the collective will of the house of Israel, the city, the leadership — revealing the characteristic as operating at the level of shared inner orientation.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The soul-level location reveals that the characteristic's domination extends from the spirit level downward through the soul-level faculties to the body. The spirit inhabits and controls at the spirit level; the soul's faculties are suppressed (will overridden, speech and hearing suppressed); the body is subject to violent external control (convulsions — Mar 1:26, Luk 9:42; breaking chains — Luk 8:29). This downward cascade reveals the constitutional comprehensiveness of the characteristic: it reaches and dominates every layer of the human person.

---

##### T2.2.3 — If the evidence is silent on soul-level location, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The evidence is not fully silent — soul-level faculties (conscience, affect, will) are engaged by the characteristic, though the characteristic is not explicitly named as a soul-condition. The distinction is between the condition (bodily-mechanism or verdict-mechanism) and its soul-level impact (conscience, grief, will-response).

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The evidence is not silent. Soul-level faculties are explicitly engaged across VCG-02, -03, and -04. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The evidence is not silent. Soul-level faculties (will, desire, heart allegiance) are engaged as the generating forces across VCG-02 and VCG-01. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Not silent. Soul-level faculty engagement (will, speech/hearing) is evidenced. Not applicable.

---

#### T2.3 — Heart

##### T2.3.1 — Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the heart?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

The 133-verse corpus does not locate the ritual defilement-state in the heart. Heart language (lev, lebab) does not appear in connection with the characteristic in these verses. The characteristic's primary location is the body (as the locus of acquisition and contamination) and the sacral community (as the relational structure affected). Heart-level engagement appears in Characteristics 2 and 3 (moral-inner defilement, corporate-covenantal defilement) but not in Characteristic 1's ritual register.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes. Rom 1:24 (VCG-02): "in the lusts of their hearts to impurity" — the heart is named as the seat from which the lusts arise that lead to the impurity condition; the defilement is described as originating in heart-level desire. Mat 23:27 (VCG-04): the hypocrites are described as "within full of dead people's bones and all uncleanness" — the interior (the inner person, encompassing the heart) is the site of the defilement.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Implicitly rather than explicitly. The heart (lev/lebab) is not named by that term in the 83-verse corpus, but the heart's allegiance-forming function is what drives the characteristic. Eze 23:7 (VCG-02): "she defiled herself with all the idols of everyone after whom she lusted" — lust/longing as the heart-level allegiance-direction toward idols. Eze 22:3 (VCG-02): "a city that makes idols to defile herself" — the corporate will's purposeful idolatrous devotion is a heart-allegiance reality. The Ezekiel oracle corpus throughout VCG-02 characterises the community as having turned their heart-allegiance toward idols — the defilement is the consequence of this allegiance disorder.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The 21-verse corpus does not explicitly name the heart (kardia) as the site of the characteristic. The characteristic's external-agency mechanism bypasses the heart's allegiance and desire functions — it is not generated from the heart's interior but from an external spiritual invasion.

---

##### T2.3.2 — What does the heart-location reveal — what aspect of the heart's integrating function (knowing, willing, feeling, moral awareness) does this characteristic engage?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

Not evidenced from the 133-verse corpus. See T2.3.3.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The heart-location engages the heart's allegiance-forming function — the faculty by which the heart orients itself toward or away from God. Rom 1:24 (VCG-02): the heart's lusts are the engine of defilement; the heart has oriented its desires toward corrupted objects. Eph 5:5 (VCG-04): the impure person is equated with an idolater — "covetous (that is, an idolater)" — the heart's allegiance has been displaced from God to corrupt desire. The heart-location reveals the characteristic as a condition of allegiance disorder: the integrating function of the heart, which should orient all inner faculties toward God, has been redirected toward desire-objects that defile.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The implicit heart-allegiance dimension reveals that the corporate/covenantal defilement-state originates in the community's disordered allegiance — the heart that should be directed toward God (covenant fidelity) has been directed toward idols (Eze 20:7/18/30/31 — the repeated commands not to defile with Egypt's idols and fathers' idols, which the community persistently ignores). This reveals the characteristic as flowing from the heart's most fundamental function: the setting of ultimate loyalty and allegiance. When corporate loyalty is disordered, the defilement extends to the entire sacred relational environment.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

Not evidenced. See T2.3.3.

---

##### T2.3.3 — If the evidence is silent on heart-location, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

The evidence is silent on heart-location for Characteristic 1's ritual defilement-state. No verse in the 133-verse corpus explicitly places the defilement-state in the heart. Heart-engagement with defilement is a feature of Characteristic 2 (M10c-C corpus) and Characteristic 3 (M10c-D corpus), not Characteristic 1.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The evidence is not silent. Heart-location is directly evidenced at Rom 1:24 and Mat 23:27. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The evidence is not explicitly silent but uses implicit allegiance-language rather than explicit heart-terminology. The heart-allegiance dimension is present through the corporate desire and loyalty language throughout VCG-02. Not fully silent.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The evidence is silent on heart-location. This silence confirms the characteristic as fundamentally different from Characteristics 2 and 3 in its mechanism: those characteristics originate in heart-allegiance disorder; Characteristic 4 bypasses the heart entirely through external invasion.

---

#### T2.4 — Mind

##### T2.4.1 — Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the mind?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The verse evidence does not use mind (sekhel, nous) language directly, but the discernment register of M10c-B-VCG-01 is a mind-adjacent phenomenon. Lev 10:10 requires "active inner discernment that distinguishes the unclean from the clean" — a perceptual and cognitive faculty. Lev 11:47 names the purpose of all purity laws as cultivating this capacity. The NT categorical conscience (Act 10:14, M10c-B-VCG-05) shows the mind-level conviction that the clean/unclean categories have formed — a structured cognitive-moral framework operating in Peter's inner judgment. The characteristic engages the mind-adjacent faculty of discernment, though the defilement-state itself is not explicitly located in the mind.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes, with a cross-reference internal to the characteristic's VCG-03 network. Tit 1:15 is referenced in the structural input's VCG-03 description: "to the defiled and unbelieving, nothing is pure; both their minds and their consciences are defiled" — the mind (nous) is explicitly named as a site of defilement in the moral-inner register. This verse is cross-referenced in the characteristic's definition but its vc_id does not appear in §3 — however the VCG-03 description includes it. Within §3 directly, the most mind-adjacent evidence is 1Cor 8:7 (VCG-03): conscience as the cognitive-moral faculty that is defiled; and 2Pe 2:10 (VCG-03): "bold and willful" — the will-and-mind complex in defiant posture.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes, through two evidenced engagements. (1) The cognitive faculty of discernment: Eze 22:26 (VCG-05) — "they have made no distinction between the holy and the common, neither have they taught the difference between the unclean and the clean" — the priests' failure is a failure of the cognitive-discernment faculty; the collapse of moral-spiritual discernment is both a cause and a symptom of the corporate defilement-state. (2) Self-deceptive cognition: Jer 2:23 (VCG-02) — "how can you say, 'I am not unclean, I have not gone after the Baals'?" — the corporate community's cognitive self-assessment is distorted; they cannot correctly cognise their own defilement-state.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The 21-verse corpus does not explicitly name the mind (nous) as the site of the characteristic. The suppression of speech and hearing (Mar 9:25) impairs the communicative faculties adjacent to the mind, but the mind itself is not named as the site of inhabitation or suppression.

---

##### T2.4.2 — What does mind-location reveal — what aspect of the mind's function (thought, discernment, understanding) does this characteristic engage?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The relevant mind-function is discernment — the capacity to distinguish, categorise, and apply the clean/unclean boundary correctly. The purity laws function as a training curriculum for this faculty: sustained engagement with the clean/unclean distinction in its many sub-categories (which animals are clean, what transmission patterns produce defilement, which conditions are permanent and which temporary) forms the person in a structured pattern of categorical perception. Peter's Act 10:14 conviction ("I have never eaten anything that is common or unclean") shows this categorical knowledge as fully internalised — not a rule consulted but a deeply embedded inner judgment.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The mind-location (via Tit 1:15 reference in VCG-03) reveals the characteristic as engaging the mind's moral-assessment function: the defiled mind cannot correctly assess what is pure, because the standard for moral evaluation has itself been compromised. The defiled mind produces defiled moral judgement. This is the deepest cognitive impact of the characteristic: it does not merely distort behaviour but corrupts the inner instrument of moral perception and judgement. Within §3, 1Cor 8:7 (VCG-03) shows the conscience (the mind's moral-witness function) as the locus of defilement from acting against inner conviction.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The mind-location reveals that the corporate/covenantal defilement-state both requires cognitive formation (the clean/unclean distinction must be taught — Eze 44:23 VCG-05, Eze 22:26 VCG-05) and corrupts cognitive self-assessment (Jer 2:23 — the community cannot see its own condition). The priestly failure at Eze 22:26 is cognitive: the priests who should maintain and teach the clean/unclean framework have failed in their cognitive-formative role. This reveals the characteristic as inhabiting the cognitive domain at two levels: the knowledge-formation dimension (teaching discernment) and the self-knowledge dimension (recognising one's own condition).

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

Not evidenced. See T2.4.3.

---

##### T2.4.3 — If the evidence is silent on mind-location, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Evidence is present; not silent. The discernment register (M10c-B-VCG-01) engages the mind-adjacent capacity for categorical distinction.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The evidence is not silent — mind-location is evidenced through the VCG-03 network (Tit 1:15 cross-reference) and the conscience register at 1Cor 8:7. Not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The evidence is not silent. Mind-level engagement is evidenced through priestly discernment failure (Eze 22:26) and self-deceptive cognition (Jer 2:23). Not applicable.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The evidence is silent on explicit mind-location. The characteristic's domination is whole-person and constitutional rather than targeting the cognitive domain specifically.

---

#### T2.5 — Other Soul Subsets

##### T2.5.1 — Does the verse evidence surface any soul-level location beyond heart and mind for this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes: the affective dimension. Num 9:7 (M10c-A-VCG-07) — the men's grief at exclusion from worship — shows affect (grief, desire for worship) as a soul-level response to the condition. The grief is specifically named: "why are we kept from bringing the Lord's offering?" — the grief of a worship desire blocked by the defilement-state. Lev 13:45 (M10c-B-VCG-03) — the public cry "Unclean, unclean" — shows the social-relational soul-dimension engaged: the declaration is simultaneously a ritual act and a social-relational act of self-naming before the community. The social exclusion of Lev 13:46 ("he shall live alone; his dwelling shall be outside the camp") shows the relational soul-dimension as the site of the condition's most sustained impact.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes: the will and desire are additional soul-level locations. Rom 6:19 (VCG-02): "slaves to impurity" — the will is specifically named as the faculty bound by the defilement-state; the person's volitional capacity is in bondage. Rom 1:24 (VCG-02): "lusts of their hearts" — desire (epithumia) as the soul-level faculty through which the characteristic operates. Eph 4:19 (VCG-02): "given themselves up to sensuality, greedy to practice every kind of impurity" — the volitional self-surrender and the appetitive desire are both named.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes: the memory faculty and the affect faculty. Memory: Eze 20:43 (VCG-02) — "there you shall remember your ways and all your deeds with which you have defiled yourselves" — the corporate memory of the defilement-state is the named inner mechanism of future repentance; memory is explicitly engaged as the faculty through which defilement becomes the generative force of self-loathing and moral grief. Affect: Gen 34:5 (VCG-01) — Jacob's "restrained, simmering awareness of wrong done" is an affective response; Num 5:14 — jealousy as the immediate affective inner response to suspected covenantal betrayal.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes: the will and the speech/hearing communicative-perceptive complex. Will: Luk 8:29 (VCG-01) — "driven by the demon into the desert" — the person's will is completely overridden; the spirit drives where the person's will would not go. Mar 9:25 (VCG-01): the spirit suppresses speech (a volitional-expressive faculty) and hearing (a perceptive faculty).

---

##### T2.5.2 — If so, what is that location, and what does it reveal?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The affective and social-relational dimensions are the other soul-level locations. Affect: the defilement-state activates grief at exclusion and desire for restored access (Num 9:7). Social-relational capacity: the characteristic structurally impairs the person's ability to participate in communal worship and communal life (Lev 13:46, Num 5:2, M10c-A-VCG-07 and M10c-B-VCG-03). This reveals that the characteristic is not only a condition of the body but a condition that restructures the person's social-relational standing within the covenant community.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Will and desire. The will's location reveals the characteristic as a condition that actively constrains freedom — it is not merely a passive colouring of the inner life but a bondage of the willing capacity (Rom 6:19: "slaves"). The desire-location (epithumia) reveals the characteristic as rooted in a specific distortion of the appetitive faculty: desire has been detached from its proper orientation toward God and redirected toward corrupting objects (Rom 1:24 — "lusts of their hearts to impurity"; Col 3:5, VCG-02 — "passion, evil desire, and covetousness").

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The memory location (Eze 20:43) reveals the characteristic's most distinctive inner-being contribution: corporate memory of defilement is the mechanism of repentance. Unlike Characteristic 2, where memory is present but ineffective in the hardened state (2Cor 12:21), Characteristic 3 envisions memory as the precisely appointed instrument of corporate moral transformation — the community's future self-loathing will be generated by the memory of its own defilement. This reveals the characteristic as having a built-in eschatological repentance function: the very condition of defilement, when remembered in the context of restoration, becomes the generative force of the community's humility before God.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The will-location and speech/hearing-location reveal the characteristic as targeting the specific soul-level faculties that enable the person's relationship with God (prayer/hearing divine speech) and with others (speech/hearing in community). The suppression of these faculties reveals the characteristic as attacking the person at precisely the soul-level points where their relational-covenantal existence is constituted.

---

##### T2.5.3 — If the evidence is silent, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Evidence is present; not silent. The affective and social-relational dimensions are evidenced at Num 9:7 and Lev 13:45-46.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Not silent. Will and desire are explicitly evidenced as soul-level locations beyond heart and mind. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Not silent. Memory and affect are both evidenced. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Not silent. Will and speech/hearing are evidenced as soul-level locations. Not applicable.

---

#### T2.6 — Body — Significance

##### T2.6.1 — Does the verse evidence link this characteristic to a specific body part?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes, several body-part linkages are explicit. Skin: the leprous-disease verdict system (M10c-B-VCG-02, Lev 13 corpus) is entirely skin-focused — the priest examines "the diseased area on the skin of his body" (Lev 13:3); the skin's surface is both the site of the condition and the medium of assessment. Head: Lev 13:44-45 (M10c-B-VCG-02/03) — disease on the head receives a specific verdict; the head is the locus of the public self-declaration. Mouth/saliva: Lev 15:8 (M10c-A-VCG-06) — spitting by the discharge-person defiles. Hand: Lev 15:11 (M10c-A-VCG-06) — the unwashed hand is the vector of defilement-transmission. Lips: implied in the self-declaration cry (Lev 13:45 — "cover his upper lip and cry out"). Genitals/bodily fluids: the entire discharge register (M10c-A-VCG-05 and -06) is anchored in bodily-fluid emission — menstrual blood, seminal fluid, abnormal discharge.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes. Isa 6:5 (VCG-01): "I am a man of unclean lips" — the lips are named as the bodily organ in which the inner moral defilement is expressed and perceived; the prophet's mouth/lips are the body part that articulates the inner condition. Rom 1:24 (VCG-02): "to the dishonoring of their bodies among themselves" — the body as a whole receives the consequence of the impurity, though no specific body part is named here beyond "bodies." 2Cor 7:1 (VCG-03): "defilement of body and spirit" — the body (soma) as a whole is named alongside the spirit as the constitutional locus of the defilement.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes. Num 5:27 (VCG-01): the ordeal water produces consequences in the body — "her womb shall swell, and her thigh shall fall away" — when defilement through broken covenant faith is real; the body is the site of the judicial consequence of the covenantal defilement. The womb and thigh (probably genitals/reproductive organs) are the specific body parts named as the site of the physical judgment. Eze 22:10 (VCG-01): men violating women "in their menstrual impurity" — the body's menstrual state defines the boundary being transgressed; the female body's specific physiological condition is the boundary marker.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes. (1) Speech organs: Mar 1:26 (VCG-02) — "crying out with a loud voice" — the spirit uses the person's voice; Mar 9:25 (VCG-01) — "mute and deaf spirit" — the mouth/voice is the specifically suppressed speech organ. (2) Body as a whole: Luk 8:29 (VCG-01) — "bound with chains and shackles, but he would break the bonds" — the body's limbs are the sites of both restraint and supernatural strength; Luk 9:42 (VCG-01) — "threw him to the ground and convulsed him" — the whole body is the instrument of the spirit's violent self-expression.

---

##### T2.6.2 — If so, what is Scripture doing by making that link — is it emphatic, functional, expressive, indicative, or mediating?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The body-part links serve distinct functions. The skin linkage (Lev 13 leprosy corpus) is diagnostic and indicative: the skin's condition is the external indicator of the defilement-state's presence and severity. The hand linkage (Lev 15:11) is functional: the unwashed hand is the transmission vector — washing the hand could prevent the transfer, making the hand's cleansing the moral act. The bodily-fluid linkages (Lev 15 discharge) are mediating: the fluid is the medium through which the defilement-state transmits from person to person and to objects. The head linkage (Lev 13:44-45) is both indicative (the disease location) and expressive (the self-declaration involves the whole visible head — "let the hair hang loose, cover the upper lip, cry out").

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The lips-link at Isa 6:5 (VCG-01) is expressive and indicative: the lips are the organ of confession, prophecy, and speech before God — naming them as unclean is both the prophet's self-recognition (expressive) and an indication that the defilement extends to his primary instrument of divine service (indicative). The body-link at Rom 1:24 (VCG-02) is consequential: the body receives the dishonour that results from the defilement-state; the body mediates the moral consequence outwardly. The body-link at 2Cor 7:1 (VCG-03) is constitutional: defilement of body and spirit together names the full extent of the condition — neither bodily nor spiritual is excluded; the link is comprehensive rather than specific.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The body-part links serve distinct functions. The womb/thigh link at Num 5:27 (VCG-01) is judicial-consequential: the specific body parts associated with reproduction and covenant-sexual integrity receive the physical consequence of covenantal infidelity — the defilement of a sexual covenant bond is judged in the bodily domain most directly associated with that bond. The menstrual-impurity link at Eze 22:10 (VCG-01) is boundary-indicative: the body's physiological state defines a relational-moral boundary whose transgression constitutes covenantal defilement.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The speech/mouth link (Mar 1:23, Mar 1:26, Mar 9:25) is functional and expressive: the spirit uses the person's voice as its instrument of declaration and protest; and the spirit suppresses speech to isolate the person from relational communication. The body-as-a-whole link (Luk 8:29 — breaking chains; Luk 9:42 — convulsions) is emphatic and indicative: the spirit's expression through the body demonstrates the power of the domination — the body is no longer the person's own instrument but the spirit's.

---

##### T2.6.3 — If no body-part link is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Body-part links are extensively evidenced across the 133-verse corpus. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Body-part links are evidenced. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Body-part links are evidenced. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Body-part links are evidenced. Not applicable.

---

#### T2.7 — Body — Direction

##### T2.7.1 — Where a body-characteristic link exists, which direction does it run — does the soul express through the body, does the body feed back to the soul, or does it run in both directions?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Primarily the body feeds to the soul. The defilement-state originates in a bodily event (carcass-contact, discharge, skin condition) and feeds back into the inner person as a condition affecting conscience, will, affect, and social standing. Lev 5:2-3 (M10c-A-VCG-01): the bodily contact creates the condition that the conscience then recognises. Lev 15:2 (M10c-A-VCG-06): the bodily discharge is the source of the unclean state that governs the person's relational and ritual standing. In M10c-B, the direction is more complex: the bodily condition (skin disease) is assessed by the priest, whose speech act then constitutes the social reality of the unclean status — so body → priestly assessment → performative speech → social condition. But also a soul-to-body direction in VCG-04: Lev 11:43-44 (M10c-A-VCG-04) — the will's refusal of defiling contact is the inner act that prevents the bodily acquisition of the state; the soul's volitional choice governs what the body does, preventing the body-to-soul contamination chain. Both directions are evidenced, with body-to-soul dominant.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Primarily soul-to-body, though with a bidirectional component. The soul's desires and will-failure are the originating force: Rom 1:24 (VCG-02) — "lusts of their hearts" leads to "dishonoring of their bodies" — the soul-level disorder (desire) produces the bodily consequence (dishonour). This is soul-to-body direction. However, at 2Cor 7:1 (VCG-03), the defilement is named as inhabiting both body and spirit simultaneously — suggesting that the body is not merely a passive recipient but a co-site of the condition; the direction is bidirectional in that the defilement inhabits both simultaneously and the cleansing must address both.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Primarily soul-to-body in consequence. The soul's covenantal betrayal (the will's volitional unfaithfulness — Num 5:20: "if you have defiled yourself... having lain with another man") produces a judgment received in the body (Num 5:27 — womb and thigh affected). The directional sequence is: volitional-covenantal betrayal (soul level) → defilement-state incurred (condition) → judicial consequence in body (body level). There is also a body-to-community movement: Eze 36:17 (VCG-04): "their ways before me were like the uncleanness of a woman in her menstrual impurity" — the bodily-impurity register (nid.dah) is the metaphor for the community's moral uncleanness, suggesting the body's impurity state provides the framework through which the corporate moral condition is understood (body informs the characterisation of the corporate soul-condition).

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The direction runs from the external spirit through the person's spirit-level to the body: external unclean spirit → spirit-level invasion → soul-will domination → body as instrument (convulsed, driven, voice appropriated). There is no reverse direction — the body does not feed back to the spirit or produce the characteristic from below. The domination is entirely top-down.

---

##### T2.7.2 — What is the consequence of that directionality for understanding the characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The predominantly body-to-soul direction reveals the characteristic as one in which the creaturely body's vulnerability is the primary generating reality. The inner person does not produce the ritual defilement-state through sin of the soul (that is Characteristics 2-3); rather, the body's contact with death, disease, and discharge creates a condition that then imposes itself on the whole person — conscience, will, social standing. This reveals the characteristic as a condition of creaturely finitude and mortality, not primarily a condition of inner moral failure. The soul's response — whether the will seeks remedy or refuses it — is the morally significant act within the condition; but the condition itself arrives through the body.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The primarily soul-to-body direction confirms the characteristic as originating in the inner person's willingness and desire rather than in bodily contact (distinguishing it from Characteristic 1). The defilement flows from the soul's disordered desire outward to the body — the body becomes the site of the condition's expression and consequence (Rom 1:24). The bidirectional element at 2Cor 7:1 reveals that once the condition is established, it inhabits the whole constitutional person — not only in the soul but also in the body — making the call to cleansing a call for the whole person's engagement.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The soul-to-body direction at Num 5:27 (VCG-01) reveals the characteristic as one in which covenantal volitional betrayal produces bodily consequences — the body bears the judicial consequence of the soul's covenantal defection. This reveals the characteristic as one in which the sacred relational order (covenant) is so constitutive of the person's and community's existence that betrayal of it produces consequences at the physical/bodily level. The covenantal bond is not merely a spiritual or social reality but one with bodily stakes.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The top-down directionality reveals why human restraint is futile (Luk 8:29 — chains and shackles broken): attempting to restrain the body (the lowest level of expression) cannot address the spirit-level cause. Only divine authority (operating at the spirit level — commanding the spirit directly, Mar 5:8) is effective. The consequence: the resolution must match the origin — external spirit-level invasion requires external divine authority at the spirit level to reverse.

---

##### T2.7.3 — If no body-characteristic link is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Body-characteristic links are extensively evidenced. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Body-characteristic links are evidenced. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Body-characteristic links are evidenced. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Body-characteristic links are evidenced. Not applicable.

---

#### T2.8 — Body — Deposit

##### T2.8.1 — Does sustained operation of this characteristic leave a constitutional deposit in the body or its design — including DNA or generational consequence?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

The 133-verse corpus does not evidence a constitutional deposit in the body from sustained ritual defilement. The characteristic is structured as a temporary and resolvable condition: "shall be unclean until the evening; then it shall be clean" (Lev 11:24, M10c-A-VCG-02). Even the most severe form (corpse-contact, seven-day defilement) is bounded and resolved through the prescribed remedy (Num 19:19-20, M10c-A-VCG-07). The earthenware vessel that must be broken (Lev 11:33, M10c-A-VCG-03) is an object, not a person; and the condemned house (Lev 14:44-45, M10c-B-VCG-04) is a structure. The evidence does not suggest a generational constitutional deposit within the person from the ritual defilement-state per se.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The evidence suggests a constitutional hardening rather than a physical deposit. Eph 4:19 (VCG-02): "become callous" — the sustained moral-inner defilement produces a progressive hardening of the conscience and of the inner moral faculties; this is a constitutional change in the inner person's capacity for moral response. The process described in Rom 1:24 (VCG-02) — God's judicial abandonment leading to further deepening of the impurity — suggests a self-reinforcing deterioration of the inner constitution over time. The "callousness" of Eph 4:19 is a constitutional deposit in the soul: the faculty that should respond to moral reality (conscience) has been hardened. Whether this constitutes a deposit in the body in a biological sense is not evidenced in the 26-verse corpus.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The evidence suggests a sustained corporate moral deterioration rather than a specific constitutional deposit in the individual body. Eze 22:3-4 (VCG-02): the city that "makes idols to defile herself" and has "become guilty" by sustained idolatrous practice — over time the community's identity becomes constitutively defiled, no longer incidental. Psa 106:39 (VCG-02): "thus they became unclean by their acts, and played the whore in their deeds" — the became-unclean is a condition that has taken hold. The "deposit" is at the corporate-communal level rather than in the individual body: the community's collective moral-spiritual identity is the site of the sustained deposit.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The 21-verse corpus does not evidence a lasting constitutional deposit from sustained spirit-possession. The restoration evidenced is complete: Luk 6:18 (VCG-02) — "were cured"; Luk 9:42 (VCG-01) — "healed the boy, and gave him back to his father"; Act 5:16 (VCG-02) — "they were all healed." The language of healing and cure implies full restoration without named residual deposit. Mat 12:43/Luk 11:24 — the spirit seeking re-entry after expulsion suggests remaining vulnerability to re-invasion, but this is a habitation-dynamic rather than a constitutional deposit.

---

##### T2.8.2 — What evidence supports or contradicts this?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

Supporting the absence of lasting deposit: the consistent pattern of remedy and restoration throughout the corpus (washing, waiting, priestly clearance, water of impurity) implies the condition leaves no permanent trace. Contradicting it weakly: the pattern of Num 19 where the defilement is substantial enough to require an elaborate community-wide remedy (the standing red-heifer ash provision — "for the congregation of the people of Israel," Num 19:9) suggests that defilement is a persistent communal reality requiring perpetual institutional provision. But this does not indicate a deposit within the individual body — it indicates the recurrent nature of the condition in creaturely life.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Supporting a constitutional deposit (in the soul): Eph 4:19 (VCG-02) — callousness as a lasting inner condition produced by sustained impurity; 2Cor 12:21 (VCG-02) — unrepented impurity as a hardened state resistant to change; Rom 1:24 (VCG-02) — the judicial abandonment leading to further defilement suggesting a downward trajectory that accumulates. Contradicting a permanent/irreversible deposit: 2Cor 7:1 (VCG-03) — "let us cleanse ourselves from every defilement of body and spirit" — the call to cleansing implies the deposit is not permanent; the condition can be resolved through cleansing. The evidence shows a serious constitutional hardening but one that remains within the scope of possible cleansing.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Supporting a sustained corporate deposit: Eze 20:30/31 (VCG-02) — the pattern is generational ("will you defile yourselves after the manner of your fathers?"), suggesting the corporate defilement-state accumulates across generations as an inherited pattern of moral defection. Eze 20:43 (VCG-02) — the future community will "loathe yourselves for all the evils that you have committed" — the deeds themselves are something the community carries into the future as a burden of memory. Contradicting permanent irreversibility: Eze 37:23 (VCG-05) — "they shall not defile themselves anymore" — the promise of permanent non-defilement implies the deposit can be addressed through divine cleansing. Zec 13:1 (VCG-05) — the cleansing fountain removes the defilement.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Supporting full restoration: Luk 6:18 — "cured"; Act 5:16 — "all healed"; Luk 9:42 — "healed... gave him back to his father" — no residual condition named. Potentially complicating: Mat 12:43/Luk 11:24 (VCG-02) — the "house" metaphor suggests the person remains a potential habitation after expulsion, implying vulnerability. But this is a relational-habitation dynamic rather than a biological/constitutional deposit.

---

##### T2.8.3 — If the evidence is silent, note this explicitly. This finding feeds directly into T5.7.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

The evidence is silent on constitutional deposit in the body from the ritual defilement-state. T5.7 will note this finding accordingly.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The evidence is not silent. A constitutional hardening (callousness of conscience — Eph 4:19) is evidenced as a sustained deposit of the condition. T5.7 will address the developmental consequence.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The evidence is not silent. A sustained corporate-generational deposit is evidenced (Eze 20:30 generational pattern; Psa 106:39 becoming-unclean through acts). T5.7 will address the developmental consequence.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The evidence is silent on lasting constitutional deposit. Restoration is consistently framed as complete. T5.7 will note this finding accordingly.

---

#### T2.9 — Origin and Source

##### T2.9.1 — Where does this characteristic originate constitutionally — is it generated from within the person, received from outside, bestowed by God, or carried generationally?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The ritual defilement-state has multiple origins evidenced in the corpus. (1) External physical contact: the most common origin — a person touches, carries, or sits on a defiling agent (carcass, discharge-surface, corpse) and acquires the state from outside (M10c-A-VCG-02, -06, -07). The origin is external, transmitted through material contact. (2) Internal bodily process: menstruation, childbirth, seminal emission, abnormal discharge (M10c-A-VCG-05, -06) originate the state from within the body itself — the body's own processes generate the condition. (3) Authoritative verdict: in M10c-B-VCG-02, the priestly pronouncement establishes the condition as a social reality — the origin is the authoritative speech act applied to a pre-existing bodily condition. (4) Spatial proximity: Num 19:14 (M10c-A-VCG-07) — being in a tent with a corpse produces defilement without direct contact; proximity is the origin. (5) Ingestion: Lev 17:15 (M10c-A-VCG-02) — eating a naturally dead animal defiles through ingestion.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The evidence identifies multiple origin paths. (1) Constitutional human uncleanness — a prior-to-individual-act condition: Job 14:4 (VCG-01) — "who can bring a clean thing out of an unclean? There is not one" — the origin is in the inherited human condition; the person is born into a constitutionally unclean state before specific choices. (2) Heart-level desire unchecked by God's ordering: Rom 1:24 (VCG-02) — "lusts of their hearts" — the desire arising within the heart is the proximate origin of the impurity condition when unchecked. (3) Former association with defiling contexts: 1Cor 8:7 (VCG-03) — "through former association with idols" — the formative environment generates the vulnerability in the conscience. (4) The silencing of conscience: Eph 4:19 (VCG-02) — "become callous" — the progressive suppression of the conscience is the origin of the condition's escalation.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The characteristic has multiple origin pathways, all within the community's volitional-covenantal life. (1) Sexual betrayal of covenantal bonds: VCG-01 — adultery (Num 5:13-29), sexual violations (Lev 18), violation of a person (Gen 34) — origin in volitional sexual transgression of covenant relationship. (2) Idolatrous desire and attachment: VCG-02 — "she defiled herself with all the idols of everyone after whom she lusted" (Eze 23:7) — origin in the community's desire oriented toward idols rather than God. (3) Deliberate desecration of sacred spaces: VCG-03 — Jer 7:30 — deliberate installation of detestable things in the sanctuary — origin in the will's purposeful desecration. (4) Habitual moral conduct contaminating the land: VCG-04 — "they defiled it by their ways and their deeds" (Eze 36:17) — origin in accumulated habitual conduct.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Uniquely, this characteristic originates from entirely outside the person: an external spiritual being (the unclean spirit) enters and inhabits the person from without. This contrasts with Characteristic 1 (bodily contact with material defiling agent), Characteristic 2 (from within the person's own desires and will), and Characteristic 3 (from the community's corporate volitional defection). Characteristic 4's origin is the only one in the M10c cluster entirely external — the person contributes nothing to the origin of their own condition.

---

##### T2.9.2 — What does the evidence reveal about whether the origin is singular or multiple?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The origin is clearly multiple. The 133-verse corpus encompasses at least five distinct origin pathways (external contact, internal bodily process, authoritative verdict, spatial proximity, ingestion). The diversity of origins reflects the characteristic's function as a comprehensive system for managing the person's sacral status across the full range of bodily and relational interactions with the material world. No single origin dominates; the system is designed to catch the full range of creaturely vulnerability.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The origin is clearly multiple. The constitutional origin (Job 14:4) is prior to and deeper than the habitual-desire origin (Rom 1:24); the formative-context origin (1Cor 8:7) is different again. The characteristic does not have a single point of origin but arises through the intersection of inherited constitutional vulnerability, unchecked desire, formative context, and progressive conscience-suppression.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The origin is clearly multiple. The characteristic does not arise from a single type of act or disposition but from the intersection of sexual betrayal, idolatrous attachment, deliberate desecration, and habitual moral conduct — all of which produce corporate/covenantal defilement through different mechanisms applied to different sacred objects (person, sanctuary, land, name).

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The origin is singular in kind (always an unclean spirit as the external agent) but may involve multiple individual spirits. Mar 5:13 (VCG-02): "the unclean spirits came out and entered the pigs" — plural spirits inhabiting one person. Mar 9:25 (VCG-01): one specific spirit addressed as "mute and deaf" — singular. The origin is consistently external-spiritual-agent, whether singular or multiple in number.

---

##### T2.9.3 — Does the origin of this characteristic change across different contexts evidenced in Scripture?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes. The Levitical context (the dominant origin context in the 133 verses) is comprehensively bodily and material. The NT akathartos categorical context (M10c-B-VCG-05) shows a shift: the origin of the "unclean" category at Act 10:14/28 is the conscience-level conviction formed by the categorical system — the origin of the functional unclean status is no longer bodily contact but categorical learned judgment. God's word then overturns that inner categorical origin: "what God has made clean, do not call unclean" (Act 10:28). The 1Cor 7:14 use shows yet another origin: covenantal-relational status (sanctifying influence of the believing spouse) as the origin of the clean/unclean status for children and spouses. The origin thus moves across the Testaments from primarily bodily/material to including categorical-conscience and relational-covenantal origins.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes. The Hebrew prophetic register (VCG-01: Job 14:4, Isa 64:6) frames origin as constitutional — the human condition as such is the unclean source. The Pauline epistolary register (VCG-02) frames origin as habitual-desire and God's judicial abandonment. The Corinthian epistolary register (VCG-03: 1Cor 8:7) frames origin as formative context and conscience-vulnerability. The Revelation apocalyptic register (VCG-04: Rev 16:13, 17:4, 18:2) frames origin as cosmic corruption — the characteristic appearing in spiritual beings sourced in darkness. The origin shifts from personal-constitutional (Job), to societal-moral (Isa 64:6), to habitual-volitional (Pauline), to contextual (1Cor), to cosmic (Revelation), reflecting the breadth of the characteristic's domain.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes. The legal-covenantal context (VCG-01: Lev 18, Num 5, Deu 24) frames origin in specific volitional sexual acts. The prophetic context (VCG-02: Ezekiel) frames origin in corporate spiritual whoredom and idolatrous desire across generations. The narratival context (VCG-01: Gen 34) frames origin in violent personal violation. The lament context (VCG-05: Lam 1:17/4:15) frames origin in the accumulated corporate defilement whose consequences have arrived as exile. The origin shifts in mode (individual volitional act vs corporate sustained pattern) and time-frame (single event vs generational accumulation) across the corpus.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The 21-verse corpus does not evidence different mechanisms of origin across contexts. All 21 verses share the same origin pattern: an external unclean spirit inhabiting a person. The mechanism is the same whether in a synagogue (Mar 1:23), among tombs (Mar 5:2), a child (Mar 7:25, Luk 9:42), or many persons (Act 5:16, Act 8:7). The consistency of the origin mechanism across all contexts confirms the characteristic as purely externally-generated.

---

#### T2.10 — Constitutional Movement

##### T2.10.1 — Does this characteristic move across constitutional levels — from spirit to soul, from soul to body, or across boundaries in other directions?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes, in one primary direction: from body to the soul's functional faculties. The characteristic originates in bodily events (contact, emission, disease, proximity) and moves upward to engage the conscience (Lev 5:2-3, M10c-A-VCG-01), the affect (Num 9:7, M10c-A-VCG-07), the will (Num 19:20, M10c-A-VCG-07), and the social-relational standing (Lev 13:46, M10c-B-VCG-03). It also moves outward from the person to objects (M10c-A-VCG-03: vessels, food, water) and to other persons through transmission (M10c-A-VCG-06 and -07: secondary and cascading contact). The reverse movement is evidenced at M10c-A-VCG-04 (Lev 11:43-44): the will's inner choice (soul-level) acts preventively to keep the body from acquiring the condition — soul governing body to prevent the body-to-soul contamination chain.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes. 2Cor 7:1 (VCG-03) directly evidences constitutional movement: "defilement of body and spirit" — the condition is named as present at both levels simultaneously. The sequence of movement from the evidence: desire at the soul level (heart-lusts, Rom 1:24) → impurity as condition (the state entered through the desire) → bodily dishonour as consequence (Rom 1:24: "dishonoring of their bodies") → spirit-level defilement (2Cor 7:1). The movement is from soul-desire → soul-condition → body-expression → spirit-penetration. The characteristic penetrates downward from the soul's desiderative function to the spirit and upward/outward to the body.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes. The characteristic originates at the soul level (corporate will, desire, allegiance — VCG-01, -02) and moves outward to: the body (judicial consequence in Num 5:27), social-communal space (expulsion — Lam 4:15, exile — Eze 4:13, Hos 9:3), sacred physical environment (land — VCG-04, sanctuary — VCG-03), and the divine name (Eze 43:7/8). The movement is from soul outward to sacred environment. There is also a counter-movement: God's perception of the defilement (Eze 23:13: "I saw that she was defiled") moves from the sacred/divine perspective inward to assess the community's condition.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes, in one primary direction: external spirit → person's spirit-level (invasion and domination) → soul-level will and faculties (overridden and suppressed) → body (convulsed, driven, voice appropriated). The movement is exclusively downward from spirit through soul to body, driven entirely by the external agent.

---

##### T2.10.2 — What does the evidence reveal about the sequence or pattern of that movement?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The standard sequence is: bodily event (contact/emission/disease/proximity) → condition acquired → conscience awakening → will engages (toward remedy or refusal) → social consequence (exclusion or restoration). This sequence is most fully evidenced in the corpse-contact sub-register (M10c-A-VCG-07): the bodily contact is the trigger; the condition is immediately imposed (Num 19:11: "shall be unclean seven days"); the conscience and will must then engage the remedy (Num 19:19-20: sprinkling on third and seventh days, washing); failure to engage produces the social-covenantal consequence (cut off from the assembly). The sequence in the verdict register (M10c-B-VCG-02) is different: bodily condition (skin deterioration) → priestly observation → priestly speech act → condition established socially → personal-social consequences.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The sequence is: (1) soul-level desire generated internally (Rom 1:24 — "lusts of their hearts"); (2) the condition of impurity entered as desire goes unchecked; (3) bodily consequences expressed outwardly (Rom 1:24 — "dishonoring of their bodies"); (4) simultaneous body-and-spirit habitation of the defilement (2Cor 7:1). The pattern is inward-first (desire at the heart), then spreading to both constitutional extremes (body and spirit). The cleansing reversal (2Cor 7:1) must therefore address both body and spirit — confirming that the movement has penetrated to both and that the remedy must match the scope of the spread.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The sequence evidenced in the prophetic corpus (especially Ezekiel): corporate will oriented toward idols (soul-desire) → acts of defiling self with idols/abominations (volitional acts) → land defiled by ways and deeds (Eze 36:17: habitual conduct contaminating sacred space) → sanctuary desecrated (Eze 5:11, 23:38) → divine name defiled (Eze 43:7/8) → God withdraws (Eze 5:11) → exile and expulsion (VCG-05). The sequence moves from the innermost (soul-desire) outward through concentric circles of sacred space (land → sanctuary → name → divine presence) with the final consequence being exile — the reversal of the centripetal covenant-gathering — as the community is expelled from the sacred space it has contaminated.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The sequence: (1) external spirit enters/seizes (Mar 5:2 — "had an unclean spirit"; Luk 8:29 — "many a time it had seized him"); (2) will is overridden (Luk 8:29 — "driven by the demon," breaking restraints); (3) specific faculties suppressed (Mar 9:25 — speech and hearing); (4) body becomes instrument of the spirit's expression (Mar 1:26 — convulsing and crying out). The resolution sequence reverses: divine command addresses the spirit (Mar 5:8 — "Come out of the man"); spirit departs (Mar 1:26; Act 8:7); person's faculties restored; person returned to community (Luk 9:42 — given back to father).

---

##### T2.10.3 — If no constitutional movement is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Constitutional movement is evidenced. Not applicable.

## T3 — Inner Being Faculties (33 prompts)

---

### T3

#### T3.1 — Perception

##### T3.1.1 — Does this characteristic engage the perceptive faculty — the inner senses including hearing, sight, taste, touch, smell, and spiritual discernment — and if so, which inner sense and how?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes, substantially. The characteristic engages: (1) Inner sight (visual discernment): the priestly examination system (M10c-B-VCG-02) is entirely visually-mediated — "the priest shall look" and assess by sight the appearance of skin disease (Lev 13:3, 13:8, 13:14, 13:20, 13:25, 13:27, 13:30, 13:36). The priest's inner sight — trained to distinguish appearance markers (hair colour, depth of lesion, spread) — is the primary diagnostic faculty. (2) Touch: touch is the primary transmission vector in M10c-A — touching carcasses (Lev 11:24-31, VCG-02), touching the discharge-person (Lev 15:7, VCG-06), touching objects (Lev 15:5-10), touching the corpse (Num 19:11, VCG-07). Touch is the dominant mode of acquiring the defilement-state. (3) Spiritual discernment: Lev 10:10 (M10c-B-VCG-01) requires "active inner discernment" — the faculty of distinguishing holy/common and clean/unclean is named as a priestly and communal discipline that goes beyond mere visual observation.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes. The dominant perceptive engagement is spiritual discernment — the inner capacity to perceive what is clean or defiled, holy or corrupt. Isa 6:5 (VCG-01): the prophet's eyes perceive the divine holiness ("my eyes have seen the King, the Lord of hosts") — the visual perception triggers the conscience-mediated recognition of inner defilement. Mat 23:27 (VCG-04): Jesus perceives the hidden inner defilement that is invisible to human sight — "outwardly appear beautiful, but within are full of... uncleanness" — this is the divine perceptual faculty seeing through the surface to the moral-inner reality. 1Cor 8:7 (VCG-03): the person's perception of food as idol-offered (rather than as simply food) is the mechanism through which the defiled conscience is engaged — perception shapes the conscience's response.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes. Three perceptive modes are engaged. (1) Divine spiritual perception: Eze 23:13 (VCG-02) — "I saw that she was defiled" — God's comprehensive spiritual perception perceives the community's defilement as an objective fact, even when the community cannot perceive it themselves. Hos 5:3 (VCG-02): "I know Ephraim, and Israel is not hidden from me; for now, O Ephraim, you have played the whore; Israel is defiled" — divine perceptive omniscience holds the defilement clearly. (2) Prophetic visual discernment: Eze 22:26 (VCG-05) — priests who "have made no distinction between the holy and the common... and the unclean and the clean" — perceptive discernment failure is a key component of the characteristic's systemic propagation. (3) God's moral revulsion: Eze 36:17 (VCG-04) — "their ways before me were like the uncleanness of a woman in her menstrual impurity" — the divine perception is one of moral revulsion, perceiving the community's conduct through the lens of what is most repugnant.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes, at two levels. (1) The spirit suppresses specific perceptive faculties: Mar 9:25 (VCG-01) — the spirit is addressed as "mute and deaf" — the person's hearing is suppressed. (2) The spirits have perceptive self-awareness toward the divine: Mar 3:11 (VCG-03) — "whenever the unclean spirits saw him, they fell down before him and cried out, 'You are the Son of God'" — the spirits perceive and recognise divine identity. The person in the characteristic cannot receive speech (deaf), while the spirits possess heightened perceptive recognition of Christ.

---

##### T3.1.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair the perceptive faculty in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic enables and deepens perceptive faculty in the volitional/discernment register: sustained engagement with the clean/unclean categorical system trains the person in refined visual and categorical discernment (Lev 11:47: "to make a distinction between the unclean and the clean" — a cultivated perceptual discipline, M10c-B-VCG-01). However, the characteristic can also reveal the limits of perception: Lev 5:2-3 (M10c-A-VCG-01) shows that defilement can be acquired before the person perceives it — the condition precedes perceptual awareness, exposing the perceptive faculty's inadequacy to catch all contamination events. The conscience supplements what perception misses.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic impairs the perceptive faculty in its advanced form: Eph 4:19 (VCG-02) — "become callous" — the callousness of conscience includes a progressive impairment of the inner capacity to perceive moral reality correctly. The Tit 1:15 reference (VCG-03) — "to the defiled and unbelieving, nothing is pure" — shows that advanced defilement produces a condition where the person's perceptive moral faculty cannot correctly assess moral reality: everything appears defiled because the instrument of perception (conscience, mind) is itself defiled. However, the characteristic also enables a negative form of perceptive sharpening in those resisting it: the positive-inverse (VCG-05 — Rev 3:4, 14:4) shows persons whose perceptive faculty has been maintained in moral clarity through not soiling their garments.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The characteristic impairs perception in two registers. (1) Self-perception: Jer 2:23 (VCG-02) — "how can you say, 'I am not unclean, I have not gone after the Baals'?" — the community cannot correctly perceive its own defilement-state; self-perception is compromised by the same self-deception that sustains the condition. (2) Priestly discernment: Eze 22:26 (VCG-05) — the priests' failure to teach clean/unclean distinction shows a systemic failure of the institutional perceptive-discernment faculty. However, the characteristic also enables a future acute perception: Eze 20:43 (VCG-02) — the community will "remember" and "loathe" — the eschatological perception of what they have done will be clear and grievous.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The characteristic impairs the perceptive faculty of the inhabited person: Mar 9:25 (VCG-01) — hearing suppressed; speech suppressed (the perceptive-expressive complex). The characteristic bypasses the person's perceptive self-awareness of their own condition — there is no evidence that the inhabited person perceives or articulates their own condition from within it.

---

##### T3.1.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with perception reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The pervasive engagement with visual assessment (the leprous-disease priestly examination in Lev 13-14, M10c-B-VCG-02) reveals that the characteristic treats the bodily surface as a readable text — the skin's appearance encodes the person's sacral status. Simultaneously, the VCG-01 evidence (defilement hidden from perception) reveals that the characteristic is not reducible to what the person perceives: the condition exists objectively prior to awareness. This shows the characteristic as operating in a domain that partially exceeds the perceptive faculty's reach, requiring conscience to supplement perception.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The perceptive engagement reveals the characteristic as self-obscuring at the advanced stage: the condition suppresses the perceptive faculty that would recognise it. The person fully in the moral-inner defilement-state can no longer perceive it as defilement (Eph 4:19 — callousness; Tit 1:15 reference — nothing pure to the defiled). The characteristic is thus not simply a condition alongside normal inner functioning but one that compromises the inner faculties' ability to perceive themselves correctly. This distinguishes it from Characteristic 1 (Ritual defilement-state), which the person can recognise through the categorical system; Characteristic 2 corrupts the very instrument of recognition.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The perceptive pattern reveals the characteristic as self-obscuring in the present and self-revealing in the eschatological future. The community in the defilement-state cannot perceive its own condition (Jer 2:23), while God perceives it clearly (Eze 23:13, Hos 5:3) and prophetic speech confronts the gap. The future restoration is precisely the moment when the community's perception will align with God's — they will see what God has always seen (Eze 20:43). This reveals the characteristic as involving an epistemological disruption: the defiled community cannot assess itself correctly, requiring divine and prophetic counter-testimony.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The perceptive pattern reveals the characteristic as selectively targeting the person's relational perceptive faculties (hearing and speech), precisely the faculties required for relationship with God and with others. The selective suppression of hearing and speech reveals the characteristic as operating to isolate the person relationally — cutting off their perceptive access to the voices of God and neighbour. This is consistent with the broader pattern of communal severance (Mar 5:2).

---

#### T3.2 — Cognition

##### T3.2.1 — Does this characteristic engage the cognitive faculty — knowing, understanding, discerning — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes. The most explicit cognitive engagement is the discernment imperative of M10c-B-VCG-01: Lev 10:10 ("to distinguish between the holy and the common, and between the unclean and the clean"), Lev 11:47 ("to make a distinction between the unclean and the clean"), Lev 14:57 ("to show when it is unclean and when it is clean"), Lev 20:25 (commanding Israel to "separate the clean beast from the unclean"). The cognitive faculty is engaged in learning, applying, and transmitting the categorical system. Lev 10:10 frames the priestly vocation as inherently cognitive: the priest must know the distinctions and teach them. Act 10:14/28 (M10c-B-VCG-05) shows the same categorical knowledge in NT conscience — Peter's cognitive framework of clean/unclean is fully internalized and requires divine speech to revise.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes. The defiled-mind reference in VCG-03 (Tit 1:15: "both their minds and their consciences are defiled") most directly names the cognitive faculty. Within §3: 2Pe 2:10 (VCG-03) — "bold and willful" — names a specific cognitive-volitional posture (bold defiance) that accompanies the defilement. Mat 23:27 (VCG-04) — the hypocrites' outer appearance and inner reality being in contradiction — reveals that cognitive-self-assessment (they present themselves as righteous) is distorted by the defilement: they cannot correctly cognise their own condition.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes. Eze 22:26 (VCG-05): the priestly failure to "make distinction between the holy and the common" is a failure of the cognitive-categorical faculty — the structured knowledge of clean/unclean that the characteristic requires is collapsed by priestly dereliction. Eze 44:23 (VCG-05): "they shall teach my people the difference between the holy and the common, and show them how to distinguish between the unclean and the clean" — cognition (categorical knowledge of clean/unclean) is the faculty that must be restored in the new priestly order. Jer 2:23 (VCG-02): self-deceived cognition — the community asserts claims about its own condition that are not accurate.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The 21-verse corpus does not explicitly evidence engagement with the cognitive faculty (knowing, understanding, discerning) in the inhabited person. The spirits themselves demonstrate cognitive self-awareness (Mar 3:11 — recognising divine identity), but this is the spirits' cognition, not the person's.

---

##### T3.2.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair cognition in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic deepens cognition through the categorical training effect noted at T3.2.1. The purity system is a comprehensive training curriculum for the perceptual and categorical cognitive faculty. However, it can also impair cognition in the NT sense: Peter's deep categorical knowledge, formed through lifelong observance, initially prevents him from perceiving what God is doing in the vision (Act 10:14/28, M10c-B-VCG-05). The formed cognitive framework becomes a resistance to new revelation. The characteristic thus shows cognition as both enabled (through systematic categorical formation) and potentially impaired (when the formed category becomes an inflexible inner resistance to divine revision).

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Impairs cognition in the advanced state: the Tit 1:15 reference (VCG-03) — "to the defiled and unbelieving, nothing is pure" — names a condition where the cognitive faculty cannot correctly categorise moral reality; the instrument of moral cognition is compromised. Mat 23:27 (VCG-04): the hypocrites' self-cognition is distorted — they appear to themselves as righteous while "within full of... uncleanness." The advanced moral-inner defilement-state thus produces cognitive distortion of self-assessment and moral categorisation.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)
