The characteristic impairs cognition specifically in the domains of self-assessment (Jer 2:23 — self-deception) and categorical moral discernment (Eze 22:26 — failure to distinguish holy from common). These two cognitive failures are both symptoms of and contributors to the corporate defilement-state: when the community cannot correctly assess its own moral condition or the sacred/common distinction, the defilement can persist without self-corrective response.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

Not evidenced within the 21-verse corpus. The characteristic suppresses specific faculties (will, speech/hearing) but does not explicitly address the cognitive faculty.

---

##### T3.2.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with cognition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic is constitutively cognitive — it cannot operate without categorical knowledge. The person must know which animals are categorically clean or unclean (Lev 11 corpus, M10c-A-VCG-02), what disease markers indicate leprous defilement (Lev 13 corpus, M10c-B-VCG-02), how contamination transmits through which contact pathways (M10c-A-VCG-06 and -07). The characteristic is thus a system that requires cognitive formation to navigate. This reveals that the characteristic is not merely a bodily-mechanism condition but an intellectually structured domain: a person cannot adequately manage the ritual defilement-state without the cognitive equipment provided by the purity laws.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The cognitive impairment pattern reveals the characteristic as epistemically corrupting: sustained moral-inner defilement does not merely produce wrong behaviour but wrong moral cognition — the person cannot correctly assess the moral character of actions, things, or their own inner condition. This reveals the characteristic as striking at the root of moral reasoning rather than merely redirecting the will.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The cognitive pattern reveals the characteristic as dependent on institutional knowledge transmission: the clean/unclean distinction is a taught faculty (Eze 44:23 — priests must teach it; Eze 22:26 — priests have failed to teach it). When the cognitive-formative institution (priesthood) fails, the community's capacity for the self-knowledge that would interrupt the defilement-cycle is lost. The characteristic propagates in part through the collapse of institutional cognition.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The silence on cognitive engagement reveals that the characteristic does not target the cognitive faculty specifically; it operates through will-domination and faculty-suppression rather than through cognitive distortion. This contrasts with Characteristics 2 and 3 where defiled cognition and self-deception are part of the mechanism. Characteristic 4 bypasses the cognitive faculty rather than corrupting it.

---

#### T3.3 — Memory

##### T3.3.1 — Does this characteristic engage the memory faculty — the holding and retrieving of inner-being reality across time — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Memory is engaged in the cognitive-formation role: the categorical system must be remembered and applied consistently. Lev 11:47 (M10c-B-VCG-01) names the purpose of all purity laws as cultivating active moral discernment — a capacity that can only function through memory of what is clean and what is unclean. Peter's Act 10:14 conviction — "I have never eaten anything that is common or unclean" — is the product of memory: a lifetime of categorical observance retained as a deeply embedded inner rule. Memory in this characteristic functions as the repository of the categorical system that the person draws on in each encounter with a potential defiling agent.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes, at two evidenced points. 2Cor 12:21 (VCG-02): Paul speaks of "those who sinned earlier and have not repented of the impurity... that they have practiced" — the memory of past impurity as practiced sin is the frame for the present unrepented state. The memory of what has been practiced (the history of the defilement-state) is part of what Paul expects repentance to engage. Rom 6:19 (VCG-02): "just as you once presented your members as slaves to impurity" — the memory of the prior condition is the rhetorical frame for the call to a new orientation; the person is asked to remember what they were to understand what they are being called away from.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes, centrally and uniquely. Eze 20:43 (VCG-02) is the most important evidence: "there you shall remember your ways and all your deeds with which you have defiled yourselves, and you shall loathe yourselves for all the evils that you have committed." The memory of corporate defilement is the named mechanism of the characteristic's eschatological resolution — the community's future remembering of its defilement-state will generate the self-loathing that is the inner mechanism of repentance. No other verse in the 83-verse corpus provides this direct evidence of memory as the defilement-state's resolution mechanism.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The 21-verse corpus does not evidence engagement with the memory faculty. The characteristic is focused on present domination rather than on memory's holding of inner-being reality across time.

---

##### T3.3.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair memory in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic deepens memory in the cognitive formation role: the repeated application of the categorical system across a lifetime of observance forms a deep memory structure. The duration provisions ("until the evening," "seven days") also engage temporal memory — the person must remember when their defilement was incurred to know when they are restored. Lev 15 (M10c-A-VCG-05 and -06) implies that the menstruating woman and the discharge-person must track time within their condition. Memory of the incurred defilement's timing governs the resolution.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic impairs repentance-memory in the advanced state: 2Cor 12:21 (VCG-02) — the persons who "have not repented" show that the memory of past impurity is not functioning as a summons to change; the memory exists but does not produce the response that memory of sin should produce (repentance). The characteristic thus interferes with the memory faculty's proper moral function: the memory of defilement should lead to grief and repentance, but sustained impurity produces a memory that is present but inactive as a moral summons.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The characteristic both impairs memory in the present (the community cannot remember what it is doing — Jer 2:23 suggests denial and forgetting of the prophets' testimony) and will enable memory in the future as the appointed instrument of repentance (Eze 20:43). In the present, the community remembers its own self-justifying narrative ("I am not unclean"); in the future restoration, it will remember the actual narrative of its defilement. The characteristic thus suppresses correct memory in the present and requires it for repentance in the future.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

Not evidenced. The characteristic bypasses the memory faculty — it operates in the present moment of invasion and domination.

---

##### T3.3.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with memory reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The memory engagement reveals that the characteristic is temporally structured — it has beginnings and endings (acquisition and resolution), durations (until-evening vs seven-day), and provisions tied to temporal sequence (third and seventh day sprinkling, Num 19:19). The person must hold the defilement event in memory as a temporal anchor to know when they are clean again. This reveals the characteristic as not just a static condition but a temporally dynamic one, requiring the memory faculty for proper navigation.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The pattern reveals the characteristic as memory-resistant in its advanced stage: the person can remember past impurity but has not repented of it (2Cor 12:21, VCG-02). The memory faculty's proper function — to make past moral failure present as a summons to repentance — is blocked by the same callousness that blocks conscience (Eph 4:19). Memory of defilement and repentance from defilement are thus disconnected in the advanced state: memory without transformation.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The memory pattern reveals the characteristic as uniquely designed for a future redemptive function through memory: unlike Characteristic 2 where memory is present but ineffective (because the conscience is suppressed), Characteristic 3 has a specific divine appointment for corporate memory to function as the mechanism of self-loathing and repentance (Eze 20:43). The characteristic is thus not merely a condition to be escaped but a past reality to be remembered as the generative force of the restored community's humility. This is Characteristic 3's most analytically distinctive feature.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The silence on memory reveals the characteristic as temporally immediate in its impact — seizing, dominating, and suppressing in the present without requiring a history of the person's own choices or memories. This contrasts with Characteristic 3 (where memory of past defilement is the designed mechanism of future repentance — Eze 20:43). Characteristic 4 operates without engaging the memory faculty because its mechanism is external imposition.

---

#### T3.4 — Affect

##### T3.4.1 — Does this characteristic engage the affective faculty — feeling and emotional experience — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes, at two documented points. First, grief at exclusion: Num 9:7 (M10c-A-VCG-07) — the men rendered unclean through corpse-contact "said to him, 'We are unclean through touching a dead body. Why are we kept from bringing the Lord's offering at its appointed time among the people of Israel?'" The grief of desire blocked by an involuntary condition is directly named. Second, the distress of enforced isolation: Lev 13:45-46 (M10c-B-VCG-03) — the person with skin disease must live alone outside the camp for the entire duration of the condition. The cumulative isolation of a sustained defilement state is a condition of relational deprivation that engages the affective faculty, though the verses do not use emotional vocabulary directly.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes. Paul's anticipated mourning at 2Cor 12:21 (VCG-02) — "I may have to mourn over many of those who sinned earlier" — shows that the unrepented impurity produces grief in the pastoral observer who perceives the condition. The affective register of grief is the proper response of one who sees the condition clearly. The positive-inverse in VCG-05 engages affect differently: Rev 14:4 — "they follow the Lamb wherever he goes" — the undefiled inner state is characterised by devotion and following, which is an affective orientation toward Christ. Isa 6:5 (VCG-01) — "woe is me! For I am lost" — the prophet's recognition of his moral-inner defilement produces the affective response of lostness-distress.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes. Three affective registers are evidenced. (1) Simmering grief and restrained anger: Gen 34:5 (VCG-01) — Jacob's immediate affective response to the violation of Dinah is restrained awareness; the brothers' affective response (Gen 34:13: "the sense of violated honour drives a calculated, vengeful will") is controlled outrage. (2) Jealousy: Num 5:14 (VCG-01) — "if the spirit of jealousy comes over him" — covenantal betrayal generates jealousy as the immediate affective inner response. (3) Future self-loathing: Eze 20:43 (VCG-02) — "you shall loathe yourselves for all the evils that you have committed" — the anticipated eschatological affect is self-loathing generated by the memory of defilement. (4) Moral revulsion: Eze 36:17 (VCG-04) — God's perception of the community's conduct as "like the uncleanness of a woman in her menstrual impurity" — the language of moral revulsion describes God's affective response to the corporate defilement.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes, indirectly — through the response of those around the affected person. Mar 7:25 (VCG-01): "immediately a woman whose little daughter had an unclean spirit... came and fell down at his feet" — the mother's urgent, prostrate supplication shows intense affective response generated by the child's condition. Act 5:16 (VCG-02): "people gathered from the towns around Jerusalem, bringing the sick and those afflicted with unclean spirits" — the corporate affective response of concern and care. The affected person's own affect is not narrated (dominated and suppressed), but the affect of those who love them is strongly engaged.

---

##### T3.4.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair affect in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic engages affect primarily in the direction of impairment of access to affect's desired objects: the worship desire is blocked (Num 9:7); the communal belonging is severed (Lev 13:46). The affect is not generated by the characteristic; it pre-exists as desire for worship and belonging. The defilement-state blocks the fulfilment of that desire, creating grief. The defilement-state also generates the grief of self-recognition at Lev 13:45 — the public cry "Unclean, unclean" is a ritually required expression that externalises the inner condition; the person cannot keep the inner reality of their condition to themselves.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic impairs affect in a specific way: it suppresses the affective capacity for appropriate grief and distress over moral failure. Eph 4:19 (VCG-02) — "become callous" — the callousness that accompanies advanced moral defilement includes affective numbing: the person no longer feels the distress that should accompany moral failure. The characteristic also enables a perverse affect: "greedy to practice every kind of impurity" (Eph 4:19) — desire/appetite experienced as positive drive, where the defilement is sought rather than mourned.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The characteristic engages affect in two directions. It suppresses appropriate grief and repentance in the present (the community in denial — Jer 2:23 — does not feel the appropriate grief over its defilement). It activates a future acute affective response (Eze 20:43 — self-loathing as the eschatological affective consequence). The characteristic thus suppresses the affective response that would interrupt the defilement in the present, while positioning a future affective crisis (self-loathing) as the mechanism of resolution.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The characteristic bypasses the affected person's own affect — there is no evidence of the inhabited person's own emotional response from within the condition. Simultaneously, the characteristic generates intense affect in those who love the person: the mother's prostrate urgency (Mar 7:25), the father receiving his son back (Luk 9:42). The characteristic displaces affect: the person's own affect is suppressed or inaccessible, while the community's affect is intensified.

---

##### T3.4.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with affect reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The affective engagement reveals that the characteristic is not affectively neutral — the state of ritual exclusion is experienced, not merely catalogued. The grief at Num 9:7 and the enforced isolation of Lev 13:46 show that the defilement-state has emotional cost. This reveals that the characteristic operates within a relational and affective economy: the person in the defilement-state is not simply a legal category but a person who feels the loss of worship access and communal belonging. The characteristic's management thus requires attending not only to the legal remedy but to the affective experience of the excluded person.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The affective pattern reveals an inversion: the characteristic should produce grief and distress (Isa 6:5 — "woe is me!"; 2Cor 12:21 — Paul's anticipated mourning). But sustained defilement suppresses the grief-capacity (callousness, Eph 4:19) and replaces it with an appetite for more defilement. The characteristic thus inverts the proper affective response — from distress to desire, from mourning to greed. This affective inversion is one of the characteristic's most diagnostically significant features.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The affective pattern reveals the characteristic as inverting proper affect in the present (the community feels justification — Jer 2:23 — rather than grief) and reversing this inversion in the eschatological future (Eze 20:43 — self-loathing). The characteristic is thus an affective disorder that will be eschatologically corrected: the community that should have felt grief over its defilement will finally feel it in the moment of restoration, and that grief will be generative of repentance.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The affective pattern reveals the characteristic as relationally disruptive at the affective level: the person cannot express their own affect normally, while those who love them experience intense grief and urgency. The characteristic generates suffering not only in the possessed person but in their relational community — the mother (Mar 7:25), the father (Luk 9:42), and the communities bringing afflicted members (Act 5:16) all bear the affective cost alongside the person directly inhabited.

---

#### T3.5 — Creativity

##### T3.5.1 — Does this characteristic engage the creative faculty — imagination and the capacity to originate — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

The 133-verse corpus does not evidence engagement with the creative faculty. The ritual defilement-state is a condition managed through prescribed ritual procedures (washing, waiting, examination, water of impurity), not through creative or imaginative acts. The characteristic operates within a fixed normative system; the person's response is governed by law, not by creative origination.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (S)

The 26-verse corpus does not evidence engagement with the creative faculty (imagination, capacity to originate). The characteristic operates in the domain of desire, will, conscience, and moral orientation — not in the domain of creative imagination or origination. No verse in §3 names creativity or imagination as engaged by the moral-inner defilement-state.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (S)

The 83-verse corpus does not evidence engagement with the creative faculty (imagination, capacity to originate). The characteristic operates in the domain of will, desire, covenant fidelity, and sacral stewardship — not in the domain of creative imagination or origination.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The 21-verse corpus does not evidence engagement with the creative faculty. The characteristic operates through domination, suppression, and affliction, not through the imaginative dimension.

---

##### T3.5.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair creativity in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

Not evidenced from the 133-verse corpus.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (S)

Not evidenced within the 26-verse corpus.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (S)

Not evidenced in the 83-verse corpus.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

Not evidenced within the 21-verse corpus.

---

##### T3.5.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with creativity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

The silence on creativity reveals that the characteristic belongs to the domain of normative regulation rather than imaginative origination. The defilement-state is managed through prescribed, structured responses — there is no latitude for creative improvisation in its handling. This reveals the characteristic as a condition embedded in law and covenant structure, not in the open domain of the creative faculty.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (S)

The silence on creativity reveals that the characteristic operates primarily in the moral-volitional-desiderative domain rather than the imaginative. Its impact is on the inner faculties of willing, desiring, conscience-forming, and moral evaluation — not on the constructive or imaginative capacities.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (S)

The silence on creativity reveals the characteristic as operating in the domain of moral-covenantal conduct and its consequences for sacred environments rather than in the generative-imaginative domain. The characteristic's inner-being engagement is with the will's fidelity or betrayal, not with the imaginative or creative capacity.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The silence confirms the characteristic as operating in the domain of will, faculty-suppression, and bodily domination rather than in the generative-imaginative domain. The characteristic suppresses existing faculties rather than corrupting the creative capacity.

---

#### T3.6 — Volition

##### T3.6.1 — Does this characteristic engage the volitional faculty — the capacity to choose — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes, substantially. The volitional faculty is engaged at multiple points: (1) volitional avoidance: Lev 11:43-44 (M10c-A-VCG-04) — "you shall not defile yourselves with any swarming thing that crawls on the ground." The person is commanded to refuse defiling contact; this requires the will's active choice not to touch or eat the defiling agent. (2) Volitional pursuit of remedy: Lev 15:11 (M10c-A-VCG-06) — "if the one with the discharge touches someone without first rinsing his hands in water"; the washing of hands is a volitional act that prevents transmission. Num 19:19-20 (M10c-A-VCG-07) — the prescribed cleansing requires the person to present themselves for sprinkling. (3) Volitional refusal of remedy: Num 19:20 (M10c-A-VCG-07) — "if the man who is unclean does not cleanse himself" — the will's refusal of the appointed remedy is the decisive moral fault.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes, centrally. Rom 6:19 (VCG-02): "slaves to impurity" — the will is bound under the condition; the slavery metaphor names the will as the faculty constrained by the defilement. Eph 4:19 (VCG-02): "given themselves up to sensuality" — a volitional act of self-surrender that entrenches the condition. 2Cor 12:21 (VCG-02): those who "have not repented" — the will's refusal of repentance as the maintenance mechanism of the defilement-state. Rev 14:4 (VCG-05): "they follow the Lamb wherever he goes" — the will's positive orientation in the non-defiled state, following as an active volitional posture. The volitional faculty is the primary theatre in which the characteristic's progress or resolution is determined.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes, centrally. The volitional faculty is the primary generating force of the characteristic. Eze 22:3 (VCG-02): the city "makes idols to defile herself" — purposeful, self-directed volitional act of desecration. Eze 20:7/18/30 (VCG-02): the repeated commands "do not defile yourselves with the idols of Egypt / your fathers / your fathers' manner?" all presuppose volitional capacity — the command is possible because the will can choose. Jer 7:30 (VCG-03): "they have set their detestable things in the house that is called by my name, to defile it" — the phrase "to defile it" names the will's purpose; the desecration is intentional. Lev 18:20 (VCG-01): "you shall not lie sexually with your neighbor's wife and so make yourself unclean with her" — the prohibition addresses the will directly.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes, centrally — through domination. Luk 8:29 (VCG-01): "he would break the bonds and be driven by the demon into the desert" — the person's will is overridden; the body acts on the demon's impulse. The will is not eliminated but subjugated: the person exists as a will but cannot express it in their own direction. The contrast between the demon's will (driving the man) and the human person's will (which human restraint attempted to support but failed) reveals the will as the primary contested faculty.

---

##### T3.6.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair volition in the person — including its three aspects: capacity, interaction with other characteristics, and the constraints under which it operates?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic structures the volitional faculty rather than enabling or impairing it directly. It creates a framework of volitional obligation: the will must choose at each contact point (touch or refrain), at each remedy point (cleanse or refuse). The characteristic bypasses the will in the unconscious-defilement cases (Lev 5:2-3, M10c-A-VCG-01) — defilement arrives without volitional participation — but this does not eliminate the will's obligation to respond once awareness arrives. The characteristic thus reveals volition as operative at the perimeter of the condition (avoidance and remedy), not at its core (acquisition in most cases).

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic impairs volition in a specific way: it produces bondage of the will (Rom 6:19 — "slaves to impurity") while maintaining the appearance of volitional activity (Eph 4:19 — "given themselves up" — the person appears to choose). The will remains active but is redirected and constrained: it can choose to pursue impurity ("greedy to practice every kind of impurity," Eph 4:19) but cannot freely choose away from it without the intervention of the gospel's liberating power (Rom 6:19 — "so now present your members as slaves to righteousness" — the new possibility must be named as a call, implying it requires external enabling). The characteristic thus produces a pseudo-freedom that is actually bondage.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The characteristic engages volition in two contradictory directions. On one hand it is generated by volitional acts (deliberate idolatry, deliberate sexual betrayal, deliberate desecration) — the will is functional and active, choosing the defilement. On the other hand, Eze 20:30 (VCG-02) — "will you defile yourselves after the manner of your fathers?" — reveals a generational volitional pattern that has become an inherited temptation, suggesting that the will's range of motion may be constrained by generational idolatrous patterns. The characteristic does not eliminate volitional capacity but embeds it in a context of inherited temptation and communal pressure toward repeated defection.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The characteristic overrides volition rather than simply impairing it. The person's will is not gradually weakened (as in Characteristic 2's conscience-suppression trajectory) but suddenly and completely overridden by an external will: Luk 8:29 — "driven by the demon." This is the most extreme form of volitional impairment in the M10c cluster: the will exists but is effectively imprisoned by the spirit's domination.

---

##### T3.6.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with volition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The volitional engagement at the perimeter reveals the characteristic as morally significant without being primarily moral in its origin. The condition itself arrives through bodily mechanism, not primarily through sin of the will. But the will's response to the condition — whether it seeks remedy, maintains the duty not to transmit, exercises avoidance discipline, and pursues discernment — is where moral accountability resides within the characteristic's domain. Num 19:20 makes this structural contrast explicit: the defiled state is not the moral fault; willful refusal of remedy is.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The volitional pattern reveals the characteristic's most paradoxical feature: it binds the will while leaving the appearance of freedom intact. The person in moral-inner defilement-slavery (Rom 6:19) does not experience themselves as enslaved in the way a physically bound person does — they actively pursue their defilement (Eph 4:19: "greedily"). This reveals the characteristic as one that co-opts the will rather than simply overriding it: the will is not removed but is redirected, making the bondage feel like free activity. This is the mechanism that makes the characteristic so resistant to self-correction without external intervention.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The volitional pattern reveals the characteristic as one of repeated, deliberate corporate choice — the community is not innocently corrupted but repeatedly chooses the defilement despite divine warning (Eze 20:7: "do not defile yourselves with the idols of Egypt"; 20:18: "do not defile yourselves with their idols" — commands that are given precisely because the will could choose otherwise and repeatedly does not). The characteristic is thus a record of sustained volitional defection, not an overwhelming external force. The corporate will is the primary site of accountability.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The volitional pattern reveals the characteristic as the most acute form of will-subjugation in the cluster — not gradual erosion of conscience (Characteristic 2) or misdirection of corporate will (Characteristic 3) but sudden total override of individual will by an external spiritual agent. This addresses a dimension of human volitional vulnerability distinct from the moral-inner dimension: the human will can be externally overridden, not merely internally corrupted.

---

#### T3.7 — Agency

##### T3.7.1 — Does this characteristic engage the agency faculty — the capacity to act, initiate, and make happen — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes. Several agency-acts are directly prescribed by the characteristic's normative system: (1) washing: throughout M10c-A, the defiled person must wash clothes and bathe — active agency in pursuit of resolution (Lev 11:25, 15:5, 15:16, etc.); (2) presenting for priestly examination: the person with suspected skin disease must present themselves for assessment (M10c-B-VCG-02 — the examination procedures imply the person's presentation); (3) removing contaminated material: Lev 14:40-45 (M10c-B-VCG-04) — stones and plaster from a diseased house are actively removed; the condemned house is demolished; (4) carrying out the filth from the Holy Place: 2Ch 29:5 (M10c-A-VCG-08) — Levites are commanded to carry out impurity as a deliberate consecration act; (5) self-declaration: Lev 13:45 (M10c-B-VCG-03) — the person bears disease must actively cry out their status. Each of these is an agency-act required by the characteristic.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes, but in a distorted form. Agency — the capacity to act, initiate, and make happen — is engaged through the characteristic's call to cleansing (2Cor 7:1: "let us cleanse ourselves"; 2Cor 6:17: "go out from their midst, and be separate from them"; Isa 52:11: "purify yourselves"). The response to the characteristic requires active agency: the person must act to separate, purify, cleanse. In the negative direction, the characteristic produces a perverted agency: Eph 4:19 (VCG-02) — "greedy to practice every kind of impurity" — the person actively pursues defilement; their agency is intact but misdirected.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes, in both directions — defilement-generating agency and cleansing-agency. Defilement-generating agency: Eze 23:7 (VCG-02) — "she bestowed her whoring upon them... and she defiled herself with all the idols" — active agency in the pursuit of idolatrous defilement. Jer 7:30 (VCG-03) — the sons of Judah "set their detestable things" in God's house — deliberate agency of installation. Isa 30:22 (VCG-02) — "then you will defile your carved idols... you will scatter them as unclean things. You will say to them, 'Be gone!'" — the agency of the will actively declaring and rejecting its former idolatrous attachments. Cleansing-agency: 2Ch 23:19 (VCG-08 context) and Eze 4:14 (VCG-05) — the prophet's lifelong maintained purity through agency of avoidance.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes — the agency faculty is the most directly impaired. Luk 8:29 (VCG-01): "driven by the demon into the desert" — agency is taken over by the spirit; the person does not act, they are acted upon. Luk 9:42 (VCG-01): "the demon threw him to the ground and convulsed him" — the body is the instrument of the spirit's violent agency. Mar 5:13 (VCG-02): the spirits exercise agency (moving from the man to the pigs); during possession the man had no equivalent agency over the spirits.

---

##### T3.7.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair agency in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic structures and obligates agency without enabling or impairing it in itself. The required agency-acts (washing, presenting, removing, carrying, self-declaring) are prescribed responses that the person's agency must execute. The only point of agency-impairment evidenced is the person in the most severe defilement state (skin disease, Lev 13:46) — dwelling alone outside the camp structurally limits the person's capacity to act within the community. But this is a social consequence of the condition rather than a direct impairment of the agency faculty.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic misdirects agency rather than impairing it. The person in the moral-inner defilement-state is not passive — they actively pursue more defilement (Eph 4:19), actively avoid repentance (2Cor 12:21). Their agency is functional but oriented toward self-corruption rather than toward holiness. The characteristic produces a morally functional but directionally corrupted agency: fully active, fully misdirected.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The characteristic does not impair agency in the direct sense — the community retains full volitional and agentic capacity throughout the corpus. Rather, it misdirects agency toward defilement-generating acts (Eze 23:7 — actively pursuing idols; Jer 7:30 — deliberately installing abominations). The agency that should be directed toward sacral stewardship (guarding land, sanctuary, name) is directed toward their desecration. The characteristic's most distinctive feature of agency is Isa 30:22 (VCG-02): the future act of declaring the idols defiled — the same agency that was directed toward idolatry is redirected toward active rejection of those idols.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The characteristic suppresses and displaces the person's agency, substituting the spirit's agency for the person's own. The person's body acts under the spirit's direction, not their own. Human restraint attempts to compensate (Luk 8:29 — chains and shackles) but fails. Only divine authority expelling the spirit (Mar 5:8 — the command; Act 8:7 — expulsion) effectively restores agency (Luk 9:42 — "gave him back to his father").

---

##### T3.7.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with agency reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The extensive prescribed agency-acts reveal that the characteristic is not passive — the person in the defilement-state is not merely a subject of a condition but an active participant in its resolution. The entire remedial system (washing, waiting, examination, water of impurity, self-declaration, removal of contaminated material) requires sustained agency. This reveals the characteristic as a condition that mobilises the person's agency toward resolution — the defilement-state is designed to be managed, not simply suffered.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The agency pattern reveals the characteristic as operating through the redirection of human capacity rather than its elimination. The person in moral-inner defilement is not incapacitated but actively moving in the wrong direction. This reveals the characteristic as a condition of misdirection rather than nullification — the inner person retains agency and uses it, but under the condition of the defilement-state the direction of agency is toward corruption rather than holiness.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The agency pattern reveals the characteristic as the domain where the community's sacral stewardship responsibility is exercised or betrayed. The land, sanctuary, and divine name are entrusted to the community as objects of their agency; the corporate/covenantal defilement-state is the result of agency directed against those objects rather than in their service. The characteristic thus reveals the stakes of human agency in the covenantal domain: agency directed toward sacred objects determines their condition.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The agency pattern reveals the characteristic as uniquely agency-displacing: the person's agency is not corrupted (Characteristic 2) or misdirected (Characteristic 3) but replaced by the spirit's agency. The person becomes the site through which an alien agency operates — both present as a person and absent as an agent. This is the most radical form of agency impairment in the M10c cluster and the basis for the characteristic's classification as defilement by external agency.

---

#### T3.8 — Moral Evaluation

##### T3.8.1 — Does this characteristic engage the moral evaluation faculty — the capacity to assess against a standard of right, wrong, good, and true — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes, at the level of categorical boundary maintenance. Lev 20:25 (M10c-B-VCG-01) makes this most explicit: the command to "separate the clean beast from the unclean" functions as a moral-identity boundary — blurring it "renders the person detestable." The clean/unclean distinction is not only ritual but functions as a moral assessment: the person who maintains the distinction is assessed as walking in covenant integrity; the person who blurs it is assessed as detestable. Deu 26:14 (M10c-B-VCG-01) — the worshiper's declaration "I have not removed any of it while I was unclean" — is an integrity-assessment of one's own conduct within the ritual system. The moral evaluation faculty assesses whether the person has maintained the defilement boundaries.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes, critically. Isa 6:5 (VCG-01): the prophet's immediate moral self-evaluation in the presence of divine holiness — "I am a man of unclean lips" — is the exercise of moral evaluation applied to his own condition. Mat 23:27 (VCG-04): Jesus's pronouncement of the Woe is a moral evaluation of the hypocrites' hidden inner state — the authoritative naming of what moral evaluation should have detected. Eph 5:5 (VCG-04): "everyone who is... impure... has no inheritance" — the moral evaluation faculty here is doctrinal-normative, establishing the standard against which the characteristic is assessed.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes. The moral evaluation faculty is central to the characteristic at the institutional level. Eze 22:26 (VCG-05): priests have failed in the moral evaluation of "holy vs common, unclean vs clean" — their primary vocation is moral evaluation applied to persons, actions, and objects. Eze 44:23 (VCG-05): priests are charged with teaching the people "how to distinguish between the unclean and the clean" — the restored priestly vocation is moral evaluation and instruction. Eze 23:13 (VCG-02): "I saw that she was defiled" — God's moral evaluation of the community's condition as defiled, operating as the standard of assessment. Jer 2:23 (VCG-02): the community's self-evaluation ("I am not unclean") is contrasted with what prophetic moral evaluation reveals.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The 21-verse corpus does not evidence engagement with the moral evaluation faculty in the inhabited person. The characteristic operates through spiritual domination of will and faculties, not through distortion of moral assessment capacity. The spirits make one moral-evaluative declaration (Mar 3:11 — "You are the Son of God"), but this is the spirits' recognition of Christ's moral-ontological superiority, not the person's moral evaluation.

---

##### T3.8.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair moral evaluation in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic deepens moral evaluation in the direction of categorical precision. Lev 10:10 and 11:47 (M10c-B-VCG-01) name the cultivation of clean/unclean discernment as the purpose of the purity laws — this is a systematic deepening of the moral evaluation faculty through repeated categorical engagement. The purity system trains the person to make finer and finer moral-ritual assessments. The NT revision (Act 10:28, M10c-B-VCG-05) shows this same faculty requiring revision at a higher level: God's word requires that the moral evaluation framework (who is clean/unclean) be revised to include what had been categorically excluded.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic impairs moral evaluation in its advanced form — Tit 1:15 (VCG-03 reference): "to the defiled and unbelieving, nothing is pure; both their minds and their consciences are defiled" — the standard-setting faculty (mind) and the response-faculty (conscience) are both compromised, making moral evaluation unreliable. The person cannot correctly assess the moral character of their own condition or of the things they engage with. However, the characteristic does not simply eliminate moral evaluation: Isa 6:5 shows it still functioning at the point of encounter with holiness — the prophet's evaluation of himself as unclean remains correct. The characteristic impairs ongoing self-evaluation but not the acute recognition-event triggered by direct encounter with holiness.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The characteristic impairs moral evaluation at the institutional and personal level. Eze 22:26 (VCG-05): the collapse of priestly moral evaluation is both a symptom and a cause of the corporate defilement — the institution meant to maintain moral evaluation standards has failed. Jer 2:23 (VCG-02): the community's self-evaluation is distorted by self-deception. The characteristic also enables a future restored moral evaluation: Eze 44:23 (VCG-05) — the new priestly order will teach the people to distinguish correctly. The characteristic impairs and then restores moral evaluation as part of its eschatological trajectory.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

Not evidenced within the 21-verse corpus for the person's own moral evaluation faculty.

---

##### T3.8.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with moral evaluation reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The pervasive moral-evaluative dimension reveals that the characteristic is not morally neutral — the purity system is simultaneously a ritual system and a moral-formation system. The person who cultivates clean/unclean discernment is not merely learning ritual procedure; they are forming a moral identity. Lev 20:25 connects the clean/unclean distinction to identity ("blurring it renders the person detestable"), showing that maintaining or failing the boundary has character-level consequences. The characteristic thus reveals the moral evaluation faculty as the faculty through which the person's sacral identity is constructed and maintained.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The pattern reveals two modes of moral evaluation operating in relation to the characteristic: (1) an ongoing ambient assessment that is progressively compromised by the defilement-state (Tit 1:15 reference — nothing pure to the defiled); and (2) a crisis-recognition capacity that remains even in the advanced state, triggered by encounter with holiness (Isa 6:5). The characteristic suppresses the former but cannot fully extinguish the latter — the encounter with divine holiness can breach the callousness and produce recognition. This reveals the characteristic as not fully totalising: even in the hardened state, the potential for moral evaluation remains accessible through the encounter with holiness.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The pattern reveals moral evaluation as the institutional faculty whose failure enables the characteristic's propagation. The clean/unclean distinction is not self-evident to the community; it requires sustained institutional teaching (Eze 44:23). When the institution fails to maintain and teach this faculty (Eze 22:26), the community loses the cognitive-moral equipment needed to recognise and resist the defilement. The characteristic thus spreads in the absence of institutional moral evaluation and is resisted in its presence.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The silence reveals the characteristic as bypassing rather than corrupting the person's moral assessment capacity. Unlike Characteristics 2 and 3 (where moral self-deception and priestly failure to teach the clean/unclean distinction are part of the defilement's mechanism), Characteristic 4 does not involve the person's moral evaluation faculty — it operates below and prior to moral assessment through direct spiritual domination.

---

#### T3.9 — Conscience

##### T3.9.1 — Does this characteristic engage the conscience — the acute inner witness of sin, guilt, and conviction — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes, prominently. The most direct evidence is Lev 5:2-3 (M10c-A-VCG-01): defilement can be hidden from the person, but "when he comes to know it and realises his guilt" — the conscience awakens as the first inner response to recognition of the incurred condition. The guilt here is the conscience's naming of the defilement as a real condition that must be addressed. The Num 19:13 (M10c-A-VCG-07) formulation — "his uncleanness is still on him" — shows the conscience's awareness of an unresolved condition as a persisting reality. Act 10:14 (M10c-B-VCG-05) — Peter's conscience-level conviction that resists the divine vision — shows the conscience formed by the categorical system as itself a highly active inner witness operating at the boundary of the permitted and forbidden.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes, centrally. The conscience is the primary inner faculty engaged by Characteristic 2. 1Cor 8:7 (VCG-03): "their conscience, being weak, is defiled" — the conscience is both the faculty that is susceptible to defilement and the locus of the defilement-state in this verse. The defilement originates in the conscience itself (acting against conviction), not in an external contact. Tit 1:15 (VCG-03 reference): "their consciences are defiled" — advanced defilement has penetrated the conscience as a faculty, compromising its witness function. Isa 6:5 (VCG-01): the prophet's conscience functions correctly at the moment of divine encounter — "woe is me! For I am a man of unclean lips" — the conscience names the condition accurately.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes, at three evidenced points. (1) Prophetic confrontation of corporate conscience: Jer 2:23 (VCG-02) — the prophetic challenge ("how can you say, 'I am not unclean'?") is a direct confrontation of the community's corporate conscience, naming the gap between self-justifying claim and actual condition. (2) Individual conscience of maintained purity: Eze 4:14 (VCG-05) — "I have never defiled myself" — the prophet's conscience is active in defending his lifelong maintained purity; the conscience here functions as the inner witness of sustained integrity. (3) Corporate future conscience: Eze 20:43 (VCG-02) — the community will "loathe yourselves" — the future self-loathing is the eschatological activation of corporate conscience: a collective inner witness of guilt over the corporate defilement-state.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The 21-verse corpus does not evidence engagement with the person's conscience. The conscience — as the inner witness of sin, guilt, and conviction — is not named as active or suppressed in any of the 21 verses. The condition is not about guilt or conviction but about domination by an external spiritual force.

---

##### T3.9.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscience in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic enables and deepens conscience through categorical formation: sustained engagement with the clean/unclean system forms a conscience that is alert, specific, and responsive to the boundary conditions. Peter's Act 10:14 conviction is the product of a deeply formed conscience — it responds immediately and precisely to the vision's command. The characteristic can, however, initially appear to bypass conscience in the unconscious-defilement cases (Lev 5:2-3): defilement arrives without conscience activation. But this is not a bypass — it is a gap in the conscience's reach that the law addresses by requiring active vigilance (Lev 11:43-44, M10c-A-VCG-04) precisely because conscience cannot catch everything.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic impairs conscience progressively. In the early/acute register (1Cor 8:7, VCG-03), the defiled conscience is still functioning but is weakened: it produces guilt without the conviction needed to refuse the defiling action. In the advanced register (Eph 4:19 VCG-02 — callousness; Tit 1:15 reference VCG-03), the conscience is so compromised that it no longer produces reliable moral response. The characteristic thus operates as a progressive conscience-suppressor: early defilement weakens the conscience; sustained defilement silences it; advanced defilement corrupts it at the level of its standards.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The characteristic bypasses and suppresses corporate conscience in the present (Jer 2:23 — self-justifying denial; the community's collective conscience does not register its defilement-state). However, it positions corporate conscience as the instrument of future repentance (Eze 20:43 — the loathing is the conscience's delayed but eventual activation). The characteristic thus shows conscience as suppressible but not permanently eliminable: even after sustained suppression, the eschatological encounter with restored memory can activate the corporate conscience.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

Not evidenced within the 21-verse corpus. The characteristic bypasses conscience as a faculty — its mechanism is external invasion, not inner moral self-evaluation.

---

##### T3.9.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscience reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The conscience engagement reveals the characteristic as both a condition that precedes conscience (defilement can be incurred before awareness) and a condition that conscience must actively manage (the duty of watchfulness, the guilt-awakening, the pursuit or refusal of remedy). This reveals the characteristic as operating in a zone of creaturely vulnerability where the conscience's reach is limited and must be supplemented by vigilance discipline and by the law's own categorical provisions. The characteristic is designed to form conscience rather than simply to respond to existing conscience.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The conscience pattern reveals the characteristic as self-perpetuating through conscience-suppression: each episode of moral-inner defilement weakens the very faculty that should prevent the next episode. 1Cor 8:7 (VCG-03): the weakened conscience is defiled by the act — and a defiled conscience is weaker than before for the next moral encounter. This progressive suppression mechanism reveals the characteristic as having an intrinsic escalation tendency: it does not remain static but actively moves toward deeper entrenchment by suppressing the faculty that could interrupt the cycle.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The conscience pattern reveals the corporate defilement-state as more conscience-resistant than Characteristic 2: a whole community's collective self-justification can suppress corporate conscience more powerfully than an individual's. The prophetic voice (Jer 2:23; Hos 5:3: "I know Ephraim, and Israel is not hidden from me") operates as the external conscience-activating agency when the community's internal corporate conscience has been suppressed. This reveals the characteristic as one that requires external prophetic confrontation to interrupt the corporate conscience's suppression.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The silence confirms that Characteristic 4 is entirely distinct from Characteristics 2 and 3 in its relationship to conscience. Those characteristics involve conscience (defiled conscience at 1Cor 8:7; prophetic confrontation of corporate conscience at Jer 2:23). Characteristic 4 bypasses conscience entirely. The condition is not produced by, revealed through, or resolved by conscience — confirming the characteristic's structural distinctiveness as an external-invasion condition.

---

#### T3.10 — Conscientiousness

##### T3.10.1 — Does this characteristic engage conscientiousness — the integrated response of moral awareness, volition, and action — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes. Conscientiousness — moral awareness integrated with will and action — is engaged at every point of volitional response within the characteristic: avoidance discipline (Lev 11:43-44, M10c-A-VCG-04), washing after acquisition (M10c-A-VCG-02, -06, -07), presenting for examination (M10c-B-VCG-02), carrying out the filth from the Holy Place (2Ch 29:5, M10c-A-VCG-08), declaring one's own unclean status (Lev 13:45, M10c-B-VCG-03). Each of these integrates awareness (I am unclean / this is a defiling agent), will (I must act), and action (I wash / I present / I declare). The Deu 26:14 declaration (M10c-B-VCG-01) — "I have not removed any of it while I was unclean" — is a retrospective conscientiousness report: moral awareness, will-compliance, and action in integrity throughout a period of sacred activity.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes. Conscientiousness — the integrated response of moral awareness, volition, and action — is both called for and corrupted by this characteristic. The call to cleansing at 2Cor 7:1 (VCG-03) — "let us cleanse ourselves from every defilement of body and spirit, bringing holiness to completion" — is a call for integrated moral awareness (recognising the defilement), will (choosing to act), and action (cleansing). This is conscientiousness at its proper function. The corruption: Eph 4:19 (VCG-02) — "given themselves up to sensuality, greedy to practice every kind of impurity" — the same integrated awareness-will-action mechanism is operating but directed toward corruption rather than holiness; it is a perverted conscientiousness.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes. Conscientiousness — integrated moral awareness, will, and action — is both called for and corrupted by this characteristic. Called for: Eze 44:23/25 (VCG-05) — the restored priests must teach the clean/unclean distinction and guard their own purity — integrated moral awareness (knowing the distinctions), will (maintaining purity), and action (teaching and guarding) constitute the full conscientiousness required. Corrupted: Eze 22:3-4 (VCG-02) — the city's integrated awareness-will-action is directed toward idolatrous desecration rather than sacral stewardship; the same integrated mechanism is operative but directed toward corporate defilement.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes, through suppression in the possessed person and activation in those around them. Conscientiousness — the integrated response of moral awareness, volition, and action — is suppressed by the characteristic: Luk 8:29 (VCG-01) — the person cannot integrate their own awareness and will into directed action because the spirit overrides the will. However, conscientiousness is strongly engaged in those who respond: Mat 10:1 (VCG-03) — disciples given authority and sent; Act 5:16 (VCG-02) — people bringing their afflicted; Mar 7:25 (VCG-01) — the mother's urgent seeking.

---

##### T3.10.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscientiousness in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic deepens conscientiousness by creating a comprehensive domain of integrated awareness-will-action requirements. The purity system does not permit a merely cognitive engagement — knowing the categories without acting on them is inadequate. The required actions (washing, examining, declaring, removing) demand that awareness be integrated with will and action. The characteristic bypasses conscientiousness only in the unconscious-defilement cases (Lev 5:2-3), but even there, the conscientious response upon awareness is precisely specified.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic impairs conscientiousness in the specific domain of moral integrity while preserving a corrupted form of the same integrated functioning directed toward defilement. The callousness of Eph 4:19 (VCG-02) represents the complete impairment of moral conscientiousness — moral awareness no longer produces the volitional-action response it should. But the same person is greedy in pursuing impurity — showing that the integrated mechanism itself is intact but directed wrongly.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The characteristic impairs conscientiousness toward the sacred (the community no longer integrates awareness-will-action toward sacral stewardship) while activating a perverted conscientiousness directed toward idolatrous desecration (Eze 22:3: "a city that makes idols to defile herself" — integrated and purposeful). The characteristic thus co-opts the integrated moral mechanism and redirects it from its proper sacral end.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The characteristic suppresses conscientiousness in the possessed person while activating it in those around them. The possessed person's integrated capacity for moral-aware, willed action is replaced by the spirit's direction. The community responds with heightened conscientiousness: the mother falls at Jesus's feet (Mar 7:25), people bring their afflicted from surrounding towns (Act 5:16). The characteristic is a conscientiousness-displacing condition in the person and a conscientiousness-activating condition in the community.

---

##### T3.10.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscientiousness reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The integrated engagement of awareness-will-action reveals the characteristic as a comprehensive moral-formation system in miniature. The person who navigates the ritual defilement-state conscientiously — attending, willing, and acting correctly at each decision point — is being formed in the integration of the three components of conscientiousness. This reveals the characteristic as not merely a ritual compliance system but a vehicle for inner character formation through repeated, integrated moral-volitional-action engagement.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The pattern reveals the characteristic as co-opting the integrated moral-volitional-action mechanism rather than eliminating it. Conscientiousness toward holiness is impaired; but the same integrated mechanism is redirected toward the pursuit of defilement. This reveals the characteristic as a condition that captures human moral agency in its integrated form — it uses the person's capacity for intentional, motivated action, redirecting it from its proper end (holiness) to a corrupting end (impurity).

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The pattern reveals conscientiousness as a neutral integrated mechanism that can be directed toward either sacral stewardship (M12 register) or corporate defilement (Characteristic 3 register). The characteristic's propagation requires a fully functional integrated mechanism — the community is not passive but actively and conscientiously defiling. This reveals the characteristic as a condition of purposeful corporate moral defection, not of passive deterioration.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The pattern reveals the characteristic as generating a social-moral response system: the suppression of conscientiousness in one person activates conscientiousness in their community of care. The community's urgency to bring the afflicted for healing (Act 5:16, Act 8:7, Mar 7:25) shows that the characteristic, by disabling individual agency and conscientiousness, motivates communal moral-volitional response on behalf of the disabled person.

---

#### T3.11 — Relational Capacity

##### T3.11.1 — Does this characteristic engage the relational capacity — the constitutional equipment for genuine connection with another person — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes, substantially. The characteristic structures relational capacity in both its impairment and its positive expression. Impairment: the defilement-state severs or restricts relational participation — the person with skin disease dwells alone outside the camp (Lev 13:46, M10c-B-VCG-03); defiling persons are sent out of the camp (Num 5:2, M10c-A-VCG-07); corpse-contact defilement bars the person from communal worship (Num 9:6, M10c-A-VCG-07). The characteristic structurally limits the relational scope of the defiled person within the covenant community. Positive expression: the duty not to transmit one's defilement state (Lev 15:11, M10c-A-VCG-06 — washing hands before contact) and the public self-declaration (Lev 13:45, M10c-B-VCG-03) are relational acts that protect others. The 1Cor 7:14 (M10c-B-VCG-05) covenantal-status use shows the characteristic's relational scope extending to family relationships — the believing spouse's holiness affects the unbelieving spouse and children.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes. The characteristic operates in the relational domain in several ways. Eph 5:5 (VCG-04): the impure person "has no inheritance in the kingdom of Christ and God" — the characteristic severs the relational capacity toward God at its most fundamental level (covenantal inheritance). 2Cor 6:17 (VCG-03): "go out from their midst, and be separate from them... then I will welcome you" — the unclean condition blocks divine welcome; separation from the defiling environment is the condition for divine relational restoration. Mat 23:27 (VCG-04): the hypocrites' inner defilement is masked from human relational perception — they appear relationally acceptable to others while their inner condition makes them morally inaccessible. The characteristic thus operates both vertically (God-human relational barrier) and horizontally (human-human relational deception).

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes, as its primary domain. The characteristic is constitutively relational — it arises from the betrayal of covenantal relationships (VCG-01: sexual betrayal of marriage and family covenant), desecrates the community's relationship with its sacred environment (VCG-03/04), and severs the covenantal relationship with God (Eze 5:11 — divine withdrawal; Eze 20:31 — God refuses to be inquired of). Num 5:27-28 (VCG-01) shows the most direct relational engagement: the ordeal law is the mechanism for adjudicating whether the covenantal marital relationship has been violated; the defilement-state is the objective marker of that relational betrayal.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes, as its primary social consequence. The characteristic severs the person's relational capacity: Mar 5:2 (VCG-01) — "utterly cut off from clean, communal life"; Mar 9:25 (VCG-01) — hearing suppressed (cannot receive others' speech); Mar 1:23 (VCG-01) — the synagogue community is disrupted. Relational severance is comprehensive: the person cannot maintain normal social bonds (Mar 5:2), cannot engage in family life (Luk 9:42 — the boy must be "given back to his father"), and cannot participate in worship (Mar 1:23).

---

##### T3.11.2 — Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair relational capacity in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic primarily impairs relational access (exclusion from community and worship) while simultaneously structuring relational responsibility (the duty not to transmit, the public self-declaration). The impairment is temporary and remediable; the responsibility is ongoing. The impairment thus serves a protective relational function: the exclusion of the defiled person preserves the communal sacral integrity for others. This reveals the characteristic as managing individual-community relational boundaries rather than attacking relational capacity as such.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic impairs relational capacity toward God: Eph 5:5 (VCG-04) — no inheritance in the kingdom; 2Cor 6:17 (VCG-03) — conditional on separation from unclean things. It also bypasses honest horizontal relational capacity: Mat 23:27 (VCG-04) — the outward appearance of relational acceptability conceals the inner defilement, producing a relational persona that does not correspond to the inner condition. The characteristic thus impairs vertical relation (with God) and corrupts horizontal relation (with others) through self-concealment.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The characteristic severely impairs relational capacity at multiple levels: (1) the covenantal marital bond is broken by adultery (Num 5, VCG-01); (2) the corporate covenant with God is severed by idolatry (Eze 20:31 — "I will not be inquired of by you"; Eze 5:11 — divine withdrawal); (3) the community's relationship with its land is corrupted (Mic 2:10 — "no place to rest"); (4) the community's relationship with surrounding nations is reduced to being named "a filthy thing" (Lam 1:17) and expelled (Lam 4:15). The characteristic destroys relational bonds at every level — personal, communal, divine, and spatial.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The characteristic severely impairs relational capacity. The spirit substitutes its own relational agenda for the person's: the inhabited person's voice becomes the spirit's declaration (Mar 3:11; Mar 1:26), not the person's own relational speech. The person cannot give or receive the normal relational communications that constitute community. The restoration (Luk 6:18 — "cured"; Luk 9:42 — "gave him back to his father") restores the relational capacity as a primary feature of healing.

---

##### T3.11.3 — What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with relational capacity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The relational engagement reveals the characteristic as inherently communal — it cannot be understood as a purely individual condition. The defilement-state is always already a relational condition: it impairs the person's relationship to God (barring access to worship and divine presence), to the covenant community (exclusion from camp and sacred meals), and to specific others (the duty not to transmit). This reveals that the inner-being characteristic is not purely interior but is constituted partly by its relational structure — the condition exists within a network of relationships that it disrupts and that it calls the person to protect.

## T4 — Relational Interfaces (24 prompts)

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The relational pattern reveals the characteristic as inherently isolating: it severs the most important relational bond (with God — Eph 5:5) and distorts the human relational bond (Mat 23:27 — concealment). The positive-inverse at Rev 14:4 (VCG-05) — "they follow the Lamb wherever he goes" — shows that the absence of the characteristic is characterised by intimate relational following: the undefiled inner state enables the deepest possible relational orientation toward God. The characteristic is thus the relational barrier par excellence: its presence severs and distorts; its absence enables the most intimate God-directed following.

## T4 — Relational Interfaces (24 prompts)

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The relational pattern reveals the characteristic as the most relationally comprehensive defilement in the M10c cluster: it damages the God-community covenant (Eze 5:11/20:31), the inter-personal covenant bonds within the community (VCG-01), the community-land bond (VCG-04), the community-sanctuary bond (VCG-03), and the community-nations bond (Lam 1:17/4:15). This comprehensiveness reveals that the characteristic is fundamentally about the covenantal relational order: the community's vocation is to maintain and inhabit a network of sacred relationships (with God, with land, with sanctuary, with one another); the defilement-state is the condition of that network being systematically broken.

## T4 — Relational Interfaces (24 prompts)

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The relational pattern reveals the characteristic as constitutively isolating: possession severs the person from the relational network defining their human identity (family — Luk 9:42, community — Mar 5:2, worship assembly — Mar 1:23). The restoration is correspondingly relational — returning the person to their father (Luk 9:42), curing those "troubled" (Luk 6:18). The characteristic disrupts the social relational fabric and requires communal response and restoration.
