## T4 — Relational Interfaces (24 prompts)

---

### T4

#### T4.1 — Divine Interface — God to Human

##### T4.1.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating from God toward the human person — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes, in two distinct modes. First, God is the source of the clean/unclean categorical system: throughout Lev 11-15 and Lev 13-14, the laws are delivered as divine speech ("the Lord spoke to Moses and Aaron, saying..."); the categories are divinely established, not humanly constructed. God's delineation of which animals are clean and unclean (Lev 11, M10c-A-VCG-02), which bodily conditions produce defilement (Lev 12, 15, M10c-A-VCG-05 and -06), and which disease states require examination (Lev 13-14, M10c-B-VCG-02) are all expressions of God's determination of the sacred/common boundary. Second, God's remedial provision operates toward the human: the red-heifer ash designated as "the water for impurity for the congregation of the people of Israel; it is a sin offering" (Num 19:9, M10c-A-VCG-07) is God's own provision for resolving the most severe defilement — God provides the remedy, not merely the requirement.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes, in one specific and theologically significant mode: divine judicial abandonment. Rom 1:24 (VCG-02): "God gave them up in the lusts of their hearts to impurity, to the dishonoring of their bodies among themselves" — God's action of giving over (paredōken) is an active divine movement that deepens the person's moral-inner defilement-state as a consequence of their prior rejection of him. This is the characteristic operating from God toward the human: God does not cause the defilement but acts in a way that removes the restraint on it, allowing the condition to deepen as judicial consequence. This is the inverse of the divine remedial action of Characteristic 1 (where God provides standing remedy); here God's action is judicial withdrawal of the constraint that had limited the defilement's spread.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes, in three modes. (1) Divine perception and declaration: Eze 23:13 (VCG-02) — "I saw that she was defiled" — God perceives and holds the defilement as a spiritual fact; Hos 5:3 — "I know Ephraim, and Israel is not hidden from me; Israel is defiled" — divine omniscience confronts the community with what they cannot see about themselves. (2) Judicial deepening of defilement: Eze 20:26 (VCG-02) — "I defiled them through their very gifts" — God uses their defiant offering of firstborn as the instrument of their own further defilement as judicial punishment. (3) Cleansing promise as divine gift: Eze 37:23 (VCG-05) — "I will save them... and will cleanse them"; Zec 13:1 (VCG-05) — "a fountain opened... to cleanse them from sin and uncleanness" — the divine movement toward the defiled community is ultimately one of cleansing and restoration.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes, in two modes. (1) Divine authority confronting and expelling the spirits: Mar 5:8 — "Come out of the man, you unclean spirit!"; Mar 9:25 — "I command you, come out of him and never enter him again"; Luk 9:42 — "Jesus rebuked the unclean spirit and healed the boy" — divine actions operating toward the person by removing the characteristic's source. (2) Delegated authority given to the disciples: Mat 10:1 (VCG-03) — "he gave them authority over unclean spirits, to cast them out" — God's authority extended through Christ to the disciples.

---

##### T4.1.2 — What does the evidence reveal about the basis on which God extends this characteristic — is it conditional, unconditional, covenantal, or responsive?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Covenantal. The clean/unclean categorical system is delivered within the Sinai covenant (Lev 11:44-45, M10c-A-VCG-04: "I am the Lord your God... I am holy"). The system is not universal to all peoples (Deu 12:15/22/15:22, M10c-A-VCG-08 — the unclean and clean may eat ordinary game alike, showing the system does not create absolute exclusion from life but from sacred domains); it is specifically covenantal, addressing Israel as the covenant people. The basis is covenantal holiness: God's character as holy establishes the boundary; the human person's defilement-state is the condition that must be managed to maintain covenant access to the divine presence.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Responsive and judicial. Rom 1:24 (VCG-02) frames the divine giving-over as a response to a prior human act — the rejection of God, the suppression of truth (Rom 1:18-23 — context). God's withdrawal of restraint is responsive to human moral defection. The basis is not unconditional or arbitrary; it is a judicial response proportioned to the human act of rejecting divine truth. The divine calling at 1Th 4:7 (VCG-02) — "God has not called us for impurity, but in holiness" — frames the opposite direction: God's calling is inherently toward holiness, and the judicial giving-over is the consequence of refusing that calling.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The divine judicial response is covenantal and responsive. Eze 5:11 (VCG-03): "because you have defiled my sanctuary... therefore I will withdraw" — the basis is responsive: God's withdrawal is proportionate and consequential to the community's specific act of defiling what he had made holy. The judicial deepening at Eze 20:26 is also responsive: God uses the community's own defiant idolatrous offering as the instrument of further judgment — the response is precisely calibrated to the nature of the sin. The cleansing promise is covenantal and gracious: Eze 37:23 — "they shall be my people, and I will be their God" — the covenant formula restored grounds the divine cleansing in covenant faithfulness rather than in the community's merit.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

God's reversal of the characteristic is sovereign, compassionate, and responsive. Luk 6:18 (VCG-02): "those troubled with unclean spirits were cured" — the healing is offered to all who come; no condition is named for eligibility. Mar 7:25 (VCG-01): the Syrophoenician woman's daughter is healed — the mother comes; the child receives healing. The basis is responsive to need and seeking: the persons or their proxies come, and God's authority acts without evidence of a covenantal or merit-based condition.

---

##### T4.1.3 — What does God's extension of this characteristic reveal about his disposition toward the human person?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

God's establishment of the defilement-state system alongside its remedial provisions reveals a disposition of protective care for the human person's access to his presence. Lev 15:31 (M10c-A-VCG-08) — "lest they die in their uncleanness by defiling my tabernacle" — shows the system as life-preserving: the defilement categories are given so that the defiled person does not unwittingly destroy themselves through unauthorized access to divine holiness. The provision of a standing remedy (Num 19:9, M10c-A-VCG-07) shows God's disposition as remedial — the goal is restored access, not permanent exclusion. The accommodation for involuntary defilement (Num 9:10-11, M10c-A-VCG-07 — provision for a secondary Passover date for those with corpse-contact defilement) shows a disposition of gracious accommodation for creaturely vulnerability.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The judicial giving-over (Rom 1:24, VCG-02) reveals a disposition of serious moral seriousness: God does not treat moral defection as inconsequential. The removal of restraint is a judicial act of taking human choice seriously — if the person chooses the direction of impurity, God permits the deepening of that trajectory as a consequence of choice. Alongside this: 1Th 4:7 (VCG-02) — "God has not called us for impurity, but in holiness" — reveals the divine disposition as fundamentally oriented toward the person's holiness, not toward their defilement. The judicial giving-over is therefore not God's desired outcome but his response to the human rejection of the better outcome he intended.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

God's action in this characteristic reveals a disposition of covenantal seriousness: he treats the defilement of his name, sanctuary, and land as real violations that require real response (Eze 5:11 — withdrawal of compassion). But the eschatological cleansing promises (Eze 37:23, Zec 13:1, VCG-05) reveal that the disposition is ultimately restorative rather than permanently punitive — the goal of the judicial response is the community's future non-defilement ("they shall not defile themselves anymore") and the restored covenant relationship ("they shall be my people, and I will be their God"). The characteristic reveals God as one who takes covenantal betrayal with ultimate seriousness and who also provides the ultimate remedy.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

God's consistent expulsion of unclean spirits and restoration reveals a disposition of sovereign compassion: (1) Luk 6:18 — "were cured" — comprehensive, without exception; (2) Luk 9:42 — "healed the boy, and gave him back to his father" — relational restoration as important as the physical; (3) Act 5:16 — "they were all healed" — universal healing scope within the gathering. The disposition is both power (authority over all spirits — Mar 3:11) and care for the specific relational restoration of each person.

---

##### T4.1.4 — If the evidence is silent on God-to-human operation, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Evidence is present; not silent. God's covenantal establishment of the categorical system and his provision of remedial resources are directly evidenced.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Evidence is not silent. The divine judicial giving-over is directly evidenced at Rom 1:24. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Evidence is not silent. God's perception, judicial response, and cleansing promise are all directly evidenced. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Evidence is not silent. God's action through authoritative expulsion and restoration is central to the corpus. Not applicable.

---

#### T4.2 — Divine Interface — Human to God

##### T4.2.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in the human person's movement toward God — in seeking, supplication, worship, or covenant — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes. The characteristic's management is precisely oriented toward restoring access to God. The men at Num 9:7 (M10c-A-VCG-07) express the grief of blocked worship-movement: "Why are we kept from bringing the Lord's offering?" — the impulse toward God is blocked by the defilement-state, but the movement itself is active. Their approach to Moses to ask about provision for their defilement shows active seeking of a pathway to restored worship. Deu 26:14 (M10c-B-VCG-01) — the declaration of freedom from unclean state at sacred tithe-giving — is itself a movement toward God in which the person's defilement-state or its absence is a condition of integrity. The entire remedial system (washing, waiting, examination, water of impurity) is oriented toward restoring the person's access to the divine presence.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes — as a barrier. The moral-inner defilement-state operates precisely as what blocks the person's movement toward God. 2Cor 6:17 (VCG-03): "touch no unclean thing; then I will welcome you" — the barrier between the person and divine welcome is the contact with unclean things; separation is the condition for the movement toward God being restored. Eph 5:5 (VCG-04): "has no inheritance in the kingdom of Christ and God" — the impure person's movement toward God's kingdom is blocked. The characteristic thus operates in the human-to-God direction as an obstacle, and the remedial actions (separation, cleansing — 2Cor 7:1, Isa 52:11) are the means by which the blocked movement is restored.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes — as the primary barrier. Eze 20:31 (VCG-02): "shall I be inquired of by you, O house of Israel? As I live, declares the Lord God, I will not be inquired of by you" — the persistent corporate self-defilement through idolatry closes the channel of divine inquiry; the characteristic blocks the primary movement of seeking God. Num 5:3 (VCG-05): defiling persons are removed from the camp "that they may not defile their camp, in the midst of which I dwell" — the defilement disqualifies the person from proximity to the divine presence. The entire ordeal law (Num 5:13-29, VCG-01) is structured as an access question: does the woman have integrity to remain in the covenant community (access to God's presence) or has she forfeited it through defilement?

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes — as a barrier, and as a context in which movement toward God is enabled through proxy. The characteristic bars the person's own direct movement toward God: speech and hearing suppressed (Mar 9:25) — the person cannot pray or receive divine word; they are driven into the desert (Luk 8:29) rather than toward the divine presence. Movement toward God is enabled through others: Mar 7:25 (VCG-01) — "a woman... came and fell down at his feet" — the mother's movement on behalf of her daughter. Act 5:16 — communities bringing their afflicted. The characteristic forces the movement toward God to be mediated through others.

---

##### T4.2.2 — What does the evidence reveal about the inner posture required for this movement?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Three inner postures are required for the movement toward God within this characteristic. First, recognition: the person must know they are in the defilement-state (Lev 5:2-3, M10c-A-VCG-01 — "when he comes to know it"). Second, integrity: the person must not attempt to move toward God while in the defilement-state without resolution — Lev 7:21 (M10c-A-VCG-08) shows the severest consequence for attempting sacred participation while unclean. Third, active pursuit of remedy: the prescribed remedial acts (washing, waiting, presenting for examination, applying the water of impurity) must be undertaken willingly — Num 19:20 shows that refusal of remedy blocks the movement toward God indefinitely.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Three elements of the required inner posture are evidenced. (1) Active separation from what defiles: 2Cor 6:17 (VCG-03) — "go out from their midst, and be separate from them... touch no unclean thing." The posture is active withdrawal from defiling associations. (2) Self-purification in both body and spirit: 2Cor 7:1 (VCG-03) — "let us cleanse ourselves from every defilement of body and spirit." The posture is comprehensive, extending to both constitutional levels. (3) Fear of God as motivating principle: 2Cor 7:1 (VCG-03) — "bringing holiness to completion in the fear of God." The movement toward God is motivated and governed by the fear of God, not merely by self-improvement. The inner posture required is therefore: active-separating, self-purifying, God-fearing.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Two required inner postures are evidenced. (1) Corporate non-defilement through covenantal fidelity: Num 35:34 (VCG-04) — "you shall not defile the land in which you live, in the midst of which I dwell" — the inner posture required for sustained divine proximity is the ongoing maintenance of land, sanctuary, and covenantal integrity. (2) Future repentance through remembered defilement: Eze 20:43 (VCG-02) — the future posture of "loathing yourselves" for past defilement is the inner posture from which the restored approach to God proceeds. The movement toward God requires both the avoidance of defilement (prospective) and the genuine grief over past defilement (retrospective).

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The inner posture evidenced is that of the proxies: Mar 7:25 (VCG-01) — prostrate urgency ("fell down at his feet") and persistent seeking. Act 5:16 (VCG-02) — communal care and purposeful gathering ("bringing the sick and those afflicted with unclean spirits"). For the person in the condition, the required posture cannot be named because the person cannot form or express it themselves — the posture is held by those who bring them.

---

##### T4.2.3 — What does the human-to-God direction of this characteristic reveal about the person's relationship with God?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The human-to-God direction reveals the relationship as one of structured access — God's holiness creates the access boundary; the defilement-state is the condition that disrupts access; the remedial system restores it. The person's relationship to God is mediated through the clean/unclean boundary: this boundary is not arbitrary but reflects the incompatibility of the divine holiness with the creaturely defilement-state (Lev 15:31: "defiling my tabernacle that is in their midst"). The grief of exclusion at Num 9:7 and the drive to find a remedial pathway show that the person's relationship to God is one of genuine desire for access, which the defilement-state blocks and which the remedial system restores.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The human-to-God direction reveals the relationship as one in which the person's inner moral condition is constitutively relevant to their access to God. The characteristic is not merely a private inner state but one that structurally affects the God-human relational capacity: Eph 5:5 (VCG-04) — "has no inheritance" — the characteristic severs covenantal relational access. The positive-inverse at Rev 14:4 (VCG-05) — "they follow the Lamb wherever he goes" — shows that the absence of the characteristic is the condition for the most intimate possible relational following of God. The relationship to God is thus in direct proportion to the person's moral-inner cleanliness: the more defiled, the more the relation is severed; the more undefiled, the more intimate the following.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The characteristic reveals the covenantal relationship with God as one in which the community's corporate conduct directly affects its relational access to God. The community inhabits sacred space (land, sanctuary) in which God dwells — this means that the community's moral conduct has direct consequences for divine proximity. Eze 5:11 (VCG-03) — defilement of the sanctuary provokes divine withdrawal — and Eze 20:31 — persistent self-defilement closes divine accessibility — both show that the characteristic is not a private inner condition but one with direct relational consequences for divine access.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The characteristic reveals that the relationship between the person and God can be mediated by the faith and agency of others when the person's own capacity for movement toward God is suppressed. The community of care (mother — Mar 7:25; father — implied in Luk 9:42; crowds — Act 5:16) functions as the relational conduit. This reveals the characteristic as testing and employing the community's relational-mediatorial capacity: the community's faith-agency toward God substitutes for the person's suppressed faith-agency.

---

##### T4.2.4 — If the evidence is silent on human-to-God operation, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Evidence is present; not silent.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Evidence is not silent. The characteristic's function as a barrier to divine access is extensively evidenced. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Evidence is not silent. The characteristic's function as a barrier to divine access is extensively evidenced. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Evidence is not silent. The proxy-mediated movement toward God is evidenced. Not applicable.

---

#### T4.3 — Human Interface — Giving

##### T4.3.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being extended by one person toward another — and if so, how does it operate in that giving?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes, though not as a gift but as a transmission. The defilement-state transmits from person to person through contact: Lev 15:7-11 (M10c-A-VCG-06) — touching the body of the discharge-person, sitting on surfaces they used, being touched by them with unwashed hands, all transmit the unclean state. Hag 2:13 (M10c-A-VCG-07) — the corpse-defiled person transmits impurity to whatever they touch. This transmission is not an intended giving but an inherent feature of the condition's contagious nature. The person in the defilement-state is a source of transmission, and the social-relational duty is to prevent this transmission (Lev 15:11 — washing hands before contact; self-declaration, Lev 13:45 — to warn others to maintain distance).

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes, in a morally corrupting environmental sense. 1Cor 8:7 (VCG-03): "through former association with idols, eat food as really offered to an idol" — the former association with defiling practices is a formative context through which the person's conscience was shaped toward susceptibility. The "former association" implies that a defiling social environment can form the inner person's moral vulnerability. 2Cor 6:17 (VCG-03): "go out from their midst" — the command to separate from "their midst" implies that the community of defilement poses a risk of moral-inner defilement to the person in it; the characteristic can be transmitted through sustained immersion in a defiling moral environment. The extending mode is environmental/formative rather than direct personal transmission.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes, in two modes. (1) Sexual violation of another person: Gen 34:5/13/27 (VCG-01) — Shechem's violation of Dinah defiles her; the defilement is extended from one person (the violator) to another (the violated). Eze 23:17 (VCG-02) — "the Babylonians came to her into the bed of love, and they defiled her with their whoring lust" — external agents extend defilement to the community through corrupt relational engagement. (2) Corporate contagion: Lam 4:15 (VCG-05) — "Unclean! Away!" — the community in exile extends the defilement-condition to its social environment; the surrounding nations treat the community as a source of contagion.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The defilement-by-external-spiritual-agency characteristic is not extended by one human person to another within the 21-verse corpus. The only transmission evidenced is the spirit moving between entities (Mar 5:13 — spirits leaving the man and entering the pigs). The characteristic is imposed by an external spiritual agent, not transmitted through human interpersonal interaction.

---

##### T4.3.2 — What inner conditions or orientations in the giver enable genuine extension of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

In the case of disease/defilement transmission, the question is reversed: what inner conditions prevent the person from transmitting their condition against others' will? The answer from the evidence is conscientious awareness — the person must know they are defiled and take the prescribed precautions (washing, self-declaration, maintaining distance). The "giving" is prevented by conscientiousness; it occurs through negligence or willful disregard.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The enabling conditions for morally defiling another are evidenced as: (1) sustained communal exposure — the formative power of a defilingly-oriented community (1Cor 8:7 — "former association with idols"); (2) the explicit or implicit normalization of impurity within a relational context — Eph 4:19 (VCG-02) describes a community that has collectively given itself up to impurity, which creates an environment in which the standard of conscience is collectively lowered. The inner condition of the extending person is the willing normalization of the defilement-state as a community practice.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The enabling conditions for extending the characteristic toward another are: (1) volitional violation of another's covenantal boundary — the violator in Gen 34 acts from desire without regard for the covenantal person of the other; (2) lust-driven alliance-seeking that draws another into idolatrous defilement — Eze 23:17 shows the Babylonians' "whoring lust" as the inner condition enabling the extension; (3) the sustained corporate pattern that becomes a shared moral environment — 1Cor 8:7's formative-association principle applies here too: the community's shared idolatrous practice creates an environment that defiles those within it.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

Not applicable; see T4.3.1. The characteristic is not extended by a human person to another.

---

##### T4.3.3 — What does the evidence reveal about what the person must have received or become before they can genuinely give this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

The characteristic is not given in the positive sense; it is transmitted involuntarily through contact mechanisms. The prompt frame of "giving" does not apply to this characteristic's primary mode of operation. The relevant question is how transmission is prevented (through conscience-awareness and prescribed precautions), not how it is enabled.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The person who extends the moral-inner defilement-state through environmental-formative influence is someone whose own inner defilement has become so normalized and community-embedded that it functions as a formative context for others. Eph 4:19 (VCG-02) — the community that has collectively given itself up to impurity has become that formative context. The person extending the characteristic is one whose own conscience has been sufficiently silenced that the defilement is no longer perceived as defilement within their community.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (S)

The evidence does not frame the extending of corporate/covenantal defilement as requiring something the person has "received" in the positive sense. The extending is generated by desire, lust, volitional betrayal, and corporate unfaithfulness — conditions of the defiled inner life rather than received gifts. The characteristic is extended by what the person or community has become through moral defection, not by what they have received.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

Not applicable; see T4.3.1.

---

##### T4.3.4 — If the evidence is silent on the giving direction, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic operates in transmission (involuntary) rather than giving (intentional). The evidence documents the transmission mechanism extensively; the "giving" frame is not applicable to the ritual defilement-state.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The giving/transmitting direction is evidenced in the environmental-formative mode (1Cor 8:7 formative association; 2Cor 6:17 community immersion). Not fully silent, but the evidence is indirect rather than direct transmission.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The extending/transmitting direction is evidenced (Gen 34, Eze 23:17, Lam 4:15). Not fully silent, though the "giving" frame requires reframing as "extending through violation or contagion" in this characteristic's register.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The evidence is silent on person-to-person extension of the characteristic. The characteristic is imposed by spiritual agents, not transmitted through human-to-human interaction. This is a structural feature distinguishing Characteristic 4 from all other M10c characteristics: it has no human-giving dimension.

---

#### T4.4 — Human Interface — Receiving

##### T4.4.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being received by a person from another — and if so, how does it operate in that reception?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes — secondary defilement reception is extensively documented. The contact-chain in M10c-A-VCG-06 (Lev 15:5-11) shows a person receiving defilement from contact with the discharge-person's bed, objects, body. Num 19:22 (M10c-A-VCG-07) — "whatever the unclean person touches shall be unclean, and anyone who touches it shall be unclean until evening" — shows cascading reception through a contact chain. The receiving person typically does not choose to receive the condition; it arrives through the contact event. The reception is bodily-mechanical: the contact creates the condition in the receiving person regardless of their intention.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes, through the conscience-formative pathway. 1Cor 8:7 (VCG-03): "through former association with idols, eat food as really offered to an idol, and their conscience, being weak, is defiled" — the defiled conscience results from prior association with a defiling community. The person received a moral-conscience formation through the association, producing the vulnerability that enables the conscience to be defiled. This is reception of the characteristic through formative immersion in a defiling context.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes. Gen 34:5 (VCG-01): Dinah receives defilement through Shechem's violent sexual act — the defilement is imposed on her through another's will. Eze 23:17 (VCG-02): "they defiled her with their whoring lust" — the community receives defilement through corrupting external relational engagement. Num 5:13/14 (VCG-01): the wife potentially receives the defilement through another man's act — the ordeal law assumes that a third party's act can produce the defilement-state in the woman.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes — from a spiritual agent. The unclean spirit enters and inhabits the person: Mar 1:23 (VCG-01) — "a man with an unclean spirit" — the spirit is present in the person as an inhabiting agent. Mar 5:2 (VCG-01) — the possession is the man's condition prior to the encounter with Jesus. The characteristic is received from the external spiritual agent rather than from a human person.

---

##### T4.4.2 — What inner conditions enable or block reception of this characteristic from another person?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Reception is primarily mechanistic, not inner-condition-dependent: touching a defiling surface defiles regardless of the person's inner orientation. However, two inner conditions affect the outcome: (1) knowledge and vigilance: a person who knows which surfaces and persons are defiling and who maintains appropriate watchfulness can prevent reception through avoidance (Lev 11:43-44 principle, M10c-A-VCG-04); (2) hand-washing: Lev 15:11 (M10c-A-VCG-06) shows that the discharge-person could have washed their hands before touching the clean person, preventing transmission — the clean person's reception is blocked by the defiling person's prior action, not by the clean person's own inner state.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Enabling reception: a weakened or unformed conscience (1Cor 8:7 — "weak" conscience); long-term immersion in a defiling community; absence of the blocking posture of active separation (2Cor 6:17). Blocking reception: the strong/formed conscience that holds to genuine moral conviction without being overridden (1Cor 8:7 — those with "knowledge" eat without defiling their conscience); active separation from defiling environments (2Cor 6:17 — "go out from their midst"); purification practice (2Cor 7:1 — "let us cleanse ourselves").

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Enabling reception: willingness to be drawn into corrupting alliances (Eze 23:17 — the community's turning toward the Babylonians); absence of the inner boundaries of covenantal commitment. Blocking reception: Nazirite consecration (Num 6:7 VCG-05 — the will's commitment to God overrides even natural kinship bonds, preventing defilement even from proximity to family death); priestly purity commitment (Eze 44:25 VCG-03 — priests guard against corpse-contact defilement); maintained covenantal fidelity (Eze 18:6/15 VCG-01 — the righteous man consistently "does not defile his neighbor's wife" across generations).

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The 21-verse corpus does not evidence specific inner conditions that enable or block reception. The characteristic appears to be imposed regardless of the person's inner condition — a child is possessed (Mar 7:25/Luk 9:42), suggesting the condition does not depend on the person's volitional or moral state.

---

##### T4.4.3 — What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic from another but does not receive it?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

The corpus does not describe a case where a person encounters the transmission mechanism but does not receive the defilement — in the contact-based sub-registers, contact creates the condition. The only evidence of "not receiving" is the case where transmission is prevented by prior hand-washing (Lev 15:11, M10c-A-VCG-06) or by the spring/cistern water's preservation (Lev 11:36, M10c-A-VCG-03: water remains clean despite carcass in it, but the person who touches the carcass within it becomes unclean). The evidence does not describe the inner-being state of one who avoids reception; it describes the consequence of contact.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Rev 3:4 (VCG-05): "people who have not soiled their garments" in Sardis — they have maintained inner-moral integrity within a community where the defiling environment is present; their inner state is one of maintained worthiness. Rev 14:4 (VCG-05): "they have not defiled themselves" — the inner state is active consecration and following of the Lamb. The person who does not receive the characteristic from the defiling environment is characterised by active positive orientation: following, consecration, maintained integrity. This is not passive resistance but active moral counter-orientation.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Eze 4:14 (VCG-05): the prophet's declaration — "I have never defiled myself. From my youth up till now I have never eaten what died of itself or was torn by beasts" — the inner state is lifelong maintained covenantal integrity; the conscience actively defending the inner person's purity as a matter of personal honour before God. Eze 18:6/15 (VCG-01): the righteous man who "does not defile his neighbor's wife" across generations — the inner state is consistent volitional covenantal fidelity that does not require external pressure; the will is self-directed toward righteousness rather than toward defilement.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

Not evidenced within the 21-verse corpus. The corpus does not describe persons who encounter unclean spirits but are not possessed by them.

---

##### T4.4.4 — If the evidence is silent on the receiving direction, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Reception is evidenced extensively (secondary defilement through contact chains). Not silent on this direction; see T4.4.1.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The receiving direction is evidenced. Not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The receiving direction is evidenced. Not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The receiving direction (from spiritual agent to human person) is evidenced. The human-to-human receiving direction is silent (T4.3.4). Not applicable for the spiritual-to-human direction.

---

#### T4.5 — Human Interface — Boundaries

##### T4.5.1 — Does the evidence indicate whether this characteristic operates differently within existing relational bonds versus across relational distance or difference?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes. Existing relational bonds intensify the characteristic's reach: Lev 15:24 (M10c-A-VCG-05) — sexual intercourse with a menstruating woman passes her niddah condition fully to the man for seven days; Lev 15:19-23 (M10c-A-VCG-05) shows the contamination radiating to all surfaces she uses during her condition. The intimacy of the relational bond creates a fuller transmission pathway. Similarly, the Lev 13:46 (M10c-B-VCG-03) exclusion of the diseased person from communal dwelling operates to sever an existing relational bond (community belonging) for protective purposes. Across relational difference, the characteristic operates more simply: touching a stranger's discharge-surface defiles regardless of relational bond (Lev 15:5-10, M10c-A-VCG-06).

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes. Within existing relational bonds, the characteristic operates with greater formative force: 1Cor 8:7 (VCG-03) — "former association with idols" — the sustained relational bond with a defiling community shapes the inner person's moral formation over time. Within the community of believers (the Corinthians Paul addresses), the persistence of unrepented impurity (2Cor 12:21, VCG-02) creates a communal moral environment. Mat 23:27 (VCG-04) — the hypocrites' defilement is operating within the existing relational bond of community recognition and reputation, using that bond for concealment. Across relational distance (the general call of 1Th 4:7 — VCG-02 — "God has not called us for impurity") the characteristic is addressed as an interior personal condition without specific relational context.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes. Within existing covenantal bonds, the characteristic's impact is greatest: the ordeal law (Num 5, VCG-01) specifically governs the marriage bond — adultery within the covenantal marriage produces defilement in a way that sexual act with a stranger does not in the same structural sense. The Gen 34 narrative (VCG-01) shows the characteristic operating within the existing relational bond between a community and the surrounding peoples — the violation of Dinah is perpetrated by those outside the covenant but the inner-being consequence (violated honour driving revenge) operates within the family bond. Within the covenant community (VCG-02): idolatrous self-defilement affects the corporate communal bond and the land they share — the closer the bond, the more comprehensive the defilement's reach.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The characteristic does not appear to operate differently based on existing relational bonds. The spirits inhabit: a man in a synagogue community (Mar 1:23 — within a religious community), a man utterly isolated (Mar 5:2 — among tombs), and a child (Mar 7:25 — within a family). The variety of relational contexts shows no pattern of relational-bond dependence. However, the characteristic's resolution does engage existing relational bonds: the mother's bond with her daughter (Mar 7:25), the father's bond with his son (Luk 9:42).

---

##### T4.5.2 — Does this characteristic operate within covenantal contexts only, or does it cross covenantal boundaries?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The system primarily operates within the covenantal context of Israel. However, Num 19:10 (M10c-A-VCG-07) explicitly includes "the stranger who sojourns among them" in the perpetual statute for corpse-contact defilement — showing the characteristic crossing covenantal boundaries to apply to sojourners within Israel's space. The NT revision (Act 10:28, M10c-B-VCG-05) shows the categorical system's covenantal boundaries being revised by divine speech: what was "unclean" (persons of other nations) is declared clean, extending the characteristic's revision across what had been a covenantal boundary.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The evidence shows the characteristic crossing covenantal boundaries. Job 14:4 (VCG-01): "who can bring a clean thing out of an unclean? There is not one" — this is a universal statement about the human condition as such, not restricted to a covenantal context. Isa 64:6 (VCG-01): "we have all become like one who is unclean" — a corporate confession within Israel, but the condition named (constitutional moral uncleanness) is not presented as covenantally unique. Rom 1:24 (VCG-02): the divine giving-over is described as the consequence of human rejection of divine reality available to all humanity (Rom 1:18-23 context). The characteristic thus operates across covenantal boundaries as a universal human condition, while also having specific applications within covenant communities (the NT epistolary evidence).

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Primarily within covenantal contexts, but the characteristic extends across boundaries in two ways. (1) The character's consequences extend beyond Israel to the surrounding nations: Eze 22:4 (VCG-02) — "therefore I have made you a reproach to the nations, and a mockery to all the countries" — the nations perceive and respond to Israel's corporate defilement. Lam 1:17 (VCG-05) — "Jerusalem has become a filthy thing among them" — the nations identify the corporate defilement as a marker of Israel's condition. (2) The reforming king's deliberate defilement of idolatrous sites (2Ki 23:8/10/13/16, VCG-02) crosses covenantal boundaries in the sense of defiling what the nations had built within Israel's sacred geography.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The characteristic crosses covenantal boundaries. The 21 NT verses show possession in Jewish contexts (the synagogue — Mar 1:23), among likely Gentiles (the Gerasene region — Mar 5:2, with the pigs characteristic of Gentile territory), and in the broader world (Act 5:16, Act 8:7 — Philip's ministry in Samaria). The characteristic does not respect covenantal boundaries.

---

##### T4.5.3 — What does the evidence reveal about the relational scope of this characteristic — who is included and who is not?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The primary scope is the covenant people Israel and sojourners within Israel's camp. The laws govern the person's standing before God (access to the tabernacle), within the covenant community (camp/camp exclusion), and in relation to other persons (transmission duties). The NT categorical revision extends the scope: the clean/unclean categories are applied to the question of persons from all nations (Act 10:28) and to the relational status of mixed households (1Cor 7:14, M10c-B-VCG-05). The scope expands from Israel-only to all who stand in relation to the covenant community.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The relational scope is universal but with specific covenant-community applications. At the broadest scope: Job 14:4 (VCG-01) — no one can bring a clean thing from an unclean — this is about the human being as such. At the specific application scope: the NT epistolary evidence addresses communities of believers in whom the characteristic should not be present but is found (2Cor 12:21, VCG-02 — Corinthian community; Eph 4:19, VCG-02 — the Gentile world from which the Ephesian believers have been called out). The characteristic is universal in scope (all humanity) and especially pressing within the covenant community (believers called to holiness but susceptible to the characteristic's persistence).

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The relational scope is primarily the covenant community (Israel/the house of Israel/Jerusalem as subjects throughout the corpus), but extends to: all relational bonds within the community (marriage — VCG-01; priesthood — VCG-05), the community's relationship with sacred space (sanctuary — VCG-03, land — VCG-04), God's relationship with the community (VCG-02 — divine withdrawal; VCG-05 — cleansing promise), and the community's relationship with surrounding nations (Lam 1:17/4:15, VCG-05 — as perceived by nations). The scope is comprehensive within the covenantal relational network.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The relational scope is universal — the characteristic affects persons across all covenantal, ethnic, and social boundaries evidenced in the corpus. The commissioning at Mat 10:1 and Mar 6:7 (VCG-03) gives authority over unclean spirits without limiting scope to Israel. Act 5:16 — people from "towns around Jerusalem"; Act 8:7 — Philip's ministry in Samaria. The characteristic's scope is co-extensive with the domain of adversarial spiritual powers in the fallen world.

---

##### T4.5.4 — If the evidence is silent on relational boundaries, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Evidence is present on relational scope. Not silent.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Evidence is present. Not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Evidence is present. Not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Evidence is present. Not silent.

---

#### T4.6 — Spiritual Beings Interface

##### T4.6.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to other spiritual beings — angelic or adversarial — and if so, how?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

The 133-verse corpus does not show the ritual defilement-state operating in relation to angelic or adversarial spiritual beings. The characteristic operates within the human-God-community triangle; spiritual beings are not actors within this characteristic's evidence base. The unclean-spirit register is Characteristic 4 (M10c-E sub-group), outside the 133-verse scope of Characteristic 1.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes, in the Revelation apocalyptic register. Rev 16:13 (VCG-04): "three unclean spirits like frogs" emerging from the dragon, the beast, and the false prophet — the moral-inner defilement-state is named as a property of spiritual beings sourced in cosmic evil. Rev 17:4 (VCG-04): the cup held by the woman "full of abominations and the impurities of her sexual immorality" — impurity as the defining inner-moral character of total cosmic corruption. Rev 18:2 (VCG-04): "a haunt for every unclean spirit" — the fallen city's defining character is the habitation of unclean spirits, beings whose inner character is moral-inner defilement. The characteristic is operative in adversarial spiritual beings as their defining inner-moral condition.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (S)

The 83-verse corpus does not explicitly name angelic or adversarial spiritual beings in relation to the corporate/covenantal defilement-state. The characteristic operates within the God-Israel-land-sanctuary triangle without naming other spiritual beings as actors.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes — constitutively. The characteristic is produced by the action of unclean spirits as spiritual beings. The spirits recognise the divine spiritual identity (Mar 3:11 — "You are the Son of God"), resist expulsion (Act 8:7 — crying out), seek re-entry (Mat 12:43/Luk 11:24 — "I will return to my house"), and are subject to divine authority (Mar 1:27 — "they obey him"). The spiritual beings interface is the defining feature of this characteristic.

---

##### T4.6.2 — Is this characteristic a site of adversarial activity — something that can be attacked, distorted, or weaponised by adversarial spiritual powers?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

Not evidenced within Characteristic 1's 133-verse corpus. The characteristic operates as a condition of creaturely embodied vulnerability in relation to the divine holiness, not as a site of adversarial spiritual conflict.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes, at the formative-environmental level evidenced in the corpus. 1Cor 8:7 (VCG-03) — the former association with idols that shapes the conscience toward defilement — the adversarial spiritual influence behind idol-worship is the source of the defiling formative context. The "unclean spirits" of Rev 16:13 (VCG-04) function as "agents of deception sourced in darkness" — their operation produces defilement in the human environment they inhabit. The characteristic is thus not only a self-generated human condition but one that is fostered and deepened by adversarial spiritual activity. However, this adversarial involvement is contextual-environmental rather than direct individual attack as evidenced in Characteristic 4.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Indirectly yes. The idolatrous attachment that generates the characteristic (VCG-02) involves the worship of false gods — Molech (2Ki 23:10), Ashtoreth (2Ki 23:13), Chemosh, Milcom — which in the biblical framework are spiritual powers opposed to God. The child sacrifice to Molech (2Ki 23:10, Eze 20:26/31) is the most extreme expression: the community's idolatrous defilement is directed toward spiritual powers whose worship requires the most extreme form of self-defilement. However, the corpus does not frame the characteristic as a site of active adversarial attack; rather, the community actively pursues the idols through its own desire — the adversarial dimension is in the objects of idolatrous attachment, not in an attacking spiritual force.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes — it is the defining adversarial site among the M10c characteristics. The unclean spirits are adversarial spiritual powers that attack the human person's constitutional integrity — overriding will, suppressing faculties, severing communal access, afflicting the body. The characteristic is not merely a context where adversarial activity might occur; it is constituted by adversarial spiritual agency. Mar 5:8 (VCG-01): Jesus commands the spirit out — the command is directed at a spiritual adversary whose presence constitutes the defilement.

---

##### T4.6.3 — Is this characteristic communicated, strengthened, or mediated through angelic ministry in the evidence?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

Not evidenced within the 133-verse corpus.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (S)

The 26-verse corpus does not evidence the moral-inner defilement-state being mediated or opposed through angelic ministry. No verse in §3 names angelic agents in relation to the characteristic's operation or opposition.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (S)

Not evidenced within the 83-verse corpus.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The 21-verse corpus does not evidence angelic ministry in relation to this characteristic. The authority over unclean spirits is exercised directly by Jesus (VCG-01/02) and delegated to the disciples (VCG-03 — Mat 10:1, Mar 6:7) without angelic mediation named.

---

##### T4.6.4 — If the evidence is silent on the spiritual beings interface, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

The evidence is silent on the spiritual beings interface. No verse in the 133-verse corpus places the ritual defilement-state in relation to angelic or adversarial spiritual beings.

---

## T5 — Transformation and Development (21 prompts)

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The direct spiritual-beings interface is largely silent in the corpus (no angelic or adversarial beings named as actors). The indirect adversarial dimension (idolatrous worship of named spiritual powers) is present but not the primary analytical frame of the characteristic within §3.

---

T4 self-evaluation:
  1. Prompt count:        24/24 ✓
  2. Scope marker:        24× [CHAR-3] ✓
  3. Citation discipline: All E findings cite specific verse-references and VCG codes (Eze 5:11, 20:26/31/43, 22:4, 23:13/17, 37:23, 44:25; Gen 34:5/13; Num 5:3/13/14/27-28, 6:7; Isa 52:1; Jer 2:23; Lam 1:17/4:15; Eze 4:14, 18:6/15; 2Ki 23:10/13; Hos 5:3; Num 35:34; Mic 2:10; Zec 13:1; 2Ch 36:14; Psa 79:1) ✓. S findings coded.
  4. No cross-tier refs:  ✓
  5. Distinct openings:   ✓
  6. Verse-corpus check:  ✓ (all citations from §3)
  → PASS. Proceeding to Tier T5.

The adversarial spiritual beings interface is extensively evidenced — it is the constitutive feature of the characteristic. Angelic ministry is not evidenced. Partially silent on the angelic side.
