## T5 — Transformation and Development (21 prompts)

---

### T5

#### T5.1 — Nature of Transformation

##### T5.1.1 — Does this characteristic produce transformation in the person — and if so, does it change the person's condition, the person's orientation to their condition, or both?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes, the characteristic produces transformation in the person's condition. The defilement-state is a condition-change: from clean to unclean (at acquisition) and from unclean to clean again (at resolution). The entire remedial system — washing, waiting, examination, water of impurity — is a structured sequence of condition-transformation. The transformation is primarily of the person's condition (their sacral standing within the covenant community), not of their deeper character or orientation per se. However, the orientation is also transformed in the formative register: sustained engagement with the clean/unclean system over a lifetime forms the person's orientation toward sacral vigilance, as evidenced in Peter's Act 10:14 conviction (M10c-B-VCG-05) — his orientation has been transformed by a lifetime of categorical formation.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes, in both directions: the defilement-state transforms the person downward through progressive moral deterioration, and the call to cleansing represents a transformative reversal. The deterioration trajectory is documented at Rom 1:24 (VCG-02) — "gave them up to impurity, to the dishonoring of their bodies"; Rom 6:19 (VCG-02) — "lawlessness leading to more lawlessness"; Eph 4:19 (VCG-02) — "become callous... greedy to practice every kind of impurity." Each verse shows a different stage of a downward condition-transformation in the inner person. The reversal trajectory is named at 2Cor 7:1 (VCG-03) — "let us cleanse ourselves from every defilement of body and spirit, bringing holiness to completion" — a transformation in orientation from defilement to holiness. The characteristic thus produces transformation in both the person's condition (deteriorating) and their orientation (if the call is heeded, reversing toward holiness).

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes, in both directions. The characteristic transforms the community's condition downward (land contaminated, sanctuary desecrated, covenant severed, community expelled) and has a designed reversal in the eschatological register (Eze 37:23 — "they shall not defile themselves anymore"; Zec 13:1 — fountain of cleansing). The transformation of condition (land, sanctuary, divine name from holy to defiled) is thoroughly documented in VCGs -02, -03, -04. The transformation of orientation is evidenced in Eze 20:43 (VCG-02): the community will remember and loathe — their orientation toward their own past will be transformed from self-justifying denial (Jer 2:23) to self-loathing (Eze 20:43). Both condition-change and orientation-change are evidenced.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes, in both directions. Downward transformation: the spirit's seizure transforms the person's condition comprehensively — will overridden (Luk 8:29), faculties suppressed (Mar 9:25), communal belonging severed (Mar 5:2), bodily agency displaced (Luk 9:42). Upward restoration: the expulsion reverses the transformation — Luk 6:18 (VCG-02): "were cured"; Luk 9:42 (VCG-01): "healed the boy, and gave him back to his father"; Act 5:16 (VCG-02): "they were all healed." The characteristic changes the person's condition (defilement-state) and their communal orientation (given back to the father).

---

##### T5.1.2 — Is the transformation produced by this characteristic reversible or irreversible in the verse evidence?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Primarily reversible. The standard defilement pattern — "shall be unclean until the evening; then it shall be clean" (Lev 11:24 and throughout M10c-A-VCG-02, -05, -06) — is structurally reversible. The corpse-contact defilement (seven-day, M10c-A-VCG-07) is more severe but still resolved through the prescribed remedy (Num 19:19-20). However, irreversible sub-cases exist: (1) earthenware vessels that must be broken (Lev 11:33, M10c-A-VCG-03) — irreversible for that object; (2) condemned diseased house demolished (Lev 14:44-45, M10c-B-VCG-04) — irreversible for that structure; (3) willful non-cleansing resulting in excision from the assembly (Num 19:20, M10c-A-VCG-07) — the social consequence is irreversible in that moment. The reversibility pattern applies to persons; the irreversibility applies to certain objects and to the social consequence of willful non-remedy.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Primarily reversible within the 26-verse corpus's frame. The call to cleansing (2Cor 7:1, VCG-03) and separation (2Cor 6:17, VCG-03) presupposes reversibility — the imperative only makes sense if the condition can be changed. 1Th 4:7 (VCG-02) — "God has not called us for impurity, but in holiness" — the divine calling toward holiness implies the person can respond and be transformed. The threat of unrepentance at 2Cor 12:21 (VCG-02) — Paul fears those who "have not repented" — shows that repentance remains available; the condition is not named as irreversible. The Eph 5:5 (VCG-04) exclusion from inheritance is a warning about the current state, not a declaration of permanent irreversibility. The characteristic is serious and escalating, but within the 26-verse corpus it is not framed as permanently irreversible.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Primarily reversible at the eschatological level, though some specific consequences are irreversible within the historical frame. Reversible: Eze 37:23 (VCG-05) — "they shall not defile themselves anymore... and will cleanse them" — divine cleansing reverses the condition; Zec 13:1 (VCG-05) — the fountain of cleansing. Historically irreversible consequences: the destruction of the temple (Psa 79:1, VCG-03), the desecration of idolatrous altars by Josiah (2Ki 23, VCG-02 — these sites are deliberately permanently desecrated), the exile as a historical event. However, the exilic condition itself is treated as reversible through restoration: Isa 52:1 (VCG-05) — the holy city will no longer admit the unclean. The defilement is reversible at the deepest level through divine cleansing, even where specific historical consequences cannot be undone.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Fully reversible through divine authority. Luk 6:18 — "were cured"; Act 5:16 — "were all healed" — complete restoration implies reversibility. Mat 12:43/Luk 11:24 (VCG-02) — the spirit seeks re-entry after expulsion — potential vulnerability to re-possession noted, but this is a dynamic of spiritual vulnerability rather than irreversibility of the initial restoration. Mar 9:25 (VCG-01): "never enter him again" — the command against re-entry explicitly addresses the reversibility concern.

---

##### T5.1.3 — If the evidence is silent on transformation, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Transformation is evidenced. Not silent.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Transformation is extensively evidenced. Not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Transformation is extensively evidenced. Not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Transformation (both into the condition and out of it) is evidenced. Not silent.

---

#### T5.2 — Sequence of Inner States

##### T5.2.1 — Does the verse evidence describe a sequence of inner states through which this characteristic moves the person — a before, during, and after?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes. The sequence is evidenced most completely in the corpse-contact sub-register (M10c-A-VCG-07) and the skin-disease sub-register (M10c-B-VCG-02/03). For corpse-contact: before — clean, eligible for worship participation; during — unclean, barred from community access, the condition "still on him" (Num 19:13), grief at exclusion (Num 9:7); after — clean, access restored through the prescribed sprinkling and washing (Num 19:19). The sequence is: clean → defilement-event → condition imposed → conscience-awareness (Lev 5:2-3) → will-engagement (pursue remedy or refuse) → remedy applied (washing, waiting, sprinkling) → condition resolved → clean restored. For the disease register: the sequence includes a longer "during" of examination, verdict, isolation, and waiting (Lev 13-14, M10c-B-VCG-02/03).

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes. The sequence most fully documented in the corpus runs through VCG-02: (1) Heart-level desire generated internally (Rom 1:24 — "lusts of their hearts"); (2) divine judicial withdrawal as response to prior rejection (Rom 1:24 — "God gave them up"); (3) the condition of impurity entered as the result (Rom 1:24 — "to impurity"); (4) bodily dishonour as the external expression (Rom 1:24 — "dishonoring of their bodies"); (5) escalation — lawlessness generates more lawlessness (Rom 6:19 — "leading to more lawlessness"); (6) conscience silenced — callousness (Eph 4:19 — "become callous"); (7) active moral appetite substituting for suppressed conscience (Eph 4:19 — "greedy to practice every kind of impurity"). The positive-inverse sequence (VCG-05) runs: not defiling oneself (Rev 14:4) → following the Lamb → being redeemed as firstfruits → eschatological fullness.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes. The prophetic corpus (especially Ezekiel) documents a clear sequence. (1) Corporate covenantal fidelity as the baseline (Eze 18:6 — the righteous man who does not defile). (2) Inner desire-driven departure toward idols (Eze 20:7/18/30/31 — the repeated commands against defiling with Egypt's/fathers' idols, showing a persistent pull). (3) Corporate acts of defiling — idols installed in sanctuary (Jer 7:30), whoredom with nations (Eze 23:7), sexual violations within community (Eze 22:11). (4) Corporate defilement-state established — land contaminated (Eze 36:17/18), sanctuary desecrated (Eze 5:11), name defiled (Eze 43:8), divine presence withdrawn (Eze 5:11). (5) Judgment and exile — community expelled (Lam 4:15), named "a filthy thing" (Lam 1:17), eating unclean food in Assyria (Hos 9:3). (6) Eschatological restoration — memory triggers self-loathing (Eze 20:43), divine cleansing promised (Eze 37:23, Zec 13:1), holy city restored (Isa 52:1).

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes. Three stages across VCGs -01, -02, -03. (1) Pre-possession: the person in their proper self-possessed state (implied by what the spirit disrupts — communal life severed in Mar 5:2 implies prior communal belonging; family relationship disrupted in Luk 9:42 implies prior intact family bond). (2) Possessed/defiled: the condition of domination, faculty-suppression, communal severance, and bodily subjugation — Mar 1:23, Mar 5:2, Mar 7:25, Mar 9:25, Luk 4:33, Luk 8:29, Luk 9:42. (3) Restored/whole: the healed state after expulsion — Luk 6:18 ("cured"), Luk 9:42 ("healed... gave him back to his father"), Act 5:16 ("all healed").

---

##### T5.2.2 — What are those states, and what does the sequence reveal about how this characteristic works?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The three inner states are: (1) Clean — the baseline state of sacral eligibility and community belonging; (2) Defiled — the acquired condition of ritual uncleanness, with its consequences of exclusion and constraint; (3) Restored-clean — the condition after successful completion of the prescribed remedy. The sequence reveals the characteristic as inherently dynamic and oriented toward resolution: the defilement-state is not designed as a permanent condition but as a temporary disruption with a structured pathway back to the clean state. The sequence also reveals the will's critical position at the transition from defiled to restored: the will must engage the remedy for the sequence to complete. The refusal of remedy (Num 19:20, M10c-A-VCG-07) freezes the person in the "defiled" state indefinitely.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The descending sequence (Rom 1:24 → Eph 4:19) reveals the characteristic as an escalating cycle: each stage deepens the next, and the escalation is self-reinforcing through conscience-suppression. The states are: (1) desired impurity; (2) judicial release into impurity; (3) active impurity as condition; (4) bodily expression; (5) escalating lawlessness; (6) hardened conscience; (7) appetitive pursuit of more defilement. The sequence reveals the characteristic as having an internal momentum — once the defilement-state is entered and unchecked, it does not remain static but moves toward deeper entrenchment through the suppression of its own corrective mechanism (conscience).

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The six states are: (1) covenantal fidelity (positive baseline); (2) desire-directed idolatrous attachment (inner departure); (3) corporate acts of defilement (volitional defection); (4) the defilement-state as established condition (corporate contamination of land, sanctuary, name); (5) exile and expulsion as consequence; (6) memory-generated self-loathing and divine cleansing as eschatological resolution. The sequence reveals the characteristic as a covenantal arc: it begins in covenant fidelity, departs through desire and will, accumulates as a condition of sacred-space contamination, reaches its consequence in exile, and ends in the eschatological restoration that the defilement's memory enables. The arc is not merely punitive but restorative — exile is not the end; the memory of defilement in exile is the beginning of the return.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The three states: (1) wholeness (self-possessed, communally situated, faculties intact — the implied baseline); (2) spirit-dominated defilement (will overridden, faculties suppressed, communal life severed — VCG-01); (3) restored wholeness (healed, faculties returned, communal restoration — VCG-02). The sequence reveals the characteristic as a disruption of wholeness that can be definitively reversed. The movement from wholeness through defilement to restored wholeness forms the narrative arc of every possession-expulsion account in the corpus.

---

##### T5.2.3 — If the evidence is silent on sequence, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Sequence is evidenced. Not silent.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Sequence is evidenced. Not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Sequence is extensively evidenced across the prophetic corpus. Not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Sequence is evidenced. Not silent.

---

#### T5.3 — Mechanism of Change

##### T5.3.1 — What mechanism does this characteristic use to produce change in the person — discipline, encounter, gradual formation, sudden transformation, or something else?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Multiple mechanisms are evidenced. (1) Contact-event (sudden): defilement is typically acquired in a moment — touching a carcass, semen emission, proximity to a corpse (M10c-A-VCG-02, -06, -07). The condition change is sudden and immediate. (2) Progressive diagnosis (gradual): the leprous-disease sub-register (M10c-B-VCG-02) involves repeated examination over time — seven-day confinement, re-examination, verdict escalation or resolution. The change in condition is mediated through a diagnostic process over time. (3) Disciplined formation (gradual): the clean/unclean categorical system itself operates through gradual formation — the person is shaped over a lifetime into a person with categorical discernment (M10c-B-VCG-01: Lev 10:10, 11:47, 14:57). (4) Prescribed remedy (structured sequence): the transition from defiled to clean requires a prescribed sequence (washing, waiting, sprinkling), not a single transformative event.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Three mechanisms are evidenced. (1) Judicial release: Rom 1:24 (VCG-02) — God "gave them up" — the removal of divine restraint allows the characteristic's natural escalation momentum to operate unchecked; the mechanism is divine judicial withdrawal. (2) Conscience suppression through repetition: Eph 4:19 (VCG-02) — "become callous" — the gradual mechanism of repeated violations of conscience until it no longer registers; this is a gradual-formation mechanism. (3) Self-surrender: Eph 4:19 (VCG-02) — "have given themselves up to sensuality" — a volitional act of self-surrender that unlocks the characteristic's depth; the mechanism is voluntary.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Multiple mechanisms are evidenced. (1) Gradual accumulation through habitual conduct: Eze 36:17 (VCG-04) — "they defiled it by their ways and their deeds" — the land defilement is produced by accumulated habitual conduct over time. 2Ch 36:14 (VCG-03) — "exceedingly unfaithful, following all the abominations of the nations" — persistent, habitual following. (2) Deliberate will-act: Jer 7:30 (VCG-03) — the sons of Judah "set their detestable things in the house... to defile it" — a specific intentional act produces the defilement. (3) Judicial release: Eze 20:26 (VCG-02) — God "defiled them through their very gifts" — divine judicial use of the community's own defiant worship as the instrument of further defilement. (4) Eschatological memory: Eze 20:43 (VCG-02) — "there you shall remember" — memory as the mechanism of eschatological repentance-transformation.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The characteristic produces its downward change through sudden spiritual invasion: Luk 8:29 (VCG-01) — "many a time it had seized him"; Luk 9:42 (VCG-01) — "the demon threw him to the ground." The mechanism is sudden and external, not gradual or volitional. The restoration is produced through authoritative divine command: Mar 5:8 — "Come out of the man, you unclean spirit!"; Mar 9:25 — "I command you, come out of him." Both mechanisms are immediate and event-like rather than gradual.

---

##### T5.3.2 — Does the evidence distinguish between mechanisms in different contexts?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes. The mechanism differs by sub-register: the carcass/discharge/corpse contact sub-registers (M10c-A-VCG-02, -06, -07) use contact-event mechanism for acquisition and washing/waiting mechanism for resolution. The disease sub-register (M10c-B-VCG-02) uses progressive diagnosis and examination. The categorical formation sub-register (M10c-B-VCG-01) uses gradual disciplined formation. The mechanisms are not interchangeable — each sub-register has its own mechanism appropriate to its subject matter.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes. The judicial mechanism (Rom 1:24, VCG-02) operates at the theological level — God's active response to prior human defection. The gradual-formation mechanism (Eph 4:19 — callousness) operates at the natural-developmental level — the inner person changes through repeated exposure without sudden event. The volitional surrender mechanism (Eph 4:19 — "given themselves up") operates at the level of a decisive inner act. The conscience-defilement mechanism (1Cor 8:7, VCG-03) operates at the level of a specific act against inner conviction. Each mechanism operates in a different contextual register.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes. In the legal context (VCG-01: Num 5, Lev 18): a specific volitional sexual act is the mechanism of defilement acquisition — the change is immediate. In the prophetic corporate context (VCG-02: Eze, Hos): gradual accumulation through habitual unfaithfulness is the mechanism — the change is developmental. In the sanctuary context (VCG-03: Jer, Eze): deliberate installation of abominations is the mechanism — the change is both intentional and immediate. In the eschatological context (VCG-05): divine cleansing and corporate memory are the mechanisms of reversal.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes. The downward mechanism (spirit seizure) varies in duration: Luk 8:29 — "many a time it had seized him" (prolonged, repeated); Mar 7:25 — the child has been in this state before the mother seeks help (duration implied). The restoration mechanism is consistently immediate: the command is spoken; the spirit departs (Mar 1:26 — immediately; Act 8:7 — upon the ministry). The downward change can be prolonged and episodic; the restoration is immediate upon divine authority engagement.

---

##### T5.3.3 — If the evidence is silent on mechanism, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Mechanisms are evidenced. Not silent.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Mechanisms are evidenced. Not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Mechanisms are evidenced. Not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Mechanisms are evidenced. Not silent.

---

#### T5.4 — Suffering and Affliction

##### T5.4.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to suffering or affliction — as a response to it, a product of it, or a context for it?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes. Skin disease (leprous disease — M10c-B-VCG-02/03) is inherently a context of suffering: the disease itself is afflicting; the enforced isolation ("he shall live alone; his dwelling shall be outside the camp," Lev 13:46) adds relational suffering to physical. Lev 13:45 (M10c-B-VCG-03) — the requirement to wear torn clothes and let the hair hang loose — reflects mourning practices, placing the diseased person's state within a register of grief-marking. The men at Num 9:7 (M10c-A-VCG-07) experience the defilement-state as a form of grief-affliction: the loss of worship access is the suffering. The defilement-state is not a product of suffering — it is a condition that produces or accompanies suffering, particularly in the disease and exclusion registers.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The relationship to suffering is evidenced in the pastoral register. 2Cor 12:21 (VCG-02): Paul anticipates mourning "over many of those who sinned earlier and have not repented of the impurity" — Paul's suffering is the response to encountering the unrepented moral-inner defilement-state in his community. The characteristic produces suffering in those who perceive it clearly (the pastor), while the person in the defilement-state may not experience suffering proportional to their condition (callousness suppressing the grief response — Eph 4:19). The characteristic's relation to suffering is thus inverted from the normal: those with clearer moral perception suffer more when encountering the condition; those in the condition suffer less as they harden.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes, substantially. The exile register (VCG-05) documents the suffering produced by the corporate/covenantal defilement-state. Lam 1:17 (VCG-05) — "Jerusalem... has become a filthy thing among them" — the suffering of corporate shame and abandonment. Lam 4:15 (VCG-05) — "Unclean! Away!" — the suffering of expulsion. Eze 4:13 (VCG-05) — "thus shall the people of Israel eat their bread unclean, among the nations where I will drive them" — the suffering of eating unclean food in foreign lands as the divinely ordained consequence. The defilement-state produces suffering as its consequence in the exile; the suffering is both judicial (deserved) and formative (designed to lead to the memory of Eze 20:43).

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes, centrally. Act 5:16 (VCG-02): "the sick and those afflicted with unclean spirits" — the characteristic is explicitly paired with sickness as a form of affliction. Luk 6:18 (VCG-02): "those troubled with unclean spirits were cured" — "troubled" names distress and suffering. Luk 8:29 (VCG-01): "kept under guard and bound with chains and shackles" — the social management of the condition was itself a form of suffering. Mar 7:25 (VCG-01): the mother's prostrate urgency reveals the suffering the child's condition produces in the family.

---

##### T5.4.2 — Does suffering deepen, test, reveal, or produce this characteristic in the person?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Suffering does not produce the defilement-state; the bodily mechanism or verdict does. But suffering (the exclusion, the isolation, the grief of blocked worship) reveals the person's inner orientation toward the characteristic: the Num 9:7 men, whose grief at exclusion is named, reveal by their grief that their will is directed toward worship rather than away from it. Their suffering under the defilement-state is evidence of their sacral orientation — they care about worship access. Suffering thus reveals, rather than produces, the characteristic's inner significance for the person.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (S)

The 26-verse corpus does not directly evidence suffering as a mechanism that deepens, tests, reveals, or produces the moral-inner defilement-state. The characteristic is generated through desire, habitual sin, judicial release, and formative context — not through suffering directly. The corpus does not show affliction as either exacerbating or revealing the characteristic in the way that Characteristic 1 shows grief at exclusion (Num 9:7 — not in this corpus).

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Suffering reveals the characteristic by exposing what the community could not see when it was in denial. The suffering of exile (Lam 1:17/4:15, Eze 4:13, VCG-05) is the context in which the community's defilement becomes publicly visible and undeniable — what was hidden in the denial of Jer 2:23 ("I am not unclean") is now exposed. Eze 20:43 (VCG-02) shows that the suffering of exile will produce the memory that activates self-loathing and repentance — suffering does not merely reveal the characteristic but becomes the mechanism of the characteristic's resolution through memory.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

The 21-verse corpus does not evidence suffering as a mechanism that produces or deepens the characteristic. The characteristic is imposed by the spirit's agency regardless of the person's suffering state. Suffering is the consequence of the characteristic, not a contributor to its arrival or intensification.

---

##### T5.4.3 — If the evidence is silent on the relationship to suffering, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Suffering is evidenced as a context and consequence of the defilement-state, particularly in the disease and exclusion sub-registers. Not silent.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The evidence is partially evidenced (pastoral suffering as response to the condition) and partially silent (suffering as producing or revealing the condition). The primary direction evidenced is the characteristic producing suffering in the perceptive observer (2Cor 12:21), not the characteristic being revealed by the person's own suffering.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Suffering as consequence and formative mechanism is evidenced. Not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Suffering as consequence is evidenced (Act 5:16, Luk 6:18, Luk 8:29, Mar 7:25). Suffering as producer of the characteristic is not evidenced. Not fully silent.

---

#### T5.5 — Formation and Sanctification

##### T5.5.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic participating in the longer arc of character formation and sanctification — shaping the person over time toward greater likeness?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes, through the formative mechanism of the categorical system. The purity laws as a whole are framed by Lev 11:44-45 (M10c-A-VCG-04) as a participation in divine holiness: "be holy, for I am holy." The engagement with the clean/unclean system over a lifetime — learning the categories, exercising discernment, managing the defilement-state through prescribed remedies — forms the person in the orientation of sacral holiness. Lev 10:10 and 11:47 (M10c-B-VCG-01) explicitly frame the purpose of all purity laws as cultivating the discernment faculty — this is a formation goal, not merely a compliance requirement. The Deu 26:14 integrity declaration (M10c-B-VCG-01) shows the formation's fruit: a person who can declare, at the point of sacred giving, that they have maintained purity throughout the period of sacred activity.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes, as what sanctification moves the person away from. 1Th 4:7 (VCG-02): "God has not called us for impurity, but in holiness" — the sanctification arc is the movement away from the characteristic toward holiness. Rom 6:19 (VCG-02): "just as you once presented your members as slaves to impurity and to lawlessness... so now present your members as slaves to righteousness leading to sanctification" — the explicit contrast of the pre-sanctification condition (moral-inner defilement-state) and the sanctification arc (righteousness leading to sanctification). The characteristic marks the beginning of the arc from which the person is being formed away; its resolution is not a one-time event but a sustained "bringing holiness to completion" (2Cor 7:1, VCG-03).

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes, through the eschatological restoration register. The corporate/covenantal defilement-state participates in the sanctification arc as what the covenant community is being formed away from — the arc moves from defilement to holiness. Eze 37:23 (VCG-05): "they shall not defile themselves anymore with their idols and their detestable things... and they shall be my people, and I will be their God" — the promised covenant restoration is the positive fullness toward which the arc moves; the defilement-state is the departure point. Eze 44:23 (VCG-05): the restored priests will "teach my people the difference between the holy and the common, and show them how to distinguish between the unclean and the clean" — institutional formation in the clean/unclean distinction is the ongoing sanctification curriculum of the restored community.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes, through its position in the kingdom-of-God arc. Mat 10:1 (VCG-03): the authority over unclean spirits is given alongside the commission to "heal every disease and every affliction" — both form part of the kingdom announcement. The expulsion of unclean spirits is part of the disciples' mission and evidence of the kingdom's presence. Each expulsion is both a specific act of restoration and a formative event for the witnessing community (the amazement at Luk 4:36 and Mar 1:27 shapes communities' understanding of Jesus's identity).

---

##### T5.5.2 — What does the evidence reveal about the role of this characteristic in that longer arc?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic's role in the formation arc is as a recurring discipline — the management of the defilement-state is not a one-time event but a lifelong practice. Each episode of defilement (carcass-contact, discharge, disease) and each episode of cleansing (washing, waiting, remedy) is a repetition within the formation discipline. Over time, this repetition forms the person in: sacral vigilance (habitual attention to what may defile); conscience-alertness (readiness to recognise the condition when incurred); willingness to pursue remedy rather than resist it; and the discernment capacity (knowing the categorical system well enough to navigate it correctly). The characteristic forms the person not through a single transformative event but through accumulated practice.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic functions as the negative pole of the sanctification arc — it is what the person is being formed away from (Rom 6:19, VCG-02), and its progressive resolution is the content of the formative arc toward holiness. 2Cor 7:1 (VCG-03) — "bringing holiness to completion" — names the positive endpoint of the arc of which the moral-inner defilement-state is the departure point. The characteristic's role in the sanctification arc is thus as the condition that defines the starting point and the ongoing adversary of the formation process; its weakening as conscience is restored and the will is re-oriented toward righteousness is the substance of sanctification.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The characteristic functions in the formation arc in two ways: (1) as the condition that exile and suffering must address — the community's memory of defilement (Eze 20:43) is designed to produce the self-loathing that begins the repentance arc; (2) as the contrast condition that gives the eschatological restoration its positive content — the promise of "they shall not defile themselves anymore" (Eze 37:23) is meaningful only against the background of what the community has been. The characteristic thus serves the formation arc by providing both the negative basis (what must be left behind) and the eschatological contrast (what the restoration will look like).

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The characteristic functions in the formation arc as the domain in which Christ's authority over adversarial spiritual powers is demonstrated and delegated (Mat 10:1, Mar 6:7 VCG-03). Each expulsion is both a specific act of restoration for one person and a formative event for the witnessing community (Mar 1:27 — "they were all amazed"; Luk 4:36 — "they were all amazed and said... 'What is this word?'"). The characteristic participates in the formation arc by providing occasions in which the community's understanding of Christ's authority is shaped.

---

##### T5.5.3 — If the evidence is silent on formation and sanctification, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Formation and sanctification are evidenced. Not silent.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Formation and sanctification are evidenced as the arc from which the characteristic is the departure point. Not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Formation and sanctification are evidenced. Not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Formation of the disciples and witnessing communities is evidenced through the authority-commissioning and amazement registers. Not silent.

---

#### T5.6 — Eschatological Trajectory

##### T5.6.1 — Does the verse evidence point this characteristic toward an eschatological fullness — a future state toward which its present operation is oriented?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes, at two evidenced points. First, the red-heifer remedy (Num 19:9, M10c-A-VCG-07) as a "sin offering" designated for "the congregation of the people of Israel" as a perpetual provision anticipates a permanent resolution beyond what the ritual can provide within the corpus itself — it points to a cleansing economy beyond the current age. Second, the NT categorical revision (Act 10:28, M10c-B-VCG-05) — "what God has made clean, do not call unclean" — is itself an eschatological declaration: the old-covenant categorical system is being transformed by the inbreaking of the new, showing that the current ritual defilement structure is provisional. The present operation of the characteristic is oriented toward a future fullness in which the categories themselves are either fulfilled or transcended.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes, explicitly. Rev 3:4 (VCG-05): "people who have not soiled their garments... will walk with me in white, for they are worthy" — the eschatological fullness is walking with Christ in white; the present non-defilement is oriented toward this future state. Rev 14:4 (VCG-05): "redeemed from mankind as firstfruits for God and the Lamb" — the present non-defilement is oriented toward an eschatological identification as firstfruits for God. Isa 35:8 (VCG-05): the Way of Holiness — the "unclean shall not pass over it" — is an eschatological-restorative highway from which the morally unclean are excluded, showing that the eschatological fullness is characterised by the complete absence of the characteristic.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes, explicitly and substantially. Three eschatological promises address the characteristic directly. Eze 37:23 (VCG-05): "they shall not defile themselves anymore with their idols and their detestable things, or with any of their transgressions. But I will save them from all the backslidings in which they have sinned, and will cleanse them; and they shall be my people, and I will be their God" — comprehensive eschatological restoration in which the defilement-state is permanently ended. Isa 52:1 (VCG-05): "there shall no more come into you the uncircumcised and the unclean" — the holy city permanently excludes the defiling condition. Zec 13:1 (VCG-05): "a fountain opened for the house of David and the inhabitants of Jerusalem, to cleanse them from sin and uncleanness" — the divinely provided fountain of permanent cleansing.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes. (1) Mar 9:25 (VCG-01): "never enter him again" — the command against re-entry points toward an eschatological fullness in which such spirits have no permanent access to persons. (2) Mat 12:43/Luk 11:24 (VCG-02) — the spirit "passing through waterless places seeking rest, and finding none" — implies an eschatological state in which the spirit finds no place of rest at all, its domain permanently eliminated. The present expulsions are anticipations of the final comprehensive defeat of all adversarial spiritual powers.

---

##### T5.6.2 — What does the present experience of this characteristic anticipate about its future fullness?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The present experience of the defilement-state — the structured cycle of acquisition, conscience-awakening, remedy, and restoration — anticipates a future in which the need for management is no longer present: a state of unrestricted access to divine presence, without the bodily vulnerabilities of death-contact and discharge. The red-heifer provision's framing as a "sin offering" (Num 19:9) anticipates a sacrifice that resolves the defilement problem at a deeper level than the ritual can achieve. The Act 10:28 revision anticipates a community in which the relational exclusions built into the ritual system are overcome.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The present moral-inner defilement-state (in the negative form) and the present non-defilement (in the positive-inverse form of VCG-05) both anticipate the eschatological state. The present defilement anticipates exclusion from the eschatological fullness (Eph 5:5 — no inheritance; Isa 35:8 — cannot pass over the Way of Holiness). The present non-defilement anticipates inclusion in the eschatological fullness (Rev 3:4 — walk with Christ in white; Rev 14:4 — firstfruits for God and the Lamb). The eschatological fullness is the permanent, unreversible establishment of the moral-inner clean state — the completion of holiness (2Cor 7:1) that the present process of cleansing anticipates.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The present corporate/covenantal defilement-state (in the pre-exilic and exilic registers) anticipates the eschatological fullness of permanent non-defilement, restored covenant relationship, and purified sacred community. The present memory of defilement in exile (Eze 20:43 — self-loathing) anticipates the future community's humility before God in the restoration. The present defilement of land, sanctuary, and name anticipates their eschatological purification (Isa 52:1 — holy city; Zec 13:1 — cleansing fountain). The present state thus anticipates the fullness precisely through the contrast it provides: the depth of the defilement reveals the scope of the cleansing required and promised.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The present experience of expulsion and restoration anticipates an eschatological fullness of permanent wholeness — a community of persons in which no unclean spirit can inhabit, control, or defile. Each healing (Luk 6:18 — "were cured"; Act 5:16 — "all healed"; Luk 9:42 — "healed... gave him back to his father") is a present anticipation of the fullness in which the characteristic has no domain. The commissioned authority of Mat 10:1 and Mar 6:7 (VCG-03) anticipates the eschatological complete authority over all adversarial spiritual powers that the kingdom's consummation will bring.

---

##### T5.6.3 — If the evidence is silent on eschatological trajectory, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Eschatological trajectory is evidenced at two points. Not silent.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Eschatological trajectory is evidenced. Not silent.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Eschatological trajectory is explicitly and substantially evidenced. Not silent.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Eschatological trajectory is evidenced. Not silent.

---

#### T5.7 — Deposit Consequence

##### T5.7.1 — Where T2.8 has identified a constitutional deposit from sustained operation of this characteristic, what developmental consequence does that deposit produce over time?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

T2.8 found no constitutional deposit in the body from the ritual defilement-state. The characteristic is structured as a temporary, resolvable condition, not one that leaves a lasting constitutional trace. T5.7 is closed on this basis.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

T2.8 identified a constitutional hardening (callousness of conscience — Eph 4:19, VCG-02) as the deposit of sustained moral-inner defilement. The developmental consequence: progressive moral blindness — the ability to perceive one's own condition correctly is progressively lost (Tit 1:15 reference in VCG-03 — "to the defiled and unbelieving, nothing is pure; both their minds and their consciences are defiled"). The deposit produces: (1) increased susceptibility to further defilement (each act of defilement weakens the conscience further, making the next act easier); (2) distorted moral cognition (the mind cannot correctly assess purity); (3) entrenched unrepentance (2Cor 12:21, VCG-02 — those who "have not repented").

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

T2.8 identified a sustained corporate-generational deposit: the community's collective moral identity becomes constitutively defiled over time, and the generational pattern of idolatrous defection (Eze 20:30 — "after the manner of your fathers") is a transmitted pattern. The developmental consequence: (1) generational entrenching of idolatrous practice — each generation inherits the pattern of the previous (Eze 20:18 — children warned not to defile as their fathers did; 20:30 — warning that the pattern is repeating). (2) The corporate moral identity as publicly defiled — Eze 22:5 (VCG-05): "your name is defiled" — the community's name becomes a marker of defilement known to all nations. (3) Institutional collapse — Eze 22:26 (VCG-05): the priestly institution meant to interrupt the defilement-cycle fails; the institutional deposit of priestly knowledge of clean/unclean is not transmitted.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

T2.8 found no constitutional deposit from sustained possession in the 21-verse corpus. The restoration is consistently named as complete. T5.7 is closed on this basis.

---

##### T5.7.2 — Does the evidence indicate generational consequence — a deposit carried forward beyond the individual?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

No generational constitutional deposit is evidenced in the 133-verse corpus for Characteristic 1. The perpetual statutes (e.g., Num 19:10 — "this shall be a perpetual statute for the people of Israel, and for the stranger who sojourns among them") are institutional provisions, not evidence of a generational biological or constitutional deposit. The defilement-state is incurred by individuals in their own lifetime through their own bodily events.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The 26-verse corpus does not directly evidence a generational biological deposit of the moral-inner defilement-state. Job 14:4 (VCG-01) — "who can bring a clean thing out of an unclean? There is not one" — can be read as pointing to a generational constitutional condition (the human being as constitutionally unclean, from which no clean offspring can emerge), which implies a generational transmission of the constitutional uncleanness. However, the verse does not specifically name a biological mechanism; it names an existential condition. The evidence supports a generational transmission of the constitutional moral uncleanness (Job 14:4) but does not evidence a specific deposit mechanism beyond the constitutional human condition inherited from the fall.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes directly. Eze 20:18/30 (VCG-02) documents the generational transmission of the defilement pattern: the children are warned not to defile as their fathers did ("do not walk in the statutes of your fathers, nor keep their rules, nor defile yourselves with their idols" — 20:18); but the rhetorical challenge of 20:30 ("will you defile yourselves after the manner of your fathers?") reveals that the warning goes unheeded and the generational pattern is repeated. The generational consequence is: each generation inherits the temptation to repeat the defilement pattern of the previous generation, and without prophetic interruption and covenantal formation, the pattern is reproduced.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (S)

No generational consequence is evidenced in the 21-verse corpus. A child is afflicted (Mar 7:25, Luk 9:42) but this is the spirit's own invasion of the child, not a generationally transmitted condition from the parents.

---

##### T5.7.3 — If T2.8 found no deposit, note this explicitly and close T5.7.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (S)

T2.8 found no constitutional deposit. T5.7 is closed: no developmental consequence from sustained deposit is evidenced, and no generational deposit is evidenced.
