## T6 — Inter-Characteristic Relationships (24 prompts)

---

### T6

#### T6.1 — Co-occurrence

##### T6.1.1 — Which adjacent characteristics appear most frequently alongside this one in the verse evidence?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Three characteristics appear most frequently adjacent to Characteristic 1 in the 133-verse corpus's cross-register flags and internal evidence: (1) M12 (Purity) — the universal structural opposite, present in every VCG and sub-group of this characteristic; (2) M11 (Cleansing/Restoration) — the remedial counterpart that every defilement-state generates as its necessary response; the cleansing vocabulary (washing, water of impurity, examination-and-clearance) runs throughout M10c-A-VCG-07 (Num 19 corpus) and is signalled in M10c-B-VCG-03 (Lev 22:4 — "until he is clean") and M10c-A-VCG-08 (2Ch 29:5 — "carry out the filth from the Holy Place... consecrate yourselves"); (3) M07 (Shame) — the stigma and social-exclusion register, especially in M10c-B-VCG-03: the public self-declaration (Lev 13:45 "Unclean, unclean"), the enforced isolation (Lev 13:46), and the corporate expulsion of Lam 4:15 carry M07 cross-register content alongside Characteristic 1's condition.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The INTEGRATION_NOTE carry-forward observation specified five cross-register relationships to map at T6. Re-reading §3 fresh, the co-occurring characteristics evidenced are: (1) M10 (Sin-act producing defilement-state): Rom 1:24 (VCG-02) — impurity follows the sin-acts of rejecting God (Rom 1:21-23 context); Gal 5:19 (VCG-02) — "works of the flesh" lists impurity alongside acts of sin; Col 3:5 (VCG-02) — "put to death... sexual immorality, impurity, passion, evil desire, and covetousness" — impurity in a list of sin-items. (2) M11 (Cleansing/Repentance): 2Cor 7:1 (VCG-03) — the call to cleanse from defilement; 2Cor 6:17 (VCG-03) — separation as the condition for divine welcome; Isa 52:11 (VCG-03) — "purify yourselves." (3) M29 (Desire): Rom 1:24 (VCG-02) — "lusts of their hearts"; Col 3:5 — "passion, evil desire, and covetousness." (4) M08 (Pride/Contempt): 2Pe 2:10 (VCG-03) — "despise authority, bold and willful." (5) M09 (Consecration): Rev 14:4 (VCG-05) — the undefiled state defined by following the Lamb; Isa 52:11 (VCG-03) — "purify yourselves, you who bear the vessels of the Lord."

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Re-reading §3 fresh. Four adjacent characteristics co-occur most frequently. (1) M10 (Sin-act): The sin-acts that produce corporate/covenantal defilement are pervasive throughout the corpus — idolatry (Eze 20/22/23), sexual violation (Num 5/Lev 18/Eze 22), bloodshed (Eze 22:3-4). The defilement-state is consistently produced by identified sin-acts. (2) M10b (Wickedness/Abomination — INTEGRATION_NOTE carry-forward): The Ezekiel idolatry corpus (VCG-02 — Eze 14:11, 20:7/18/30/31/43, 22:3-4, 23:7/13/17/30/38, and VCG-03 — Eze 5:11, 23:38, 43:7/8) carries an M10b cross-register flag — the same acts are simultaneously "abominations" (M10b) and produce "defilement" (M10c Characteristic 3). (3) M12 (Purity — structural opposite): present as the implied structural opposite throughout all five VCGs. (4) M11 (Cleansing/Restoration): the VCG-05 cleansing-promise corpus (Eze 37:23, Zec 13:1) shows M11 as the necessary response to the corporate/covenantal defilement-state.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Re-reading §3 fresh. Two adjacent characteristics are most prominent. (1) M12 (Purity/wholeness — structural opposite): present in every VCG as the implied structural positive. Luk 6:18 (VCG-02): "cured" — wholeness is the positive M12 state restored. Luk 9:42: "healed" — healing as the M12 state. (2) M27 (Cosmic-evil agents — INTEGRATION_NOTE carry-forward): the unclean spirits operating throughout the 21 verses are the cosmic-evil agents M27 analyses; the same events are simultaneously M10c (the defilement-state produced in the person) and M27 (the agent's nature and action). Mar 3:11 (VCG-03): "You are the Son of God" — the spirits' self-aware adversarial identity is M27 content co-present with M10c's defilement-state content. M11 (Cleansing/healing) is also present: Luk 6:18 — cured; Act 5:16 — healed.

---

##### T6.1.2 — What does the pattern of co-occurrence reveal about this characteristic's place in the inner-being landscape?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The co-occurrence pattern reveals Characteristic 1 as positioned at the intersection of three vectors: the purity/holiness vector (M12), the remedial/restorative vector (M11), and the shame/social-exclusion vector (M07). This intersection reveals the characteristic as a condition that: (a) stands in structural opposition to the positive state of purity; (b) generates and requires the activity of cleansing; and (c) carries social-relational consequences in the shame register. The characteristic does not stand alone in the inner-being landscape but is constituted by its relationships to these three adjacent characteristics.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The co-occurrence pattern confirms the carry-forward INTEGRATION_NOTE: the characteristic is surrounded by a relational network of four adjacencies. M10 (sin-act) appears as the generative cause upstream of the defilement-state — the sin-act produces the condition. M11 (cleansing) appears as the necessary response downstream — the condition requires cleansing. M29 (desire) appears as the vehicle — unchecked desire is the mechanism through which the condition operates. M08 (pride) appears as a companion inner posture — defilement and bold contempt co-occur (2Pe 2:10). M09 (consecration) appears as the positive opposite — the undefiled state is the consecrated state. The characteristic sits at the centre of a five-node relational network: generated by sin-through-desire, sustained by pride, calling for cleansing, opposed by consecration.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The co-occurrence pattern confirms the INTEGRATION_NOTE observation: Characteristic 3 is embedded in a four-node relational network. M10 (sin-act) is the upstream causal generator. M10b (abomination) is a co-extensive characterisation of the same acts from a different angle — the acts are simultaneously sinful (M10), abominable (M10b), and defiling (Characteristic 3). M12 (purity) is the structural opposite providing the positive contrast. M11 (cleansing) is the downstream restorative response. Characteristic 3 sits at the junction of these four, distinguished by its focus on the defilement as it extends to the sacred environment (land, sanctuary, name) — the relational-spatial dimension that is distinctive to it.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The co-occurrence pattern confirms the INTEGRATION_NOTE: Characteristic 4 is the M10c characteristic most directly intersecting M27. The same 21 verses simultaneously evidence the defilement-state produced in the person (M10c Characteristic 4) and the character/agency of the spirits as cosmic-evil agents (M27). The co-occurrence with M12 (wholeness) reveals the characteristic's position as defined by its structural opposite. The co-occurrence with M11 (restoration/healing) reveals the characteristic as the condition that most directly calls M11 into operation — every healing of an unclean-spirit affliction is simultaneously an M11 event and a reversal of Characteristic 4.

---

##### T6.1.3 — If no significant co-occurrence patterns emerge, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Significant co-occurrence patterns are evidenced. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Significant co-occurrence patterns are evidenced across all five adjacencies. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Significant co-occurrence patterns are evidenced (M10, M10b, M12, M11). Not applicable.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Significant co-occurrence patterns are evidenced (M27, M12, M11). Not applicable.

---

#### T6.2 — Sequential Relationships

##### T6.2.1 — Does the verse evidence show this characteristic consistently preceding, following, or accompanying another characteristic in a sequence?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes. Characteristic 1 consistently precedes M11 (Cleansing) in the evidence sequence: defilement is acquired first; cleansing is the required response that follows. This sequence is structurally invariant in the corpus — every defilement event is paired with a prescribed cleansing remedy (washing and waiting throughout M10c-A-VCG-02, -05, -06, -07; examination and clearance in M10c-B-VCG-02; water of impurity in M10c-A-VCG-07). The defilement-state precedes cleansing by definition — you cannot cleanse what has not been defiled. The sequence is also evidenced in the reverse: M12 (clean state) precedes Characteristic 1's acquisition event; the person begins clean and is defilement-interrupted.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes. Three sequential relationships are evidenced. (1) M10 (sin-act) → Characteristic 2: Rom 1:24 (VCG-02) — the sin-acts of rejecting God (M10) are followed by God's giving over to impurity (Characteristic 2). Gal 5:19 (VCG-02) — "works of the flesh are evident: sexual immorality, impurity..." — the works (M10 acts) and the defilement-state (Characteristic 2) appear together. (2) Characteristic 2 → M11 (cleansing): 2Cor 7:1 (VCG-03) — the defilement-state is the condition from which cleansing (M11) flows; defilement precedes cleansing as a logical sequence. (3) M29 (desire) → Characteristic 2: Rom 1:24 (VCG-02) — desire (lusts of the heart) leads to the impurity condition; the desire-event precedes and generates the defilement-state.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes. Three sequential relationships: (1) M10 (sin-act) → Characteristic 3: the sin-acts of idolatry, sexual violation, and desecration produce the corporate/covenantal defilement-state. Psa 106:39 (VCG-02) — "thus they became unclean by their acts" — the acts precede and produce the condition. (2) Characteristic 3 → M11 (cleansing): the defilement-state calls forth the cleansing response — Eze 37:23 (VCG-05) — "and will cleanse them"; Zec 13:1 (VCG-05) — fountain opened to cleanse. (3) Characteristic 3 → exile → memory → repentance: the defilement produces the judicial consequences (exile, VCG-05) which produce the memory (Eze 20:43) which produces the self-loathing which begins the return — a multi-stage sequential chain.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes. Two sequential relationships: (1) Characteristic 4 → M11 (restoration/healing): every possession-expulsion account shows the defilement-state preceding the healing restoration. Mar 1:26 — spirit departs → Mar 1:27 — amazement at healing; Luk 9:42 — spirit expelled → "healed the boy, and gave him back to his father"; Act 5:16 — afflicted → "all healed." Characteristic 4 consistently precedes M11's restoration. (2) M27 (spirits as cosmic-evil agents) accompanies Characteristic 4 simultaneously — M27 is the co-extensive analytical lens on the same events.

---

##### T6.2.2 — What does the sequence reveal — is the relationship causal, developmental, or correlational?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The relationship with M11 (Cleansing) is causal: the defilement-state causes the need for cleansing; cleansing is the designed response to the defilement-state. The relationship with M12 (Purity) is both precedent-and-opposed: M12 is the prior positive state from which Characteristic 1 is a departure, and the goal toward which the cleansing aims. The sequence is: M12 (clean) → Characteristic 1 (defilement acquired) → M11 (cleansing required and enacted) → M12 (clean restored). This three-step sequence is the fundamental rhythm of the purity system.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The M10 → Characteristic 2 relationship is causal: sin-acts produce the defilement-state (Rom 1:24 — the sin-act of rejecting God causes the judicial giving-over to impurity). The M29 (desire) → Characteristic 2 relationship is causal: unchecked desire generates the defilement-state (Rom 1:24 — "lusts of their hearts to impurity"). The Characteristic 2 → M11 relationship is also causal: the presence of the defilement-state necessitates cleansing (2Cor 7:1 — the defilement-state is the cause of the call to cleanse). These are causal sequences, not merely correlational.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The M10 → Characteristic 3 relationship is causal: sin-acts produce the defilement-state. The Characteristic 3 → M11 relationship is also causal: the defilement-state necessitates and eventually receives the cleansing. The Characteristic 3 → exile → memory → repentance chain is developmental: the defilement-state does not immediately produce repentance but requires the intermediate stages of exile and memory before the repentance arc begins. The sequence reveals the characteristic as embedded in a longer developmental arc that operates through suffering and memory rather than through immediate correction.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The Characteristic 4 → M11 sequence is causal: the defilement-state produced by external spiritual agency is the condition that M11's healing directly addresses and reverses. M11 is not merely correlated with Characteristic 4; it is the designed response to it — every possession-expulsion account is structured as Characteristic 4 → authority engaged → M11 restoration. The M27 accompaniment is co-extensive and analytical rather than sequential: M27 and Characteristic 4 are simultaneous lenses on the same events, not a before-and-after sequence.

---

##### T6.2.3 — If no sequential pattern is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Sequential patterns are evidenced. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Sequential patterns are evidenced. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Sequential patterns are evidenced. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Sequential patterns are evidenced. Not applicable.

---

#### T6.3 — Causal and Constitutive Relationships

##### T6.3.1 — Does this characteristic produce another characteristic in the verse evidence — and if so, which one, and by what mechanism?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes. Characteristic 1 produces M11 (Cleansing) as its necessary response — not directly as an inner-being characteristic in the person, but as the system of cleansing acts that the defilement-state requires. It also produces M07 (Shame) as a secondary consequence in the stigma register: the public declaration of the disease (Lev 13:45, M10c-B-VCG-03) and the enforced isolation (Lev 13:46) generate the social-shame condition that M07 owns. The defilement-state does not produce M07 directly but creates the conditions (public declaration, exclusion) that activate the shame register.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes. Characteristic 2 produces M11 (Cleansing) as its necessary response. 2Cor 7:1 (VCG-03): the defilement-state is the condition from which the call to cleansing issues; the defilement-state is the cause of M11 being activated. Characteristic 2 also produces bodily dishonour as a consequence (Rom 1:24, VCG-02: "dishonoring of their bodies") — though bodily dishonour is a consequence expressed in action rather than a named inner-being characteristic per se. The escalation pathway — "lawlessness leading to more lawlessness" (Rom 6:19, VCG-02) — suggests that Characteristic 2 produces a deepening of itself and of the connected sin-act pattern (M10).

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes. Characteristic 3 produces: (1) M11 (Cleansing) — the defilement-state requires and eventually receives cleansing; Eze 37:23 (VCG-05) and Zec 13:1 (VCG-05) name the divine cleansing as the response to the corporate/covenantal defilement. (2) M07 (Shame/Stigma — cross-register from Phase 3 flag): Lam 1:17 (VCG-05) — "Jerusalem has become a filthy thing among them"; Lam 4:15 (VCG-05) — "Unclean! Away!" — the characteristic produces corporate shame and social expulsion as its social consequence. (3) The characteristic also escalates itself through judicial release: Eze 20:26 (VCG-02) — God "defiled them through their very gifts" — the defilement-state, when it reaches the extreme of child sacrifice, is deepened as a judicial act.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes. (1) M11 (Cleansing/restoration) as its necessary correlate: Luk 6:18 (VCG-02) — "those troubled with unclean spirits were cured" — the cure is M11's operation. (2) Relational severance as a secondary consequence: Mar 5:2 (VCG-01) — the man dwelling among tombs; the spirit severs the person's communal bonds. (3) Communal response and mobilisation: Act 5:16 (VCG-02) — the characteristic generates the community's corporate seeking of healing on behalf of the afflicted, mobilising communal agency.

---

##### T6.3.2 — Is this characteristic produced by another — and if so, which one?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Characteristic 1 is not produced by another inner-being characteristic — it is produced by bodily events (contact, emission, proximity) and authoritative verdicts (priestly examination). However, within Characteristic 1's sub-register VCG-04 (Lev 11:43-44, M10c-A-VCG-04), the willful non-avoidance of defiling contact would engage M10 (sin-act) cross-register — choosing to touch what one has been commanded not to touch is an act-of-sin that produces the defilement-state. In that sub-register, M10 (sin-act) produces Characteristic 1. More broadly, the cross-register flags from the Phase 3 verdicts identify M10 (sin→defilement) as a consistent companion: in those cases, the sin-act in M10 produces the defilement-state in Characteristic 1.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes. Three upstream producers are evidenced: (1) M10 (sin-act): Rom 1:24 (VCG-02) — the sin-act of rejecting God is followed by God's giving over to impurity; the sin-act produces the defilement-state. (2) M29 (desire): Rom 1:24 (VCG-02) — "lusts of their hearts" as the generating desire; Col 3:5 (VCG-02) — "passion, evil desire" preceding impurity in the listed complex. (3) Job 14:4 constitutional origin (VCG-01) — the inherited human condition of uncleanness; the characteristic is also "produced" by the constituted human condition prior to individual acts.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes. Two upstream producers are evidenced: (1) M10 (sin-act): the corporate sin-acts of idolatry, sexual violation, and desecration produce the defilement-state (Psa 106:39 — "they became unclean by their acts"). (2) The corporate habit-pattern operating across generations: Eze 20:18/30 — "defile yourselves after the manner of your fathers" — suggests the generational transmission of the defiling pattern is also a producing force; the generational defilement-habit is itself a prior condition that produces each generation's specific acts of defilement.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Characteristic 4 is produced by M27 (the unclean spirits as cosmic-evil agents) — the spirit's own agency is the producing cause of the defilement-state. M27 analyses the producing agents; Characteristic 4 analyses the defilement-state they produce. The INTEGRATION_NOTE confirms this relationship: defilement here is the result the external evil agent produces; in M27 the same verses analyse the agent's nature. No other characteristic in the M10c cluster produces Characteristic 4.

---

##### T6.3.3 — Is this characteristic a constituent element of another, or does another characteristic constitute part of this one?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The 133-verse corpus does not show Characteristic 1 as a constituent of another characteristic. Within the M10c cluster, the four characteristics are separate analytical registers (ritual, moral-inner, corporate-covenantal, external-spiritual) of the broader defilement domain. Characteristic 1 is constituted in part by the clean/unclean categorical system (M12's positive domain defines the negative space that Characteristic 1 inhabits), but M12 is not a constituent element of Characteristic 1 — it is its structural opposite.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The characteristic is constituted in part by desire (M29): the defilement-state is the condition that unchecked desire produces and inhabits. Desire is a constituent vehicle of the characteristic. The characteristic is also constituted by conscience-defilement (1Cor 8:7, VCG-03): the conscience's defiled state is both a part of the characteristic and the characteristic's primary inner faculty engagement. However, neither desire nor conscience-defilement is fully identical with Characteristic 2 — they are contributing constituent elements that together with the will's bondage and the heart's allegiance disorder constitute the full characteristic.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The M10b (abomination) register constitutes a partial overlap with Characteristic 3's Ezekiel idolatry corpus (VCG-02 — the INTEGRATION_NOTE carry-forward). The same acts are simultaneously abominations (M10b) and defilements (Characteristic 3). The two characteristics are not one; they characterise the same acts from different analytical lenses: M10b owns the moral-character assessment (abominable); Characteristic 3 owns the defilement-condition produced by those acts. Neither is a constituent of the other — they co-characterise the same evidence from different angles.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

M27 (cosmic-evil agents) constitutes the agency-dimension of Characteristic 4: without the M27 agents there is no Characteristic 4 defilement-state. However, the two are not identical: M27 is broader (cosmic-evil agency in all its forms) while Characteristic 4 is narrower (the specific defilement-condition produced in human persons by those agents). Characteristic 4 is a sub-domain of the consequences of M27's operation.

---

##### T6.3.4 — If no causal or constitutive relationship is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Causal relationships are evidenced (Characteristic 1 → M11; M10 → Characteristic 1 in sin-act sub-register). Not applicable.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Causal and constitutive relationships are evidenced. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Causal and co-characterising relationships are evidenced. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Causal and constitutive relationships are evidenced. Not applicable.

---

#### T6.4 — Vocabulary and Root Sharing

##### T6.4.1 — Does this characteristic share vocabulary terms with other characteristics in the programme?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes. The ta.me vocabulary (H2930A verb, H2931 adjective) is shared across all four M10c characteristics at the lexical level — the same Hebrew root for "defile/unclean" operates in the ritual register (Characteristic 1), the moral-inner register (Characteristic 2), the corporate-covenantal register (Characteristic 3), and can appear in the spiritual-agency context (Characteristic 4, though G0169 akathartos is the primary NT term there). The nid.dah (H5079) term appears in both Characteristic 1 (M10c-A-VCG-05 and -07) and Characteristic 3 (M10c-D sub-group — Eze 36:17, Lev 18:19) — the same term spans the bodily-ritual and the moral-corporate registers.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes. The ta.me root (H2931) is shared with Characteristic 1 (Ritual defilement-state), Characteristic 3 (Corporate-covenantal defilement), and Characteristic 4 (External spiritual agency defilement) — all four M10c characteristics share the same Hebrew root. G0169 akathartos is shared between Characteristic 2 (moral-inner uses: 2Cor 6:17, Eph 5:5, Rev 16:13/17:4/18:2, VCG-03/04) and Characteristic 1 (ritual/categorical uses: Act 10:14/28, M10c-B-VCG-05) and Characteristic 4 (unclean spirits, M10c-E). The vocabulary sharing across all four characteristics using the same Greek and Hebrew root confirms a shared lexical domain.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes. The ta.me root (H2930A verb, H2931 adj) is shared across all four M10c characteristics. H5079 nid.dah is shared with Characteristic 1 (ritual-bodily register of nid.dah) and appears in Characteristic 3's corporate-prophetic uses (Eze 36:17 — "like the uncleanness of a woman in her menstrual impurity"; Lam 1:17 — "a filthy thing"). The vocabulary of "abomination" (tô‛ēbāh — referenced at Jer 7:30, 2Ch 36:14, Eze 22:11 as paired with defilement in VCG-02 and -03) is shared with M10b.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes. G0169 akathartos ("unclean") is shared across all four M10c characteristics. In Characteristic 1, akathartos names the person's ritual status (Act 10:14/28). In Characteristic 2, akathartos names the morally defiled inner condition (2Cor 6:17). In Characteristic 4, akathartos names the character of the external spiritual agent ("unclean spirit" — pneuma akatharton). The same Greek adjective operates across three different registers within the M10c cluster.

---

##### T6.4.2 — Does vocabulary sharing extend to root-level architecture — a shared root that generates terms across two or more characteristics?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Yes. The ta.me root (H2930) generates both H2930A (verb: to defile/be unclean) and H2931 (adjective: unclean), which appear across all four M10c characteristics. The root is the unifying lexical architecture for the defilement domain; the four characteristics represent different registers of the same root's deployment. This shared root architecture means the characteristics are not merely analogically related but lexically unified under one semantic field.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Yes. The ta.me root (H2930/H2931) generates the primary vocabulary across all four M10c characteristics. G0167 akatharsia (Characteristic 2 primary term) and G0169 akathartos (shared across Characteristics 1, 2, 4) both derive from the alpha-privative + katharos root. G3435 molunō and G3436 molusmos (Characteristic 2) share the molunō root. The root-level architecture shows the four characteristics as lexically unified under two root systems (ta.me Hebrew; katharos/akathartos Greek) with additional terms (molunō, miasmos) adding register specificity.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Yes. The ta.me root (H2930) generates H2930A (verb) and H2931 (adj) across all four M10c characteristics. The H5079 nid.dah appears in both Characteristic 1 (bodily-physiological uses) and Characteristic 3 (corporate-prophetic metaphorical uses — Eze 36:17 and Lam 1:17), showing the same term operating across two different characteristic registers. The shared root architecture confirms the four characteristics as differentiated registers of one unified defilement domain.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Yes. G0169 akathartos (alpha-privative + katharos — "not clean") is the root shared across M10c characteristics. For Characteristic 4, akathartos is exclusively the adjectival modifier of pneuma, while in Characteristics 1 and 2 it also operates as a standalone adjective for persons and objects. The root architecture is shared; the grammatical deployment differs.

---

##### T6.4.3 — What does vocabulary sharing reveal about the conceptual relationship between characteristics?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The shared ta.me root vocabulary reveals that the four M10c characteristics are not separate, unrelated conditions — they are differentiated registers of one broadly unified inner-being domain: defilement and impurity. Characteristic 1 (ritual), Characteristic 2 (moral-inner), Characteristic 3 (corporate-covenantal), and Characteristic 4 (external spiritual agency) share the same lexical architecture because they are addressing the same fundamental category — the condition of being unclean in its various registers — from different angles. The shared vocabulary is evidence of conceptual unity beneath register differentiation.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The shared root vocabulary reveals the four M10c characteristics as differentiated registers of one broad defilement domain. The same roots (ta.me, akathartos) deploy differently in different contexts: in the Levitical bodily-mechanism context = Characteristic 1; in the NT moral-inner context = Characteristic 2; in the corporate-covenantal prophetic context = Characteristic 3; in the spiritual-agency context = Characteristics 1 or 4. The shared vocabulary signals that the programme's four characteristics are not four separate conditions but four registers of one domain — the condition of defilement/impurity as it operates across different dimensions of creaturely existence.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The shared ta.me root reveals the four M10c characteristics as differentiated registers of one lexical domain: all four use the same root to name what is fundamentally the same condition (defilement/uncleanness) as it operates in different dimensions (ritual/bodily, moral-inner, corporate/covenantal, external-spiritual-agency). The shared vocabulary confirms conceptual unity beneath register differentiation. The nid.dah sharing between Characteristics 1 and 3 is particularly revealing: the same bodily-impurity paradigm (menstruation) serves both as the archetype of the ritual defilement state (Characteristic 1) and as the metaphor for the corporate moral uncleanness that God finds repugnant (Eze 36:17, Characteristic 3). The metaphorical extension of the bodily paradigm into the corporate moral domain is the vocabulary arc that most directly shows the connection between the two registers.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The shared akathartos root reveals all four M10c characteristics as differentiated registers of one unified defilement domain. The same root concept (not-clean, defilement) applies to: bodily-ritual status (Characteristic 1), inner moral condition (Characteristic 2), corporate-covenantal defilement of sacred space (Characteristic 3), and the character of external spiritual agents (Characteristic 4). The shared vocabulary confirms that the programme's four characteristics are registers of one domain — defilement/impurity as it operates in different dimensions of creaturely existence.

---

##### T6.4.4 — If no significant vocabulary sharing is evidenced, note this explicitly.

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Significant vocabulary sharing is evidenced. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Significant vocabulary sharing is evidenced. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Significant vocabulary sharing is evidenced. Not applicable.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Significant vocabulary sharing is evidenced. Not applicable.

---

#### T6.5 — Distinctions

##### T6.5.1 — Which adjacent characteristic most closely resembles this one — and what precisely distinguishes them?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Characteristic 2 (Moral-inner defilement-state, M10c-C sub-group) most closely resembles Characteristic 1. Both are defilement-state conditions bearing on the person's inner integrity and sacred standing. The precise distinction: Characteristic 1's condition is acquired through bodily mechanism (contact, emission, disease-verdict) — the defilement is external in origin, entering through the body. Characteristic 2's condition originates in the inner person itself — the conscience, will, and heart are corrupted by desire, habitual sin, and idolatrous attachment (Rom 6:19: "prior master directing bodily members"; 2Cor 7:1: "defilement of body and spirit"). Characteristic 1 is managed through prescribed ritual remedies (washing, waiting, examination, water of impurity); Characteristic 2 requires the moral and volitional transformation of the inner person.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

Characteristic 1 (Ritual defilement-state) most closely resembles Characteristic 2 (Moral-inner defilement-state). Both are defilement-states bearing on the person's sacral standing and inner integrity. The precise distinction: Characteristic 1's condition is acquired through bodily contact with a defiling agent (external, mechanical origin) or authoritative verdict; Characteristic 2's condition originates within the inner person itself — through desire, sin, and habitual moral failure (internal, volitional origin). Characteristic 1 is managed through prescribed ritual remedies (washing, waiting, examination); Characteristic 2 requires the transformation of the inner person's orientation — repentance, cleansing of body and spirit (2Cor 7:1), re-presentation of the will toward righteousness (Rom 6:19).

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Characteristic 2 (Moral-inner defilement-state) most closely resembles Characteristic 3. Both involve moral defilement arising from volitional defection and idolatrous attachment. The precise distinction: Characteristic 2's locus is the individual inner person — conscience, will, and heart corrupted from within. Characteristic 3's locus is the corporate-covenantal domain — the defilement extends from the community's inner will outward to land, sanctuary, and divine name. The distinguishing feature is extension: Characteristic 3 requires the outward extension to sacred environmental objects (land, sanctuary, name) to be operative; Characteristic 2 operates entirely within the individual inner person without requiring external sacred-space extension.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Characteristic 1 (Ritual defilement-state) most closely resembles Characteristic 4 in that both produce a defilement-state not primarily the result of the person's own moral defection — the defilement arrives through an external mechanism. The precise distinction: Characteristic 1's mechanism is bodily contact with a material defiling agent or authoritative verdict — a physical-ritual mechanism governed by the Levitical system. Characteristic 4's mechanism is inhabitation by an external spiritual being — a personal, purposeful, adversarial agent who invades and dominates at the spirit level.

---

##### T6.5.2 — Where the evidence shows apparent overlap, what is the precise boundary?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The precise boundary is the origin of the defilement. Characteristic 1: origin is external bodily contact or authoritative verdict — the body encounters a defiling agent or is assessed by a priest. Characteristic 2: origin is the inner person's own volitional and dispositional state — the heart's allegiance disorder, the will's habitual submission to unchecked desire. The VCG-04 sub-register within Characteristic 1 (Lev 11:43-44, M10c-A-VCG-04 — volitional self-defilement) sits at the boundary: the defiling contact is a bodily act, but the willful choice to make it is foregrounded. This sub-register is the closest point of Characteristic 1 to Characteristic 2, but it remains in Characteristic 1 because the mechanism is still bodily contact (the swarming creature), even though the will is explicitly named.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The boundary is the origin and locus of the defilement. Both characteristics use the same Hebrew vocabulary (H2931 ta.me adj) for their primary terms, creating apparent overlap. The boundary: the H2931 verses in Characteristic 2 (VCG-01: Job 14:4, Isa 6:5, Isa 64:6, Hag 2:14; VCG-03: Isa 52:11; VCG-05: Isa 35:8) operate in the Hebrew metaphorical-inner register — they name constitutional moral uncleanness before God, not a ritually defined bodily condition. The H2931 verses in Characteristic 1 (Lev 11-15, Num 5, 9, 19, etc.) name the ritual-status condition from bodily contact or verdict. The boundary is determined by the locus: when H2931 names a constitutional/moral/inner condition = Characteristic 2; when it names a ritual-status condition from bodily mechanism = Characteristic 1.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The boundary is the direction and object of the defilement. When the same ta.me vocabulary names the inner condition of the individual person's conscience, will, and heart = Characteristic 2. When the same vocabulary names the defilement of land, sanctuary, name, or the covenantal relational order as extensions of the community's inner defection = Characteristic 3. Some verses span both: Eze 36:17 (VCG-04) — "they defiled it [the land] by their ways and their deeds" — the "it" (the land) is Characteristic 3's object; the "their ways and their deeds" are the inner disposition of Characteristic 2 producing the extension into Characteristic 3's domain. Characteristic 3 presupposes Characteristic 2 as its generating inner condition.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The apparent overlap is in the shared feature of external causation without volitional cooperation. The precise boundary: Characteristic 1's external cause is impersonal (a material object, a biological state, a verdict) and produces a ritual-status condition managed by prescribed Levitical remedies. Characteristic 4's external cause is personal, purposeful, and adversarial (a spiritual being with its own will and agency) producing a condition of personal domination requiring divine command for resolution. The boundary is determined by the nature of the external cause: impersonal/material vs personal/spiritual-adversarial.

---

##### T6.5.3 — Is the distinction between this characteristic and its nearest neighbour one of degree, kind, direction, or constitutional level?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

The distinction is primarily of kind and constitutional level. The kind distinction: ritual defilement (Characteristic 1) is a legal/sacral condition arising from bodily mechanism; moral-inner defilement (Characteristic 2) is a condition of the inner person arising from within. The constitutional level distinction: Characteristic 1 is primarily a condition of the embodied person at the level of bodily function and sacral status; Characteristic 2 penetrates to the spirit level (2Cor 7:1: "defilement of body and spirit"). The distinction is not merely of degree (more or less severe defilement) but of a different kind of condition at a deeper constitutional level.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

The distinction is primarily of kind and constitutional level. Kind: Characteristic 1 is a legally-defined bodily-mechanism condition; Characteristic 2 is a morally-defined inner-volitional condition. Constitutional level: Characteristic 1 operates at the bodily-mechanism and social-sacral level; Characteristic 2 penetrates to the spirit level (2Cor 7:1 — "defilement of body and spirit") and operates primarily at the soul level of conscience, will, heart, and desire. Characteristic 2 is constitutionally deeper than Characteristic 1.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

The distinction is primarily of direction and scope. Kind: both are defilement-state conditions. Constitutional level: Characteristic 2 penetrates to the spirit level (2Cor 7:1); Characteristic 3 operates at the soul level (will, desire, heart allegiance) and extends outward to the corporate-covenantal domain (land, sanctuary, name) — not inward toward the spirit level. Direction: Characteristic 2 moves inward (from desire to the deepest constitutional level); Characteristic 3 moves outward (from the community's inner will to the sacred spatial and relational environment). Scope: Characteristic 2 is individual; Characteristic 3 is corporate.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The distinction is primarily of kind and constitutional level. Kind: the defiling agent is categorically different — material/impersonal (Characteristic 1) vs spiritual/personal/adversarial (Characteristic 4). Constitutional level: Characteristic 1 operates at the bodily-mechanism and social-sacral level; Characteristic 4 operates at the spirit level (the deepest constitutional level), which is why the domination is more comprehensive and the resolution requires divine command rather than ritual remedy.

---

#### T6.6 — Shared Verse Anchors

##### T6.6.1 — Does any verse in this characteristic's evidence base also function as a primary anchor in another characteristic's study?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Possible shared anchor material within the M10c domain: Lev 11:44 (M10c-A-VCG-04, vc_id 21418) anchors the volitional self-defilement VCG in Characteristic 1 and also functions as a key expression of the holiness/defilement boundary that M12 (Purity) owns as its structural positive — the verse serves both as Characteristic 1's evidence (the will's refusal of defilement) and as M12's framing (divine holiness as the positive standard). Act 10:28 (M10c-B-VCG-05, vc_id 21281) is the anchor for the NT categorical conscience VCG in Characteristic 1; it also functions as a pivotal verse for covenantal-status questions within the broader programme. Within the M10c cluster, the Num 9:7 (vc_id 21546) verse anchors the grief-at-exclusion finding in VCG-07 of Characteristic 1.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

2Cor 7:1 (vc_id 9329, G3436 molusmos, VCG-03) functions as the primary anchor for Characteristic 2's body-and-spirit purification call (VCG-03). This verse is also cited in the broader programme's purity/holiness discussion as a locus classicus of M12 (purity completing holiness). Isa 6:5 (vc_id 21547, H2931, VCG-01) — the prophet's conscience-recognition of moral-inner defilement under divine holiness — could function as an anchor for the broader guilt/awareness characteristic studies. Rev 14:4 (vc_id 9328, G3435 molunō, VCG-05) — the undefiled following the Lamb as firstfruits — is relevant as an anchor for M09 (consecration) and M12 (purity) studies given its explicit consecration language.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Eze 20:43 (vc_id 21420, H2930A, VCG-02) is the primary anchor for Characteristic 3's memory-of-defilement-as-repentance mechanism — this verse functions within both Characteristic 3 and potentially within clusters addressing corporate repentance (M11) and corporate memory. Num 5:27 (vc_id 21472, H2930A, VCG-01) anchors the ordeal-of-jealousy in Characteristic 3's covenantal-relational register; this verse is also relevant to the M07 (shame) register and to the justice/ordeal register in other programme studies. Zec 13:1 (vc_id 21706, H5079, VCG-05) functions as anchor for Characteristic 3's cleansing-promise register and would also function as an M11 (Cleansing) anchor given its explicit cleansing-fountain language.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

Mar 3:11 (vc_id 21286, G0169, VCG-03) — "whenever the unclean spirits saw him, they fell down before him and cried out, 'You are the Son of God'" — functions as a primary anchor for Characteristic 4's authority-recognition register and would also function as a primary anchor in M27 (cosmic-evil agents) for the spirits' self-aware recognition of divine superiority. Mat 10:1 (vc_id 21282, G0169, VCG-03) — the commissioning of authority over unclean spirits — functions as an anchor for both Characteristic 4's authority-commissioning register and M27.

---

##### T6.6.2 — What does the shared anchor reveal about the relationship between the two characteristics?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (E)

Lev 11:44's shared role (Characteristic 1 and M12) reveals that the defilement-state and purity are constitutively defined by each other — the verse that most clearly defines what it means not to defile (Characteristic 1's VCG-04 anchor) is simultaneously the verse that most clearly defines what holiness means (M12's positive statement). The two characteristics are not merely structurally opposite — they are co-defined by the same verse. Act 10:28's shared role reveals that the categorical revision of clean/unclean (Characteristic 1) is simultaneously a revelation about covenantal inclusion (which belongs to broader programme clusters).

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (E)

2Cor 7:1's shared role across Characteristic 2 (defilement of body and spirit) and M12 (bringing holiness to completion) reveals that the defilement-state and purity are co-defined by this verse — it simultaneously describes the problem (defilement of body and spirit) and the goal (holiness brought to completion). The verse is a boundary-point between the two characteristics: it belongs to Characteristic 2 because of the defilement named, and to M12 because of the holiness called for. Rev 14:4's shared role across Characteristic 2 (not defiled) and M09 (consecration — following the Lamb) reveals the positive-inverse of the defilement-state as a consecration state, confirming M09 as the positive structural companion of Characteristic 2's resolution.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (E)

Eze 20:43's shared role (Characteristic 3 and M11 repentance/corporate memory) reveals that the memory of corporate defilement and the beginning of repentance are co-constituted in this verse — the characteristic and its remedy are inseparable at the point of initiation. Zec 13:1's shared role (Characteristic 3 and M11) reveals that the comprehensive cleansing of corporate defilement and the M11 cleansing cluster are addressed by the same eschatological provision. The shared anchors confirm that Characteristic 3 is structurally embedded in a larger soteriological arc (defilement → memory → repentance → cleansing) that spans multiple clusters.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (E)

The shared anchors (Mar 3:11, Mat 10:1) reveal the deep integration between Characteristic 4 and M27: the verses most fully expressing the authority structure governing Characteristic 4's resolution also most fully characterise the nature of the M27 agents. The two clusters are analytically inseparable at the anchor-verse level — the same events simultaneously evidence both the defilement-condition (Characteristic 4) and the agent's nature (M27). This confirms the INTEGRATION_NOTE: the two lenses are complementary, not duplicative.

Full dimensional-sharing data across programme characteristics is not available within the current session scope — the broader programme's completed cluster analyses are not all accessible here. The dimensions identifiable within this characteristic (condition, volitional-perimeter, social-relational, discernment-formative) are likely shared with M12 (Purity — shared condition/discernment dimensions as structural mirror), M11 (Cleansing — shared condition/remedial dimensions as sequential counterpart), and M07 (Shame — shared social-relational/exclusion dimensions). A complete cross-programme dimensional sharing count requires access to the full programme's completed characteristic analyses.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (G)

Full cross-programme dimensional sharing data is not available within this session's scope. Within this characteristic's 26-verse corpus, the dimensions identified (condition, dispositional, volitional, constitutional, spirit-level, heart-level, desire-vehicle) are likely shared with: M12 (purity — structural mirror, sharing condition/constitutional dimensions); M11 (cleansing — sharing condition/remedial dimensions as sequential counterpart); M29 (desire — sharing desire-vehicle dimension as constituent element); M10 (sin-act — sharing volitional/condition dimensions as causal predecessor); M09 (consecration — sharing constitutional/spirit-level dimensions as positive inverse).

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (G)

Full cross-programme dimensional sharing data is not available within this session's scope. Within this characteristic's 83-verse corpus, the dimensions identified (condition, volitional-generative, corporate-covenantal, memory-repentance, spatial-extension to sacred environment) include some shared with other characteristics and some distinctive. The memory-repentance dimension (Eze 20:43) is the most distinctive; it is not evidenced in Characteristics 1 or 2. The volitional-generative dimension is shared with Characteristics 2 and partially 1. The spatial-extension dimension (to land, sanctuary, name) is distinctive to Characteristic 3.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (G)

Full cross-programme dimensional sharing data is not available within this session's scope. Within this characteristic's 21-verse corpus, the dimensions identified (condition, external-spiritual-agency, will-domination, faculty-suppression, communal-severance, spirit-level operation) include some shared and some distinctive. The spirit-level-externally-sourced dimension is shared with M27. The will-domination dimension is partially shared with Characteristic 2 (where the will is bound internally) and M27. The communal-severance dimension is partially shared with Characteristic 3. The condition dimension is shared with all M10c characteristics.

##### T6.7.2 — What does the pattern of dimensional sharing reveal about the relationship between this characteristic and those it shares dimensions with?

**[CHAR-1] Ritual defilement-state** (G)

Based on the available evidence within this characteristic's corpus: the dimensional sharing with M12 (Purity) reveals the two characteristics as constitutively mirror-defined (each requires the other for definition); with M11 (Cleansing) as sequentially paired (defilement generates cleansing as its necessary response); with M07 (Shame) as contextually overlapping in the stigma/exclusion sub-register but distinct in primary mechanism. The pattern suggests a cluster of characteristics centred on the sacral condition of the person in relation to divine holiness, each occupying a distinct position in the purity economy.

**[CHAR-2] Moral-inner defilement-state** (G)

Based on available evidence: dimensional sharing with M12 reveals them as constitutively mirror-defined; with M11 as sequentially paired; with M29 as Characteristic 2 being a downstream consequence of M29's operation; with M10 as M10 being the upstream causal act whose consequence is Characteristic 2; with M09 as Characteristic 2's resolution pointing toward M09's consecrated state. The pattern suggests Characteristic 2 is at the intersection of a network of characteristics: downstream from sin-act and desire, requiring cleansing, opposed by consecration, mirroring purity.

**[CHAR-3] Corporate/covenantal defilement** (G)

Based on available evidence: dimensional sharing with Characteristics 1 and 2 (volitional-generative, condition dimensions) reveals all three M10c defilement characteristics as sharing the same basic condition/volitional structure. Characteristic 3's distinctive dimensions (corporate, spatial-extension, memory-repentance) show its unique analytical contribution: it is the only M10c characteristic whose domain is the sacred spatial-relational environment (land, sanctuary, name) and the only one that names memory as the instrument of repentance.

**[CHAR-4] Defilement by external spiritual agency** (G)

Based on available evidence: dimensional sharing with M27 reveals Characteristic 4 as the M10c characteristic most directly embedded in the M27 cosmic-adversarial domain. Dimensional sharing with Characteristic 2 (will-domination, through different mechanisms) reveals that both characteristics strike at the same faculty (will) through different mechanisms (external override vs internal bondage). The distinctive dimension — externally-sourced spirit-level invasion — is Characteristic 4's unique contribution to the inner-being landscape.
